Raising Hands with Takbirs in Eid Prayer
Ruling with proof: raising hands in Eid takbirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands during Eid takbirs and explain the evidentiary basis of the munqati' hadith.

Core Idea
Raising hands with each Eid takbir is sunnah muakkadah, confirmed by the practice of 'Umar.

This lesson examines a specific sunnah of the Eid prayer: raising the hands with each takbir. While the supporting narration is technically munqati' (disconnected), the Hanafi school accepts it for recommended acts. This illustrates the school's nuanced approach to hadith classification and its application to fada'il al-a'mal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
What is being ruled upon? Raising hands with each takbir in Eid prayer. Its hukm is sunnah muakkadah.
Sunnah muakkadah is a confirmed recommendation, not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, as narrated in a hadith.
The hadith is recorded in Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq.
3
Classify the hadith
The narration is munqati' (disconnected chain). Understand its status in Hanafi usul: accepted for non-obligatory matters.
Munqati' means a link is missing in the chain, but it is still used for fada'il.
4
Apply the school's principle
In Hanafi fiqh, a weak (da'if) or munqati' hadith can be used for fada'il and recommended acts, not for obligations.
This principle is known as al-takhfif fi al-fada'il.
5
Derive the practical ruling
Therefore, raising hands with each takbir is recommended (sunnah) but not obligatory.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is to raise hands.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۳۷۳ (۹) ويرفع يديه في تكبيرات العيدين.
ان عمر بن الخطاب كان يرفع يديه مع كل تكبيرة في الجنازة والعيدين وهذا منقطع (ج) (سن للبیھقی ، باب رفع الیدین فی تکبیر العيدج ثالث ص ۴۱۲ نمبر ۲۱۸۹ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب التکبیر بالیدین ج ثالث ص ۲۹۷ نمبر ۵۶۹ ) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ تکبیر زوائد کہتے وقت ہاتھ بھی کانوں تک اٹھائے گا۔
حاشیہ : (ج) حضرت عمر ابن خطاب ہاتھ اٹھایا کرتے تھے ہر تکبیر کے ساتھ جنازہ میں اور عیدین میں ، یہ حدیث منقطع ہے۔
[374] (9) And he raises his hands in the takbirs of the two Eids. Umar ibn al-Khattab used to raise his hands with every takbir in the funeral prayer and the two Eids, and this is munqati' (disconnected). From this it became known that when saying the extra takbirs, he should also raise his hands to the ears. Footnote (c): Umar ibn al-Khattab used to raise his hands with every takbir in the funeral and the two Eids; this hadith is munqati'.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on raising the hands during the extra takbirs of Eid prayer. The evidence is the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him), who raised his hands with every takbir in both the funeral and Eid prayers. Although the narration is munqati' (disconnected in chain), it is sufficient for establishing a recommended act. In the Hanafi school, it is sunnah to raise the hands to the ears with each takbir in Eid prayer.

Key Terms
منقطع (munqati‘): A hadith with a disconnected chain; its acceptance for legal rulings is debated, but here it is used as evidence for a recommended act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What action is recommended in the Hanafi school when saying the extra takbirs in Eid prayer?
A) Lowering the hands
B) Raising the hands to the ears
C) Placing the right hand over the left
D) Pointing the index finger

Key Takeaway
Raising hands with each takbir in Eid prayer is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) based on the practice of 'Umar, even though the narration is munqati'.

The Extra Takbirs in Eid Prayer: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on the extra Takbirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number and timing of extra Takbirs in Eid prayer and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Eid prayer has extra Takbirs: Hanafi says 3+3; Shafi'i says 7+5; both are sunnah, not wajib.

Eid prayers include additional Takbirs beyond the regular prayer. But how many, and when? The Hanafi school has a clear ruling based on the practice of the Companions, while Imam al-Shafi'i follows a different hadith. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps you appreciate the method of juristic preference (tarjih) in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the number of extra Takbirs in each rak'ah and their timing: first rak'ah: 3 extra after Takbir al-Ihram (total 4 before recitation including the opening). Second rak'ah: 3 extra after recitation, then a fourth for bowing.
The total Takbirs per rak'ah are four when counting the opening or bowing Takbir.
2
Identify the opponent (Shafi'i) and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds: first rak'ah: 7 Takbirs (including opening? Actually 6 extra + 1 for bowing), second: 5 (4 extra + 1 for bowing), all before recitation.
The numbers sometimes count the opening Takbir as part of the total, so Hanafi total is 4+4, Shafi'i is 7+5.
3
Follow the Shafi'i proof
The hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr: 'The Takbir in al-Fitr is seven in the first and five in the last, and recitation is after both.'
This is a Prophetic hadith, though its transmission is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the Athar from Ibn Mas'ud (a Sahaba) is more reliable and consistent with the practice of the early community. They also note that the difference is over istihbab (recommendation), not obligation.
The Hanafi preference (tarjih) is based on the strength of the Companion's practice and the principle that the hadith may have been superseded or not widely practiced.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a Hanafi follower says 4+4 takbirs (including the opening and bowing) with the extra ones at specific times; a Shafi'i follower says 7+5 all before recitation. Both are valid within their schools.
The dispute is one of istihbab (recommendation), so following either view is acceptable, though the Hanafi mufta bihi is 4+4.

And then after it, he recites Surah al-Fatihah and a Surah with it, then he says Takbir and bows with it. (1373 (8)) Then he begins the second rak'ah with recitation. When he finishes the recitation, he says three Takbirs and says a fourth Takbir and bows with it. [1373 (9)] And he raises his hands in the Takbirs of the two Eids. From the hadiths it is known that in Eid prayer, in the first rak'ah after Takbir al-Ihram, three Takbirs are said. So with Takbir al-Ihram there are four Takbirs. Similarly, in the second rak'ah after recitation, three extra Takbirs are said, so with the Takbir of bowing there are four Takbirs. And in the second rak'ah after recitation, four Takbirs are said; its proof is this Athar: 'They referred their matter to Ibn Mas'ud, and he said: Say four Takbirs before recitation, then recite, when you finish say Takbir and bow, then stand for the second rak'ah and recite, when you finish say four Takbirs.' (a) (Sunan al-Siti, chapter: ...) In this Athar it is present that in the second rak'ah after recitation, four Takbirs are said: three extra Takbirs and one Takbir for bowing. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, in the first rak'ah seven Takbirs are said and in the second rak'ah five, and in both the Takbirs are before recitation. His proof is the hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As who said: The Prophet said: The Takbir in al-Fitr is seven in the first and five in the last, and the recitation is after both of them. (b) From these hadiths it is established that in the first rak'ah seven and in the second five Takbirs are said, and they are said before recitation. This difference is about istihbab. (373 (8)) Then he begins the second rak'ah with recitation, so when he finishes the recitation, he says three Takbirs and a fourth Takbir and goes into bowing with it. The detailed explanation and proof have passed. (374 (9)) He will raise both hands in the Takbirs of the two Eids. 'Umar ibn al-Khattab used to raise his hands with every Takbir in Janazah and the two Eids, and this is maqtu'. (c) From this it is known that when saying the extra Takbirs, he will raise his hands to the ears. Footnote: (a) The narrator traced to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. Ibn Mas'ud said: Four Takbirs are said before recitation, then recitation is done, when you finish recitation, say Takbir and bow. Then stand in the second rak'ah and recite, when you finish recitation, say four Takbirs. (b) He said: The Takbir of Eid al-Fitr is seven in the first and five in the second, and the recitation is after both. (c) Umar ibn al-Khattab used to raise his hands with every Takbir in Janazah and the two Eids; this hadith is munqati'.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the number and timing of extra Takbirs in Eid prayer. The author first presents the Hanafi ruling: in the first rak'ah, three extra Takbirs follow Takbir al-Ihram (so four total before recitation including the opening takbir). In the second rak'ah, after recitation, three extra Takbirs are said, then a fourth Takbir for bowing. The Hanafi proof is the Athar from Ibn Mas'ud, where he instructs four Takbirs before recitation in each rak'ah (the first being Takbir al-Ihram, the last being the bowing takbir in the first rak'ah, but in the second rak'ah the fourth is the bowing takbir). This is a Sahih Athar according to the Hanafi school. The Shafi'i view is also presented: seven Takbirs in the first rak'ah (including Takbir al-Ihram? Actually they count six extra plus one for bowing, or seven including Takbir al-Ihram), and five in the second (four extra plus bowing), all before recitation. Their proof is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr directly from the Prophet. The author notes that this difference is only over istihbab (recommendation), not obligation. Then the passage separately rules that hands should be raised during these extra Takbirs, citing Umar's practice as a weak (munqati') narration but used as supporting evidence. The commentary emphasizes the Hanafi position as the operative ruling.

Key Terms
تکبیرات زوائد (takbirat zawā'id): The extra Takbirs said in Eid prayer beyond the obligatory Takbirs of bowing and prostration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many extra Takbirs are said in the second rak'ah of Eid prayer?
A) Three extra before recitation
B) Three extra after recitation, followed by a fourth for bowing
C) Four extra after recitation
D) Five extra before recitation

Key Takeaway
Hanafi Eid prayer includes three extra Takbirs in each rak'ah: after Takbir al-Ihram in the first and after recitation in the second.

Raising Hands During Eid Takbirs
Ruling statement on raising hands in Eid takbirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands during the extra Takbirs of Eid prayer and identify its evidentiary basis.

Core Idea
Raising hands with each extra Takbir in Eid prayer is a confirmed sunnah, supported by the practice of Umar.

While the number of Takbirs is a disputed issue, the act of raising the hands is a clear sunnah in the Hanafi school. This brief lesson examines the evidence and the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is raising hands to the ears with each extra Takbir in Eid prayer. The ruling: it is sunnah (recommended), not wajib.
This applies to both Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who used to raise his hands with every Takbir in Janazah and the two Eids. This is reported as a munqati' narration (incomplete chain) but used as supporting evidence.
The narration is considered weak by hadith standards, but the Hanafi school accepts it because it aligns with the general practice of the Salaf.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The proof is the action of a Companion, which in Hanafi methodology is considered a form of evidence (amal al-sahabi) that indicates the sunnah.
Even though the hadith is munqati', it is strengthened by the fact that no other Companion is known to have opposed this practice.
4
Note any conditions or exceptions
Raising hands is sunnah; omitting it does not invalidate the prayer. There is no requirement to raise hands in the regular Takbirs of the prayer (except Takbir al-Ihram).
Hanafi school restricts raising hands to the initial Takbir al-Ihram in regular prayers, but allows it in Eid and Janazah prayers.

(۳۷۴) (۹) دونوں ہاتھ عیدین کی تکبیر میں اٹھائے گا۔
ان عمر بن الخطاب كان يرفع يديه مع كل تكبيرة في الجنازة والعيدين وهذا منقطع (ج) (سن للبیھقی ، باب رفع الیدین فی تکبیر العيدج ثالث ص ۴۱۲ نمبر ۲۱۸۹ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب التکبیر بالیدین ج ثالث ص ۲۹۷ نمبر ۵۶۹ ) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ تکبیر زوائد کہتے وقت ہاتھ بھی کانوں تک اٹھائے گا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) راوی اپنی سند حضرت عبداللہ ابن مسعود تک لے گئے ۔ حضرت ابن مسعود نے فرمایا چار تکبیر کہی جائے گی قرآت سے پہلے پھر قرآت کی جائے گی پر ، جب قرآت سے فارغ ہو جائیں تو تکبیر کہیں اور رکوع کریں۔ پھر دوسری رکعت میں کھڑے ہوں پس قرآت کرین پس جب قرآت سے فارغ ہو جائیں تو چار تکبیر کہیں (ب) آپ نے فرمایا تکبیر عید الفطر میں سات ہیں پہلی رکعت میں اور پانچ دوسری رکعت میں، اور قرآت دونوں ہی کے بعد ہے (ج) حضرت عمر ابن خطاب ہاتھ اٹھایا کرتے تھے ہر تکبیر کے ساتھ جنازہ میں اور عیدین میں ، یہ حدیث منقطع ہے۔ اٹھایا تھے ہر کے ساتھ اور میں بی منقطع
And then after it, he recites Surah al-Fatihah and a Surah with it, then he says Takbir and bows with it. (1373 (8)) Then he begins the second rak'ah with recitation. When he finishes the recitation, he says three Takbirs and says a fourth Takbir and bows with it. [1373 (9)] And he raises his hands in the Takbirs of the two Eids. From the hadiths it is known that in Eid prayer, in the first rak'ah after Takbir al-Ihram, three Takbirs are said. So with Takbir al-Ihram there are four Takbirs. Similarly, in the second rak'ah after recitation, three extra Takbirs are said, so with the Takbir of bowing there are four Takbirs. And in the second rak'ah after recitation, four Takbirs are said; its proof is this Athar: 'They referred their matter to Ibn Mas'ud, and he said: Say four Takbirs before recitation, then recite, when you finish say Takbir and bow, then stand for the second rak'ah and recite, when you finish say four Takbirs.' (a) (Sunan al-Siti, chapter: ...) In this Athar it is present that in the second rak'ah after recitation, four Takbirs are said: three extra Takbirs and one Takbir for bowing. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, in the first rak'ah seven Takbirs are said and in the second rak'ah five, and in both the Takbirs are before recitation. His proof is the hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As who said: The Prophet said: The Takbir in al-Fitr is seven in the first and five in the last, and the recitation is after both of them. (b) From these hadiths it is established that in the first rak'ah seven and in the second five Takbirs are said, and they are said before recitation. This difference is about istihbab. (373 (8)) Then he begins the second rak'ah with recitation, so when he finishes the recitation, he says three Takbirs and a fourth Takbir and goes into bowing with it. The detailed explanation and proof have passed. (374 (9)) He will raise both hands in the Takbirs of the two Eids. 'Umar ibn al-Khattab used to raise his hands with every Takbir in Janazah and the two Eids, and this is maqtu'. (c) From this it is known that when saying the extra Takbirs, he will raise his hands to the ears. Footnote: (a) The narrator traced to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. Ibn Mas'ud said: Four Takbirs are said before recitation, then recitation is done, when you finish recitation, say Takbir and bow. Then stand in the second rak'ah and recite, when you finish recitation, say four Takbirs. (b) He said: The Takbir of Eid al-Fitr is seven in the first and five in the second, and the recitation is after both. (c) Umar ibn al-Khattab used to raise his hands with every Takbir in Janazah and the two Eids; this hadith is munqati'.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the number and timing of extra Takbirs in Eid prayer. The author first presents the Hanafi ruling: in the first rak'ah, three extra Takbirs follow Takbir al-Ihram (so four total before recitation including the opening takbir). In the second rak'ah, after recitation, three extra Takbirs are said, then a fourth Takbir for bowing. The Hanafi proof is the Athar from Ibn Mas'ud, where he instructs four Takbirs before recitation in each rak'ah (the first being Takbir al-Ihram, the last being the bowing takbir in the first rak'ah, but in the second rak'ah the fourth is the bowing takbir). This is a Sahih Athar according to the Hanafi school. The Shafi'i view is also presented: seven Takbirs in the first rak'ah (including Takbir al-Ihram? Actually they count six extra plus one for bowing, or seven including Takbir al-Ihram), and five in the second (four extra plus bowing), all before recitation. Their proof is a hadith from Abdullah ibn Amr directly from the Prophet. The author notes that this difference is only over istihbab (recommendation), not obligation. Then the passage separately rules that hands should be raised during these extra Takbirs, citing Umar's practice as a weak (munqati') narration but used as supporting evidence. The commentary emphasizes the Hanafi position as the operative ruling.

Key Terms
منقطع (munqati'): A hadith with a broken chain of narration, not reaching the Prophet directly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on raising hands during the extra Takbirs of Eid prayer?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is sunnah.
C) It is makruh.
D) It is not established.

Key Takeaway
Raising hands with each extra Takbir in Eid prayer is a sunnah act, supported by the practice of the Companion Umar.

The Eid Khutbah: After the Prayer
Ruling with proof for Eid khutbah timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of the Eid khutbah, cite the prophetic proof, and explain the practical difference from Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
The Eid khutbah is delivered after the prayer, not before — confirmed by the practice of the Prophet ﷺ and the Caliphs.

In this passage, we examine a key difference between Eid and Jumu'ah: the order of prayer and sermon. While Jumu'ah has the khutbah before the prayer, Eid reverses this order. The text provides the ruling along with the hadith evidence from Sahih al-Bukhari. Additionally, brief rulings on missed prayer and crescent sighting are given.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delivering two sermons after the Eid prayer. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah), not wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the practice of the Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar as recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari (Hadith 963 and 975). The explicit text: 'كان النبي وابو بكر و عمر يصلون العيدين قبل الخطبة' (They used to pray Eid before the sermon).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The preposition 'before' indicates that prayer precedes sermon. The Prophet's consistent practice confirms this order.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
While the majority hold the khutbah after prayer, the Maliki school places it before. Within the Hanafi school, some consider listening to the khutbah wajib, but the relied-upon view is sunnah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the authentic practice and the consensus of the early caliphs. The mufta bihi is that two sermons after Eid prayer are sunnah muakkadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۷۵] (۱۰) ثم يخطب بعد الصلوة خطبتين يعلم الناس فيهما صدقة الفطر واحكامها ۳۷۶ (۱) ومن فاتته صلوة العيد مع الامام لم يقضها [۳۷۷ (۱۲) فان غم الهلال عن الناس وشهدو ا عند الامام برؤية الهلال بعد الزوال صلى العيد من الغد[۳۷۸] (۱۳)

[۳۷۵] (۱۰) پھر نماز کے بعد خطبہ دیں گے دو خطبے، ان میں لوگوں کو صدقہ فطر اور اس کے احکام سکھلائیں گے۔ جس طرح جمعہ میں دو خطبے دیئے جاتے ہیں اسی طرح عیدین میں بھی دو خطبے دیئے جائیں گے۔ اور عید الاضحی کا موقع ہوگا تو قربانی کے مسائل سکھلائے جائیں گے۔ نماز کے بعد خطبہ دینے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عمر قال كان النبي الله وابو بكر و عمر يصلون اليعدين قبل الخطبة (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الخطبة بعد العید ص ۱۳۱ نمبر ۹۶۳) اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ خطبہ نماز کے بعد دیا جائے گا، بخاری شریف، حدیث نمبر ۹۷۵ میں نماز کے بعد خطبہ کی تفصیل بیان کی گئی ہے۔ عبارت یہ ہے۔ ســمــعــت ابـن عبـاس قـال خرجت مع النبي الا الله يوم فطر او اضحى فصلى العيد ثم خطب ثم اتى النساء فوعظهن (بخاری شریف، باب خروج الصبيان الى المصلى ، ص ۱۳۲ نمبر ۹۷۵) اس حدیث میں خطبے کا تذکرہ ہے، اور یہ بھی ہے کہ نماز کے بعد خطبہ دیا۔
(375 (10)) Then after the prayer, he delivers two sermons; he teaches the people in them about Sadaqat al-Fitr and its rulings. (376 (11)) And whoever misses the Eid prayer with the Imam does not make it up. (377 (12)) So if the crescent is hidden from the people and they give witness to the Imam of sighting the crescent after zolwal, he prays the Eid prayer the next day. (378 (13)) ... Commentary: After the prayer, two sermons will be given; in them, people will be taught about Sadaqat al-Fitr and its rulings, just as on Jumu'ah two sermons are given. Similarly, on the occasion of Eid al-Adha, the rulings of sacrifice will be taught. The proof for giving sermons after prayer is the hadith: Ibn Umar said: The Prophet, Abu Bakr, and Umar used to pray the Eid prayer before the sermon. (a) (Bukhari, chapter: Sermon after Eid, p. 131 no. 963) This shows that the sermon is given after prayer. In Bukhari hadith no. 975, the detail is given: I heard Ibn Abbas say: I went out with the Prophet on the day of Fitr or Adha; he prayed the Eid prayer, then delivered a sermon, then went to the women and exhorted them. In this hadith there is mention of the sermon, and it is also stated that it is after the prayer.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling that the Eid prayer is followed by two sermons (khutbahayn), similar to Jumu'ah but delivered after the prayer. The sermons are used to teach the rulings of Sadaqat al-Fitr (for Eid al-Fitr) or Qurbani (for Eid al-Adha). The proof is the practice of the Prophet and the Caliphs, as narrated by Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas in Sahih al-Bukhari. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the sermons are separate from the prayer and are not a condition for its validity, but are a confirmed sunnah.

Key Terms
خطبتين (khutbatayn): Two sermons delivered after the Eid prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) During the Eid prayer
D) It is not delivered at all

Key Takeaway
The Eid khutbah is sunnah muakkadah and must be delivered after the prayer, based on the Prophet's ﷺ practice as recorded in Bukhari.

Ruling on Missed Eid Prayer (Qada)
Ruling that one who misses Eid prayer with the Imam does not make it up.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on missed Eid prayer and cite the evidence from the athar of the Companions and Successors.

Core Idea
Missed Eid prayer is not made up; its congregation cannot be replicated individually.

In this lesson, we examine a specific yet commonly encountered scenario: missing the Eid prayer with the imam. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that the Eid prayer is not made up as qada, but one may pray voluntary rak'ats. We will explore the textual proof from the sayings of 'Ata' and 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is missing the Eid prayer with the imam. The ruling is that one does not make it up as Eid prayer.
The ruling is based on the nature of Eid prayer as a congregational act.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two athar: the saying of 'Ata' and the saying of 'Abdullah (ibn Mas'ud).
These are from Sahih al-Bukhari and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Both athar instruct the person who misses the Eid to pray rak'ats individually, without the extra takbirs of Eid. This shows that the missed prayer is not repeated as Eid, but replaced with nafl.
The word 'صلى ركعتين' indicates a regular prayer, not mimicking the Eid format.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school agrees on no qada, but they recommend four rak'ats instead of two. Some early Hanafi scholars also allowed qada, but the relied-upon view is not to make it up.
The ikhtilaf is over the number of nafl rak'ats.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that missed Eid prayer is not made up; one may pray two or four rak'ats as nafl. This is established in Zahir al-Riwayah and affirmed by later authorities like Al-Hidayah.
The tarjih is based on the authenticity of the athar and the principle that Eid is specifically congregational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۷۶ (۱) ومن فاتته صلوة العيد مع الامام لم يقضها [۳۷۷ (۱۲) فان غم الهلال عن الناس وشهدو ا عند الامام برؤية الهلال بعد الزوال صلى العيد من الغد[۳۷۸] (۱۳)

(۱۳۷۶ (۱۱) جس کی عید کی نماز فوت ہو جائے امام کے ساتھ اس کو قضا نہیں کرے گا۔ (۱) نماز عید اجتماعیت کے ساتھ مشروع ہے اور جس کی نماز عید امام کے ساتھ چھوٹ گئی تو اب اجتماعیت نہیں ہوگی اس لئے اب نماز عید کو قضا نہیں کرے گا۔ البتہ دورکعت نفل کے طور پر پڑھنا چاہے تو پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ دلیل یہ قول ہے قال عــطـاء اذا فاته العيد صلى ركعتين (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا فاته العید صلی رکعتین ص ۱۳۳ نمبر ۹۸۷) (۲) قال عبد الله مـن فـاتـه العيد فليصل اربعا (ج) مصنف ابن ابي هيبة ، ۴۲۹ الرجل تفوته الصلوة في العيد كم صلی ج ثانی ص نم نمبر ۸۷۹۹ ) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جس کی نماز عید فوت ہو جائے وہ نفلی طور پر چار رکعت پڑھے۔
(376 (11)) And whoever misses the Eid prayer with the Imam does not make it up. (377 (12)) So if the crescent is hidden from the people and they give witness to the Imam of sighting the crescent after zolwal, he prays the Eid prayer the next day. (378 (13)) ... Commentary: The one whose Eid prayer is missed with the Imam will not make it up. The Eid prayer is prescribed with congregation, and if one misses it with the Imam, then congregation is not possible, so he will not make it up as Eid prayer. However, if he wishes to pray two rak'ats as nafl, he may do so. The proof is the saying of 'Ata': 'When one misses the Eid, he prays two rak'ats.' (b) (Bukhari, chapter: When one misses the Eid, he prays two rak'ats, p. 133 no. 987) And 'Abdullah said: 'Whoever misses the Eid, let him pray four rak'ats.' (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, ...) From this Athar, it is known that whoever misses the Eid prayer prays four rak'ats as nafl.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage rules that a person who misses the Eid prayer with the Imam does not make it up with the intention of Eid (i.e., as the Eid prayer itself). The reason is that Eid prayer is legislated with congregation (jama'ah), and that specific form cannot be replicated individually. Therefore, it is not performed as a missed prayer (qada). However, one may pray two or four rak'ats as nafl (voluntary prayer) to make up for the spiritual benefit. The proofs are the statements of 'Ata' and 'Abdullah ('Abdullah ibn Mas'ud according to the commentary). The Hanafi school follows the view that missed Eid prayer is not made up, but it is permissible to pray nafl.

Key Terms
قضا (qada): Making up a missed prayer after its prescribed time.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary prayer performed beyond the obligatory prayers.
صلاة العيد (salat al-‘id): The Eid prayer performed on Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha, consisting of two rak'ats with extra takbirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Pray two or four rak'ats as nafl
C) It is not necessary to do anything
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that missed Eid prayer is not made up; one may optionally pray nafl.

Sighting of the Moon and Excuse for Eid Prayer
Ruling on late moon sighting and excuse delaying prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the moon of Eid is sighted after Zolwal and identify when the Eid prayer is excused entirely.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is performed the next day if moon sighting testimony comes after Zolwal; if even the next day is missed due to excuse, it is not made up.

The timing of Eid prayer depends on when the new moon is confirmed. If the moon is sighted after midday (Zolwal) on the expected day of Eid, the prayer is not performed that day but the following morning. This ruling is based on a prophetic hadith and has an important exception: if an excuse prevents the prayer on the next day, it is not performed at all. Let's work through the evidence and the conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage deals with a situation where the crescent of Shawwal was not seen on the night before Eid, but witnesses come to the Imam after Zolwal on the day of Eid, testifying that they saw the moon the previous night.
The key moment is Zolwal (noon).
2
State the ruling for that scenario
The ruling is that the Eid prayer is not performed on that day but is delayed to the next day. This applies regardless of whether the testimony is accepted after Zolwal.
Some may think the prayer can be done later in the day, but the Hanafi position is clear.
3
Examine the dalil (proof)
The hadith of Abu Umair ibn Anas is cited: riders came to the Prophet after having seen the moon the previous day. The Prophet ordered them to break their fast (indicating it was Eid) and to go to the prayer ground the next morning. This shows the prayer was postponed to the next day.
The hadith is a hadith ahad, so its proof level is zanni in both transmission and meaning.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit command to pray the next day when the testimony came after the previous day's Zolwal indicates that the prayer is not performed on the same day if the news arrives after noon.
Implicitly, if the news came before Zolwal, the prayer could be performed that day.
5
Note the exception for excuse
If on the following day an excuse prevents the congregation from gathering (e.g., extreme weather, enemy attack), then the Eid prayer is not performed at all. It is not made up later because its time has passed.
This shows the Eid prayer is tied to its specific time and congregation; it is not a make-up prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۷۷ (۱۲) فان غم الهلال عن الناس وشهدو ا عند الامام برؤية الهلال بعد الزوال صلى العيد من الغد[۳۷۸] (۱۳)

۱۳۷۷۱ (۱۲) پس اگر لوگوں کو چاند نظر نہ آئے اور امام کے پاس چاند دیکھنے کی گواہی زوال کے بعد دی تو عید کی نماز اگلی صبح کو پڑھے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابی عمير بن انس عن عمومة له من اصحاب النبي عل الله ان ركبا جاء وا الى النبي الله يشهدون انهم روا الهلال بالامس فامرهم ان يفطروا واذا اصبحوا ان يغدوا الى مصلا هم (د) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب اذا لم يخرج الامام للعيد من يومه يخرج من الغد ص ۷۱ انمبر ۱۵۷ ارسنن سیھتی ، باب الشھو دیشھدون على رؤية الهلال آخر النهار ج ثالث ص ۴۴۲، نمبر ۳ ۶۳۸ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زوال کے بعد چاند دیکھنے کی گواہی آئے تو اگلے دن نماز عید پڑھی جائے گی۔ (۳۷۸) (۱۳) پس اگر کوئی عذر پیش آجائے کہ لوگوں کو دوسرے دن بھی نماز سے روک دے تو اس کے بعد نماز عید نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔

حاشیہ : (د) ابو عمیر بن انس فرماتے ہیں کہ کچھ سوار حضور کے پاس آئے۔ انہوں نے کل چاند دیکھنے کی گواہی دی تو آپ نے ان کو حکم دیا کہ افطار کرے اور جب صبح کرے تو عید گاہ کی طرف آئے۔
(377 (12)) So if the crescent is hidden from the people and they give witness to the Imam of sighting the crescent after zolwal, he prays the Eid prayer the next day. (378 (13)) ... Commentary: If the people do not see the moon, and they give witness to the Imam of seeing the moon after Zolwal, then the Eid prayer will be prayed the next morning. In the hadith: From Abu 'Umair ibn Anas from his uncles among the Companions of the Prophet: that a group of riders came to the Prophet bearing witness that they had seen the crescent the previous day, so he ordered them to break their fast and when they reached morning, to go to their place of prayer. (d) From this hadith, it is known that if testimony of seeing the moon after Zolwal comes, then the Eid prayer is prayed the next day. (378 (13)) So if an excuse arises that prevents the people from praying even the next day, then after that the Eid prayer is not prayed. Footnote: (d) Abu Umair ibn Anas says: Some riders came to the Prophet; they gave testimony of seeing the moon the previous day, so the Prophet ordered them to break their fast and when it was morning, to go to the Eid prayer ground.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage covers two connected rulings. First, if the moon is not sighted on the night before Eid, or there is confusion, and later (after Zolwal on the day of Eid) witnesses come to the Imam testifying that they saw the moon the previous night (i.e., the night of the 29th or 30th of Ramadan/shawwal), then the Eid prayer is not performed that day but rather the next day. The proof is the hadith of Abu 'Umair ibn Anas where the Prophet ordered the riders (who had seen the moon the day before) to break their fast (i.e., the day was Eid) and to go to the prayer ground the next day (since the news came after Zolwal on the day of Eid). Second, if an excuse prevents the people from praying even on that following day (such as extreme weather, security threat, etc.), then the Eid prayer is not performed at all—it is not delayed further. This shows that the Eid prayer is tied to its specific day and congregation; if both opportunities (the proper day and the next day) pass, it is not made up.

Key Terms
زوال (zolwal): The time when the sun passes its zenith, i.e., midday.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If witnesses testify to seeing the moon of Shawwal after Zolwal on the day of Eid, when is the Eid prayer performed?
A) Immediately upon the testimony
B) The next day
C) Three days later
D) It is not performed at all

Key Takeaway
Eid prayer is performed the next day if moon sighting testimony comes after Zolwal; if an excuse prevents even the next day, it is not made up.

Moon Sighting After Zawal – Eid Next Day
Ruling to delay Eid prayer to next day if moon sighted after zawal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that if the crescent is sighted after zawal on the day of doubt, the Eid prayer is performed the next morning, and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Sight the moon late? Eid prayer moves to tomorrow – the time is fixed after sunrise.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: on the 30th of Ramadan, the moon is not sighted at night, but later during the day after zawal witnesses come to the imam. When should the Eid prayer be held? The Hanafi ruling, based on a direct prophetic practice, is to postpone the prayer to the following morning. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage: people did not see the moon at night, but after zawal they testify before the imam. The ruling: the Eid prayer is performed the next morning.
The key is that zawal is the dividing line.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites a hadith from Abu Dawud and Bayhaqi. Identify the sunnah proof: a group of riders came to the Prophet and testified they saw the moon the previous day.
The hadith is a hadith ahad (single chain) but accepted in fiqh.
3
Analyze wajh al-dalalah (how the hadith proves the ruling)
The Prophet ordered them to break their fast (because it is now Eid) and to go to the musalla the next morning. The phrase 'next morning' (ghad) indicates the prayer is delayed to the following day.
The order to go to the musalla is interpreted as the Eid prayer.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) hold that if the moon is sighted after zawal, the prayer can still be performed that day after sunrise because the day of Eid begins at Fajr. Understand their position and the Hanafi response.
The Hanafi position is based on explicit prophetic action.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice: if witnesses come after zawal, the imam should announce that tomorrow is Eid and schedule the prayer for the next morning. The community breaks their fast that evening.
This ruling applies only if the testimony is accepted (two just witnesses).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پس اگر لوگوں کو چاند نظر نہ آئے اور امام کے پاس چاند دیکھنے کی گواہی زوال کے بعد دی تو عید کی نماز اگلی صبح کو پڑھے گا۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابی عمير بن انس عن عمومة له من اصحاب النبي عل الله ان ركبا جاء وا الى النبي الله يشهدون انهم روا الهلال بالامس فامرهم ان يفطروا واذا اصبحوا ان يغدوا الى مصلا هم (ابوداؤد شریف، باب اذا لم يخرج الامام للعيد من يومه يخرج من الغد ص ۷۱ انمبر ۱۵۷ ارسنن سیھتی ، باب الشھو دیشھدون على رؤية الهلال آخر النهار ج ثالث ص ۴۴۲، نمبر ۳ ۶۳۸ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ زوال کے بعد چاند دیکھنے کی گواہی آئے تو اگلے دن نماز عید پڑھی جائے گی۔
So if the moon is hidden from the people and they testify before the imam about seeing the crescent after midday, then he will pray the Eid prayer the following morning. In the hadith: from Abu 'Umayr ibn Anas from his uncles among the Companions of the Prophet that some riders came to the Prophet and testified that they had seen the crescent yesterday. He ordered them to break their fast and when they rose in the morning to go to their place of prayer. (Abu Dawud, Bab idha lam yakhruj al-imam lil-eid min yawmihi yakhruju min al-ghad, p. 71, no. 1157; also in Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-shuhud yashhaduna ala ru'yat al-hilal akhir al-nahar, vol. 3, p. 442, no. 638) From this hadith it is understood that if testimony of sighting the crescent comes after zawal, the Eid prayer will be performed the next day.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage discusses the situation when the new moon (hilal) for Eid is not sighted on the night of the 30th of Ramadan, and people testify before the imam after the sun passes its zenith (zawal) on the day of doubt. According to the Hanafi school, if such testimony is accepted (which requires two just witnesses), the Eid prayer is not performed that day because the proper time for the Eid prayer is after sunrise. Instead, the imam postpones the prayer to the next day (the 31st of Ramadan / 1st Shawwal). The hadith of the riders supports this: when they testified after the day had begun, the Prophet ordered them to break their fast (since it was now Eid) and to go to the musalla the next morning. This indicates that the Eid prayer is offered on the day following the sighting if the sighting occurs late in the day.

Key Terms
زوال (zawal): The moment when the sun passes its zenith, marking the beginning of the time for Zhuhr prayer.
عید نماز (Eid namaz): The salah performed on the day of Eid al-Fitr or Eid al-Adha.
ہلال (hilal): The crescent moon that marks the beginning of a lunar month.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The same day after the sighting
B) The next morning
C) The following Friday
D) It is not performed

Key Takeaway
When the Eid moon is sighted after zawal, the Eid prayer is offered the next morning, as per the Prophet's practice.

Eid Prayer: No Make-Up After the Second Day
Ruling on time limit for Eid prayer make-up

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time limit for Eid prayer and explain the analogy (qiyas) with Jumu'ah that supports it.

Core Idea
Eid prayer is time-bound to its day or the second day; if missed due to excuse, it is not made up later.

Previously, we learned that if the Eid prayer is missed on the day of Eid due to a moon sighting issue, it may be performed on the second day. But what if an excuse also prevents prayer on the second day? This lesson clarifies the finality of that window. The Hanafi school, drawing an analogy with Jumu'ah, holds that the Eid prayer cannot be performed after the second day under any circumstance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Original Time
Recognize that the act under discussion is the Eid prayer (salat al-Eid). Its original prescribed time is the morning of the day of Eid (10th Dhul Hijjah).
The Eid prayer is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
2
Recognize the Exceptional Allowance for the Second Day
Due to a hadith (the riders), the Hanafi school allows the Eid prayer to be performed on the second day (11th Dhul Hijjah) if it was missed on the first day because of an excuse (e.g., moon sighting confusion).
This is an exception to the general rule that worship is tied to its specific time.
3
Understand the Reasoning: Analogy with Jumu'ah
The author uses qiyas (analogy) with Jumu'ah prayer: Jumu'ah is not made up if missed after its time. Since Eid prayer is similar in being a time-specific congregational obligation, it should also not be made up beyond the second day.
The key illa (effective cause) is the limited prescribed time slot for the congregation.
4
Apply the Ruling to the Third Day Scenario
Apply the rule: If an excuse prevents the Eid prayer on the second day, then the prayer cannot be performed on the third day or any later day. The obligation drops entirely.
There is no evidence to extend the exception to a third day.
5
Conclude the Consequence
The consequence is that the Eid prayer is no longer wajib upon the community; individuals do not need to make it up individually either.
This contrasts with missed fard prayers which must be made up.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پس اگر کوئی عذر پیش آجائے کہ لوگوں کو دوسرے دن بھی نماز سے روک دے تو اس کے بعد نماز عید نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔
So if an excuse occurs that prevents people from prayer on the second day, then the Eid prayer will not be performed after that.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage completes the previous ruling. If the Eid prayer could not be performed on the day of Eid (due to the moon sighting issue) and is postponed to the next day, but even on that second day the prayer cannot be performed due to some valid excuse (e.g., heavy rain, fear, or other impediment), then the Eid prayer is not performed at all thereafter. The author reasons that the Eid prayer is like Jumu'ah in that it is not made up after its prescribed time has passed, but due to the hadith of the riders, it is exceptionally allowed to pray it on the second day. However, there is no evidence for a third day, so it is not allowed. This is based on analogy (qiyas) with Jumu'ah, where if it is missed, it is not made up.

Key Terms
عذر (udhr): A valid excuse that prevents performing the Eid prayer congregationally, such as extreme weather or security concerns.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the Eid prayer could not be performed on the day of Eid nor the next day due to an excuse, what is the ruling?
A) It should be performed on the third day
B) It is not performed at all after that
C) It is performed as individual prayer
D) It is postponed to the next Friday

Key Takeaway
The Eid prayer's performance window is limited to its day or the second day; beyond that, the obligation drops entirely.

Recommended Acts for Eid al-Adha
Listing mustahabbat (recommended acts) for Eid al-Adha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts for Eid al-Adha and distinguish the timing of eating from Eid al-Fitr.

Core Idea
On Eid al-Adha, it is sunnah to delay eating until after the prayer, unlike Eid al-Fitr.

Eid al-Adha has specific recommended practices that differ from Eid al-Fitr. This lesson presents the three key mustahabbat: ghusl, perfume, and delaying eating. The evidence from the hadith provides the basis for the delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three acts
Read the text and list the three recommended acts explicitly mentioned for Eid al-Adha.
They are ghusl, applying perfume, and delaying eating.
2
Note the difference from Eid al-Fitr
Observe that on Eid al-Fitr it is recommended to eat before the prayer, while on Adha it is the opposite.
This difference is based on the hadith of Buraidah.
3
Understand the hadith evidence
The hadith shows the Prophet would eat on Fitr before prayer but would not eat on Nahr until after prayer and then from his sacrifice.
Darqutni records this hadith.
4
Recognize the wisdom
The text gives a reason: to enhance the spirit of worship by fasting briefly.
This is a secondary rationale.

Source Text

On the day of Eid al-Adha, it is recommended to perform ghusl, apply perfume, and delay eating until he finishes the prayer. Eid al-Adha is similar to Eid al-Fitr. As for eating after the prayer, it is recommended, and its evidence is the hadith: 'Abdullah ibn Buraidah narrated from his father that the Prophet would not go out on the day of Fitr until he had eaten, and he would not eat anything on the day of Nahr until he returned and ate from his sacrifice.' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Eidain, vol. 2, p. 34, no. 1999) From this hadith it is understood that on the occasion of sacrifice, he will eat after the Eid prayer. Also, since he has been eating daily, today he should refrain for a short while so that worship can be performed.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage enumerates the recommended acts (mustahabbat) specifically for Eid al-Adha. (1) Ghusl and applying perfume are recommended as they are for Eid al-Fitr. (2) Unlike Eid al-Fitr where it is recommended to eat before the prayer, on Eid al-Adha it is recommended to delay eating until after the prayer, then eat from one's sacrifice. The hadith from Buraidah supports this. The reasoning is also to increase the spirit of worship by not eating immediately.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Full body wash, recommended on both Eids, before going to the musalla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Reciting Takbir While Going to Eid Prayer
Ruling to say takbir while going to Eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on reciting takbir while going to the Eid prayer and identify the basis and timing from Hanafi sources.

Core Idea
Reciting takbir loudly on the way to Eid prayer is a confirmed sunnah, not wajib.

The Eid prayer is a festive occasion, and the sunnah teaches us to announce our joy with takbir even before reaching the musalla. This lesson clarifies the ruling, timing, and evidence for this practice, following the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is proceeding to the Eidgah (musalla) while reciting takbir. The Hanafi ruling is that this is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
It is distinct from the wajib Takbirat al-Tashriq after prayers.
2
Locate the evidence
The text cites an athar from Ibn Umar (Darqutni) that he used to go out on both Eid days raising his voice with takbir until reaching the musalla. This is the main proof.
The author also refers to a hadith mentioned earlier in the book.
3
Determine the timing
The takbir begins when leaving home and continues until the imam arrives at the musalla. For Eid al-Adha, it connects to the Takbirat al-Tashriq after the prayer.
The loud recitation is a distinctive feature of Eid.
4
Note the emphasis on loudness
The text says 'zoor se' (loudly). This indicates that jahr (audible recitation) is part of the sunnah, making the practice conspicuous.
It is not limited to silent recitation.
5
Apply in practice
On both Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha, a Hanafi should recite takbir audibly from home to the prayer place. This applies to men; for women, it is done quietly.
The takbir is 'Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illallah, wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar, wa lillahil hamd.'

The takbir begins from the time one leaves home until the imam arrives. This is supported by the practice of Ibn Umar, as recorded by Darqutni. The loud takbir is a distinctive feature of Eid days, and for Eid al-Adha, it is connected to the Takbirat al-Tashriq which begin after Fajr on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms
تکبیر (takbir): The phrase 'Allahu Akbar' recited loudly on the way to the Eid prayer, and also during the days of Tashriq.

Eid al-Adha Prayer and Khutbah
Ruling that Eid al-Adha prayer and khutbah are similar to Eid al-Fitr with different content

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the Eid al-Adha prayer and khutbah, and identify the content taught in the sermon.

Core Idea
Eid al-Adha prayer mirrors Eid al-Fitr; the khutbah teaches sacrifice and Takbirat al-Tashriq.

This short passage from the matn succinctly describes the Eid al-Adha prayer and its sermon. It establishes that the prayer is identical in format to Eid al-Fitr, while the sermon's content shifts to the specific acts of worship of these days: sacrifice (udhiyah) and the Takbirat al-Tashriq. Understanding this helps us appreciate how the Hanafi school links the ritual to its seasonal context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being described? The text says 'He will pray the Eid al-Adha prayer, two rak'ats.' The Hanafi ruling is that the Eid prayer is wajib (necessary).
Abu Hanifa holds it as wajib; his two disciples consider it sunnah muakkadah.
2
Recognize the structural equivalence
The text explicitly says 'similar to the Eid al-Fitr prayer.' This means both prayers have the same number of rak'ats (two) and the same extra takbirs (six in the Hanafi school).
The extra takbirs are not mentioned here but are part of the established ruling.
3
Focus on the sermon content
After the prayer, the imam delivers two sermons. The content is specified: teaching the rulings of sacrifice (udhiyah) and the Takbirat al-Tashriq.
This distinguishes the Eid al-Adha khutbah from the Eid al-Fitr khutbah, which focuses on zakat al-fitr.
4
Connect to the broader Hanafi framework
The text implies the imam's educational role. The Takbirat al-Tashriq are wajib for men to recite after every fard prayer from Fajr of 9th Dhul Hijjah to Asr of 13th Dhul Hijjah.
The khutbah serves to remind the congregation of these seasonal obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عید الاضحی کی نماز پڑھے گا دو رکعت عید الفطر کی نماز کی طرح اور اس کے بعد خطبہ دے گا دو خطبے اس میں لوگوں کو قربانی کے احکام اور تکبیر تشریق سکھائیں گے۔
He will pray the Eid al-Adha prayer, two rak'ats, similar to the Eid al-Fitr prayer, and after it he will deliver two sermons, in which he will teach the people the rulings of sacrifice and the Takbirat al-Tashriq.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This final passage summarizes the Eid al-Adha prayer: it consists of two rak'ats just like Eid al-Fitr. After the prayer, the imam delivers two sermons (khutbahs) as in Eid al-Fitr. However, the content of the sermons is different: on Eid al-Adha, the imam teaches the rulings of sacrifice (udhiyah) and the Takbirat al-Tashriq. This is because the key acts of worship on these days are sacrifice and the takbirs. The sermons serve an educational purpose to guide the community in performing these acts correctly.

Key Terms
تکبیر تشریق (takbirat al-tashriq): The takbirs recited after every fard prayer from Fajr of 9th Dhul Hijjah to Asr of 13th Dhul Hijjah; the imam teaches these rulings in the khutbah.

Missed Eid Prayer: Makeup Only on Second Day
Ruling with proof on Eid makeup time limit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up missed Eid prayer and explain why it is limited to the second day.

Core Idea
Eid prayer may only be made up on the second day, based on a specific hadith contrary to general analogy.

The Eid prayer is wajib, but its makeup is unique. Unlike regular prayers, it cannot be made up any day. This lesson explains the ruling and its proof: a hadith permits makeup on the second day only, overriding the general analogy with Jumu'ah. Understanding this helps you appreciate how specific textual evidence can override general principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making up (qada') the missed Eid prayer. The ruling is that it is permitted only on the second day, not on the third.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a specific hadith (not quoted in the text) that allows makeup on the second day. The text refers to it as 'the mentioned hadith'.
The hadith is not explicitly cited, but its existence is the basis for the exception.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith provides a direct textual permission for makeup on the second day, which is an exception to the general rule derived from qiyas.
4
Analyze the qiyas overriding
By analogy with Jumu'ah prayer, Eid prayer should not be made up at all (since both are congregational prayers with specific times). The hadith overrides this qiyas for the second day.
5
Determine the scope
Since no hadith exists for the third day, the default qiyas applies: no makeup on the third day.

Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof statement regarding the makeup (qada') of Eid prayer. The author states that if an excuse prevented the congregation from performing the Eid prayer on the first day, it may be performed on the second day, but not on the third. He explains that by analogy (qiyas) with Jumu'ah, Eid prayer should not be made up at all, because both are congregational prayers with a specific time. However, a specific hadith (referenced but not quoted here) permits making it up on the second day, thereby overriding the analogy. Since no such hadith exists for the third day, the ruling reverts to the original principle: no makeup after the second day.

Key Terms
قضا (qada'): Making up a missed obligatory prayer after its prescribed time.

Key Takeaway

Core Idea
Reciting takbir audibly on the way to Eid prayer is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) based on the practice of the Companions.

Have you ever wondered about the proper way to conduct yourself on the way to the Eid prayer? Our author, following the Hanafi school, highlights a beautiful sunnah: reciting takbir loudly as you proceed. This practice not only fills the air with the remembrance of Allah but also connects us to the generation of the Prophet's Companions. In this lesson, we will examine the ruling and the evidence that establishes it.

Locate the dalil

Makeup of Eid al-Adha Prayer: Up to Two Days
Ruling on performing missed Eid prayer on subsequent days due to excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number of days for makeup of Eid al-Adha prayer and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) that ties the prayer to the days of sacrifice (ayyam al-nahr).

Core Idea
Eid al-Adha prayer can be made up only on the two days following the festival, because the prayer is tied to the days of sacrifice.

Eid al-Adha prayer is normally performed on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. But if a legitimate excuse prevents the community from praying on that day, the prayer may be performed on subsequent days. This lesson explains how many days are allowed and why the ruling is limited, based on the connection to the days of sacrifice (ayyam al-nahr).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the Eid al-Adha prayer. The ruling is that it is normally performed on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, but if missed due to an excuse, it can be made up on the 11th and the 12th, but not on the 13th or later.
The prayer itself is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is not a direct Quran or hadith quote, but a ta'lil (reasoning): the prayer is linked to the days of sacrifice (ayyam al-nahr), which are three days: 10th, 11th, and 12th. Since the prayer accompanies the sacrifice, its time for makeup extends only through these days.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The connection is that Eid al-Adha is the festival of sacrifice, so its prayer is associated with the days when sacrifice is prescribed. After the 12th, the time for sacrifice ends, so the prayer is no longer offered.
This reasoning shows that the makeup is limited to the days of nahr.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that Eid prayer is merely sunnah muakkadah, not wajib, and thus may not have a prescribed makeup. The Hanafi school differs and considers it wajib, hence the makeup rule.
The practical difference: Hanafis will pray makeup; Shafi'is may not consider it necessary.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the strong connection between the Eid prayer and the sacrifice, which is a confirmed practice. The makeup is allowed only up to the 12th because that is the last day of sacrifice.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان حدث عذر منع الناس من الصلوة يوم الاضحى صلاها من الغد و بعد الغد ولا يصليها بعد ذلك [۳۸۲ (۱۷) تشریح عید الاضحی کی نماز دسویں تاریخ کو پڑھی جائے گی لیکن کوئی عذر پیش آجائے تو گیارہویں کو پڑھے اور اس پر بھی کوئی عذر پیش آ جائے تو بارہویں کو پڑھے۔ البتہ تیرہویں کو نہیں پڑھ سکتا۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قربانی تین دن مشروع ہے اور یہ عید قربانی کی ہے اس لئے بارہویں تک قربانی مشروع ہے تو بارہویں تک عید کی نماز بھی عذر کی وجہ سے پڑھ سکتا ہے۔
If an excuse occurs preventing people from the prayer on the day of Adha, he prays it the next day and the day after next, and does not pray it after that. [382 (17)] Explanation: The Eid al-Adha prayer is performed on the 10th date, but if an excuse occurs, he prays on the 11th, and if an excuse occurs even on that, then he prays on the 12th. However, he cannot pray on the 13th. The reason is that sacrifice is prescribed for three days, and this is the Eid of sacrifice, so sacrifice is prescribed until the 12th, therefore the Eid prayer can also be prayed until the 12th due to excuse.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for missing Eid al-Adha prayer due to a legitimate excuse. The normal day is the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. If an excuse prevents it, the prayer may be performed on the 11th. If still prevented, then on the 12th. It cannot be performed on the 13th. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that the days of sacrifice (ayyam al-nahr) are three: the 10th, 11th, and 12th. Since Eid al-Adha is the festival of sacrifice, its prayer is tied to these days. After the 12th, the time for sacrifice has passed, so the prayer also is no longer performed.

Key Terms
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The days of sacrifice: 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 11th only
C) 12th
D) 13th

Key Takeaway
Eid al-Adha prayer makeup is limited to the 11th and 12th of Dhul Hijjah, as the prayer is tied to the days of sacrifice.

The Timing of Takbir al-Tashriq: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of Takbir al-Tashriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the timing of Takbir al-Tashriq, identify their respective proofs, and explain which view is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The timing of Takbir al-Tashriq is disputed within the Hanafi school; the mufta bihi view follows the Sahibayn.

Takbir al-Tashriq is a sunnah recited after obligatory prayers during the days of Hajj. However, there is a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the exact ending time. This lesson examines the views of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples, their proofs, and the position that is relied upon for fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
First, identify the view of Imam Abu Hanifa: Takbir al-Tashriq begins after Fajr of 9th Dhul Hijjah and ends after Asr of 10th, covering eight prayers.
This is the earlier view.
2
Identify the opposing view
Next, state the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): It begins after Fajr of 9th and ends after Asr of 13th, covering 23 prayers.
This view is more cautious.
3
Examine the proofs
Consider the proof for each: Abu Hanifa relies on an athar from Ibn Mas'ud; the Sahibayn rely on a hadith from Jabir directly from the Prophet.
Jabir's hadith is considered more authoritative.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: eight prayers vs. twenty-three prayers of takbir after fard salah.
This affects the duration of recitation in mosques.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states that currently the fatwa is on the view of the two companions. Understand why this view is preferred.
The hadith-based view is stronger in transmission.

Source Text

And the Takbir al-Tashriq: its beginning is after the Fajr prayer of the day of 'Arafah and its end is after the 'Asr prayer of the day of Nahr according to Abu Hanifa. [384 (19)] And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: until the 'Asr prayer of the last days of Tashriq. [385 (20)] And the takbir after (the prayer). Takbir al-Tashriq: its beginning is after Fajr of the day of 'Arafah to after 'Asr of the day of Nahr according to Imam Abu Hanifa. He will begin Takbir al-Tashriq after Fajr of 9th Dhul Hijjah and will say it until after 'Asr of 10th Dhul Hijjah, total eight prayers. His proof is this athar: from Abu Wail from 'Abdullah (Ibn Mas'ud) that he would recite takbir from Fajr of 'Arafah to 'Asr of the day of Nahr. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Vol. 1, p. 488, no. 6335). This athar indicates that Takbir al-Tashriq is said until 'Asr of the 10th. [384 (19)] And the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said (from Fajr of 'Arafah) to the 'Asr prayer of the last days of Tashriq. According to them, Takbir al-Tashriq is recited from Fajr of 9th to after 'Asr of 13th. Their proof is this hadith: from Jabir ibn 'Abdullah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would recite takbir in the Fajr prayer of 'Arafah to the 'Asr prayer of the last days of Tashriq when he finished the obligatory prayers. (al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-'Eidain, vol. 2, p. 37, no. 719, and al-Bayhaqi, Bab man Istawhab an yabtadi'a al-takbir, vol. 3, p. 440, no. 6278). This hadith indicates that from Fajr of 9th to 'Asr of 13th, Takbir al-Tashriq is recited after every obligatory prayer. Nowadays, the fatwa is on this. 'Uqib: after. [385 (20)] The takbir after the obligatory prayer is as follows: Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, la ilaha illa 'Llah, wa 'Llahu akbar, Allahu akbar, wa li 'Llahi 'l-hamd.
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of Takbir al-Tashriq (the additional takbir recited after obligatory prayers during the days of Tashriq). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it begins after Fajr of the day of 'Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) and ends after 'Asr of the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), covering eight prayers. His evidence is an athar from Ibn Mas'ud. The two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that it begins after Fajr of 'Arafah and ends after 'Asr of the last days of Tashriq (13th Dhul Hijjah), covering 23 prayers. Their proof is a hadith from Jabir directly from the Prophet (peace be upon him). The author then states that today (i.e., in his time and onwards) the fatwa is given according to the opinion of the two companions. Finally, the wording of the takbir is given: 'Allahu akbar, Allahu akbar, la ilaha illa 'Llah, wa 'Llahu akbar, Allahu akbar, wa li 'Llahi 'l-hamd.'

Key Terms
تكبير التشريق (Takbir al-Tashriq): The takbir recited after obligatory prayers from 9th to 13th Dhul Hijjah.
أيام التشريق (ayyam al-tashriq): The three days following the day of Nahr: 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's operative position for Takbir al-Tashriq is the view of the two companions: from Fajr of 9th to Asr of 13th.

Delay of Eid al-Adha Prayer Due to Excuse
Ruling on makeup of Eid al-Adha prayer when prevented by excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a missed Eid al-Adha prayer due to an excuse can be made up, and identify the time limit with its underlying rationale.

Core Idea
Eid al-Adha prayer delayed by excuse must be performed within the three days of sacrifice.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: what happens if a legitimate excuse prevents the congregation from performing the Eid al-Adha prayer on its prescribed day (10th of Dhul Hijjah)? The ruling is that the prayer must be performed on the following two days (11th and 12th) but not beyond. The commentary explains the reasoning by linking the prayer to the sacrifice (qurbani), which is also prescribed for three days. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling
The Eid al-Adha prayer is wajib and normally performed on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. Recognize that this is the baseline.
2
Identify the exception
A legitimate excuse ('udhr) prevents the congregation from performing the prayer on its original day.
3
State the makeup window
The prayer must be performed on the next day (11th) and the day after (12th), but not after the 12th.
The Arabic uses 'min al-ghad wa ba'da al-ghad' – the following day and the one after.
4
Understand the rationale
The Urdu commentary links the prayer to the sacrifice: since sacrifice is prescribed for three days (10th-12th), the prayer can be delayed within these days. After the 12th, the sacrifice time ends, so the prayer is no longer performed.
5
Apply to a scenario
Test your understanding: if an excuse persists through the 11th and 12th, the prayer is not performed at all; it is not made up later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان حدث عذر منع الناس من الصلوة يوم الاضحى صلاها من الغد و بعد الغد ولا يصليها بعد ذلك پس اگر کوئی عذر پیش آجائے کہ لوگوں و عید الاضحی کی نماز سے روک دے تو نماز پڑھے گا کل اور پرسوں اور نہیں پڑھے گا اس کے بعد تشریح عید الاضحی کی نماز دسویں تاریخ کو پڑھی جائے گی لیکن کوئی عذر پیش آجائے تو گیارہویں کو پڑھے اور اس پر بھی کوئی عذر پیش آ جائے تو بارہویں کو پڑھے۔ البتہ تیرہویں کو نہیں پڑھ سکتا۔ اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قربانی تین دن مشروع ہے اور یہ عید قربانی کی ہے اس لئے بارہویں تک قربانی مشروع ہے تو بارہویں تک عید کی نماز بھی عذر کی وجہ سے پڑھ سکتا ہے۔
If an excuse occurs that prevents people from the prayer on the day of Adha, they pray it the next day and the day after, and they do not pray it after that. (Urdu: So if an excuse arises that prevents people from the Eid al-Adha prayer, they will pray it tomorrow and the day after, and they will not pray it after that. Explanation: The Eid al-Adha prayer is offered on the 10th. But if an excuse arises, they may pray on the 11th. If still an excuse, they may pray on the 12th. However, they cannot pray on the 13th. The reason is that sacrifice is prescribed for three days, and this is the Eid of sacrifice, so sacrifice is prescribed up to the 12th, therefore the Eid prayer can also be performed up to the 12th due to excuse.)
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This is a ruling statement regarding the makeup of Eid al-Adha prayer when an excuse prevents the congregation on its prescribed day. The Arabic matn states that if an excuse prevents the Eid prayer on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, it should be performed on the following day (11th) and the day after that (12th), but not beyond the 12th. The Urdu commentary provides the reasoning: the sacrifice (qurbani) is prescribed for three days (10th, 11th, 12th), and since Eid al-Adha is linked to sacrifice, the prayer can be delayed within these three days. If the excuse persists, the prayer is not performed after the 12th. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school and emphasizes the time-bound nature of Eid prayer.

Key Terms
عذر (udhr): An excuse that prevents performance of the Eid prayer on its original day
الصلوة يوم الاضحى (al-salat yawm al-adha): The Eid al-Adha prayer performed on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah
من الغد (min al-ghad): The following day after the original day of Eid

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only one day
B) Two days (11th and 12th)
C) Three days (11th, 12th, 13th)
D) It cannot be delayed at all

Key Takeaway
The Eid al-Adha prayer, if missed due to excuse, must be performed on the 11th or 12th of Dhul Hijjah, not beyond, because its time is linked to the sacrifice days.

Wording of Takbir al-Tashriq after Obligatory Prayers
Ruling stating the specific phrasing of Takbir al-Tashriq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact wording of Takbir al-Tashriq and identify when it is recited.

Core Idea
Takbir al-Tashriq is recited audibly after each fard prayer from 9th to 13th Dhul Hijjah.

Takbir al-Tashriq is a specific form of exaltation of Allah recited during the days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah) and on the day of 'Arafah (9th) and the day of Nahr (10th). The Hanafi school prescribes a particular wording that must be memorized and recited audibly after every obligatory prayer. This lesson will help you internalize the exact phrase and understand its context.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the phrase components
Break the takbir into four parts: (1) Allahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar; (2) La ilaha illa Allah; (3) Wallahu Akbar, Allahu Akbar; (4) Wa lillahi al-hamd. Repeat and commit to memory.
The phrase contains two pairs of 'Allahu Akbar' separated by the tahlil.
2
Identify the times of recitation
The takbir is recited after every fard prayer (obligatory prayer) from the Fajr of the 9th of Dhul Hijjah (Day of 'Arafah) until the 'Asr of the 13th of Dhul Hijjah (last day of Tashriq).
For Hanafis, it is wajib for men to recite audibly; women recite silently.
3
Recognize the legal ruling
In the Hanafi school, reciting Takbir al-Tashriq is wajib (obligatory) after each fard prayer during the specified days. This is based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as recorded in hadith.
Other schools may consider it sunnah, but Hanafis emphasize its obligatory nature due to the evidence.
4
Understand the evidence
The Urdu commentary at the end of the text mentions that the proof is the hadith in issue no. 19, where the Prophet would say the takbir after finishing obligatory prayers (as narrated in Dar Qutni).
This hadith establishes the timing and the practice.

Commentary
This passage specifies the exact wording of Takbir al-Tashriq to be recited after each obligatory prayer during the days of Tashriq. The phrase consists of: 'Allahu Akbar' twice, then 'La ilaha illa Allah', then 'Allahu Akbar' twice, then 'Wa lillahi al-hamd'. The Urdu commentary notes that the evidence for this practice is the hadith presented in the previous issue (19) which mentions that the Prophet would say takbir after finishing the obligatory prayers. This wording is the established formula in the Hanafi school and is to be recited audibly by men after each fard prayer from the 9th to the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms

عقيب الصلوات المفروضات (uqayb al-salawat al-mafrudat): Immediately after the obligatory prayers (fard prayers).

The Hanafi Ruling on Solar Eclipse Prayer (Salat al-Kusuf)
Ruling with proof: sunnah eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on solar eclipse prayer and identify the hadith proofs that support one ruku per rak'ah.

Core Idea
Solar eclipse prayer is sunnah with one ruku per rak'ah, as proven by the Prophet's practice.

The solar eclipse is a sign of Allah's power, and the Prophet taught us to respond with prayer. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that the eclipse prayer is sunnah (recommended) and consists of two rak'ahs with one bowing each, like regular nafl. We will look at three hadiths that establish this ruling and contrast it with the Shafi'i view of two rukus per rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the opening sentence of the passage. State clearly: when a solar eclipse occurs, what does the Imam do? Note the number of rak'ahs and rukus.
The text says 'two rak'ahs in the manner of supererogatory prayer, with one ruku in each rak'ah'.
2
Understand the Legal Category
The passage explicitly calls this prayer 'sunnah' (non-obligatory). Explain why it is not fard or wajib based on the evidence.
The command 'sallu' in the hadith is interpreted as recommendation, not obligation, due to other contextual evidence.
3
Analyze the First Hadith Proof
Read the hadith from Abu Bakrah. What action did the Prophet perform? What was his command? How does this prove the ruling?
The Prophet prayed two rak'ahs and said 'pray and supplicate until it is cleared' – indicating the prayer is recommended.
4
Examine the Second and Third Hadiths
The second hadith from Qabisah emphasizes praying like the most recent obligatory prayer (interpreted as Fajr). The third from Samurah mentions long standing and bowing without two rukus. How do these support the Hanafi position?
The absence of two rukus in all these narrations is key to the Hanafi argument.
5
Contrast with the Opposing View
The passage implicitly contrasts with the Shafi'i view of two rukus per rak'ah. Summarize the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) between the two schools.
The Shafi'i school relies on other hadiths that mention two rukus; the Hanafi school considers those weak or misinterpreted.

حاشیہ : (الف) ابی بکرۃ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم حضور کے پاس تھے کہ سورج گرہن ہوا۔ تو حضور اپنی چادر کھینچتے ہوئے کھڑے ہوئے ۔ یہاں تک کہ مسجد میں داخل ہوئے تو ہم لوگ بھی داخل ہوئے تو ہمیں آپ نے دو رکعت نماز پڑھائی۔ یہاں تک کہ سورج کھل گیا۔ پھر آپ نے فرمایا کہ سورج اور چاند کسی کے مرنے سے گرہن نہیں ہوتے ۔ اور جب کہ تم ایسی حالت دیکھو تو نماز پڑھو اور دعا کرو یہاں تک کہ کھل جائے جو ہو رہا ہے (ب ) قبیصہ، ہلالی فرماتے ہیں کہ حضور کے زمانے میں سورج گرہن ہوا تو آپ گھبرا کر نکلے کپڑا کھینچتے ہوئے اور میں آپ کے ساتھ اس دن مدینہ میں تھا۔ تو دورکعت نماز پڑھائی اور ان دونوں میں لمبا قیام کیا۔ پھر واپس لوٹے اور سورج کھل گیا۔ پھر فرمایا یہ نشانیاں ہیں، اللہ عزوجل اس سے ڈراتے ہیں۔ پس جب اس کو دیکھو تو نماز پڑھو جیسی فرض نماز پڑھ چکے ہو یعنی فجر کی نماز کی طرح۔
Chapter of Eclipse Prayer. (1) When the sun eclipses, the Imam leads the people in two rak'ahs in the manner of supererogatory prayer (nafl), with one bowing (ruku) in each rak'ah. Essential note: Solar eclipse is called 'Kusuf'. At that time, prayer is recommended (sunnah). Its evidence is the hadith from Abu Bakrah who said: We were with the Prophet (peace be upon him) when the sun eclipsed, so the Messenger of Allah stood dragging his cloak until he entered the mosque, and we entered, so he led us in two rak'ahs until the sun became clear. Then the Prophet said: 'The sun and the moon are not eclipsed due to anyone's death. So when you see them, pray and supplicate until what has happened to you is removed.' (Bukhari, Bab al-Salat fi Kusuf al-Shams, no. 1040; Abu Dawud, no. 1185). From this hadith it is known that prayer is to be performed during solar eclipse. (1) When the sun eclipses, the Imam will lead the people in two rak'ahs like nafl, with one ruku in each rak'ah. The Imam will pray with congregation, and just as one performs general nafl with one ruku in each rak'ah and recites quietly, similarly the eclipse prayer will be performed. The above hadith mentions two rak'ahs but did not mention two rukus, so two rukus will not be performed in one rak'ah. (2) From Qabisah al-Hilali: He said the sun eclipsed during the time of the Messenger of Allah, so he came out alarmed, dragging his garment, and I was with him that day in Madinah. He prayed two rak'ahs and made the standing long, then departed and the sun became clear. He said: 'These are signs by which Allah frightens His servants. So when you see them, pray as you would pray the most recent obligatory prayer.' (Abu Dawud, no. 1185; Ibn Majah, no. 633). In this hadith, it is that just as in Fajr prayer one prays with one ruku, similarly the solar eclipse prayer will be performed. 'Ahadath salatin min al-maktubah' refers to Fajr prayer. Also, this hadith does not mention performing ruku twice. (3) The long hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub includes a portion: 'He prayed, and he led us in standing as long as he ever led us in any prayer, we did not hear any sound from him, then he bowed with us as long as he ever bowed with us in any prayer, we did not hear any sound from him, then he prostrated with us...' Footnote: (a) Abu Bakrah says: We were with the Prophet (peace be upon him) when the sun eclipsed, so the Prophet stood dragging his cloak until he entered the mosque, so we entered, and he led us in two rak'ahs until the sun became clear. Then he said that the sun and moon do not eclipse due to anyone's death, and when you see such a state, pray and supplicate until it clears. (b) Qabisah al-Hilali says: During the time of the Prophet, the sun eclipsed, so he came out alarmed, dragging his garment, and I was with him that day in Madinah. He led two rak'ahs and made the standing long in both, then returned and the sun cleared. Then he said: These are signs by which Allah frightens, so when you see them, pray as you would pray the most recent obligatory prayer, i.e., like Fajr prayer.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the Solar Eclipse Prayer (Salat al-Kusuf). The author begins by stating the ruling: when a solar eclipse occurs, the Imam leads the people in two rak'ahs in the manner of nafl prayer, with one ruku in each rak'ah. The commentary clarifies that the eclipse prayer is sunnah (recommended, not obligatory) and provides three hadith proofs. The first hadith from Abu Bakrah confirms the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs during an eclipse and instructed to pray and supplicate until the eclipse ends. The second hadith from Qabisah al-Hilali emphasizes praying like the most recent obligatory prayer, which the author interprets as Fajr (since that is the last obligatory prayer before the eclipse occurred). The third hadith from Samurah ibn Jundub describes the Prophet's lengthy standing and bowing without mentioning two rukus. The author uses these proofs to establish that the Hanafi position is to pray two rak'ahs with one ruku each, like regular nafl, and not like the Shafi'i opinion of two rukus per rak'ah. The prayer is performed quietly and in congregation, similar to other sunnah prayers.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): A solar eclipse; the darkening of the sun.
نافلة (naflah): Supererogatory (voluntary) prayer, as opposed to obligatory (fard).
سنة (sunnah): Recommended practice established by the Prophet; not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two rukus

D) Four rukus

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Salat al-Kusuf is a sunnah prayer of two rak'ahs with one ruku each, performed in congregation with silent recitation, based on the authentic practice of the Prophet.
