intermediate
6 min
Solar Eclipse Prayer: One Ruku' per Rak'ah in Hanafi School
Establishes the Hanafi ruling and defends against Shafi'i view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on solar eclipse prayer, identify the key hadith evidence, and explain why the Hanafi school rejects the Shafi'i position of two ruku's per rak'ah.

Core Idea
In solar eclipse prayer, the Hanafi school follows one ruku' per rak'ah, as supported by multiple hadiths, while the Shafi'i school requires two ruku's, based on a different interpretation of the Aisha hadith.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on salat al-kusuf (solar eclipse prayer). The Hanafi school holds that it consists of two rak'ahs with one ruku' each, similar to nafl prayer. However, Imam al-Shafi'i maintains that each rak'ah should have two ruku's. Understanding the evidence and reasoning behind each position will clarify why the Hanafi view is considered stronger.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal status
Recognize that solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf) is a sunnah muakkadah, as performed by the Prophet (peace be upon him) without being commanded as an obligation.
The Hanafi position is that it is sunnah, not fard.
2
State the Hanafi ruling on the format
The imam leads two rak'ahs, each with one ruku', with quiet recitation, exactly like the regular nafl prayer.
This is the mufta bihi position with no intra-Hanafi dispute.
3
Examine the Hanafi evidence
Three hadiths are cited: (1) Abu Bakrah, (2) Qabisah, (3) Samurah ibn Jundub. All describe two rak'ahs without mentioning multiple bowings, implying the default of one ruku' per rak'ah.
The hadiths are from Bukhari and Abu Dawud, considered authentic (zanni thubut).
4
Understand the Shafi'i objection and its evidence
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith of Aisha, which describes the Prophet performing two ruku's in one rak'ah during the eclipse prayer.
This is the primary basis for the Shafi'i ruling of two ruku's per rak'ah.
5
Analyse the Hanafi response and tarjih
The Hanafi response interprets Aisha's hadith as describing two rak'ahs each with a long ruku', not two ruku's in one rak'ah. The majority of hadiths (three vs. one) support the single ruku' format, making the Hanafi position stronger.
If someone performs two ruku's in one rak'ah, the prayer is still valid (sahih), but the sunnah is to follow the Hanafi format.

باب صلوة الكسوف ) ضروری نوٹ سورج گرہن کو کسوف کہتے ہیں۔ اس وقت نماز سنت ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابی بکرۃ قال كنا عند النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم فانكسفت الشمس فقام رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يجر رداءه حتى دخل المسجد فدخلنا فصلى بنا ركعتين حتى انجلت الشمس فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ان الشمس والقمر لا ينكسفان لموت احد فاذا رأيتموها فصلوا وادعوا حتى ينكشف ما بكم (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الصلوۃ فی کسوف الشمس ص ۱۴۱ ابواب الکسوف نمبر ۱۰۴۰ را بود او د شریف، باب من قال اربع رکعات ص ۱۷۵ نمبر ۱۱۸۵ ، اس باب کی آخری حدیث ہے ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورج گرہن کے وقت نماز پڑھنی چاہئے۔
[۳۸۶] (۱) جب سورج گرہن ہو جائے تو امام لوگوں کو دورکعت نماز پڑھائے گانفل کی طرح ہر رکعت میں ایک رکوع۔ سورج گرہن ہو جائے تو امام جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھائے گا۔ اور جس طرح عام نفل پڑھتے ہیں کہ ہر ایک رکعت میں ایک رکوع کرتے ہیں اور قرآت آہستہ کرتے ہیں۔ اسی طرح نماز کسوف بھی پڑھائیں گے۔ اوپر کی حدیث میں تھا کہ دو رکعت نماز پڑھائے گا۔ اور اس میں دو رکوع کا ذکر نہیں تھا اس لئے ایک رکعت میں دو رکوع نہیں کریں گے (۲) عن قبيصة الهلالى قال كسفت الشمس على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فخرج فزعا يجر ثوبه وانا معه يومئذ بالمدينة فصلى ركعتين فاطال فيهما القيام ثم انصرف وانجلت فقال انما هذه الآيات يخوف الله عز و جل بها فاذا رأيتموها فصلو اكاحدث صلوة صليتموها من المكتوبة (ب) ( ابو داؤد شریف ، باب من قال اربع رکعات ص ۷۵ انمبر ۱۱۸۵ رسن الله تی باب من صلى في الخسوف ركعتين ج ثالث ص ۴۶۴، نمبر ۶۳۳) اس (۳) سمرة بن جندب کی لمبی حدیث ہے۔ جس کا ٹکڑا اس طرح ہے فصلى فقام بنا كاطول ما قام بنا في صلوة قط لا نسمع له صوتا قال ثم ركع بنا كاطول ما ركع بنا في صلوة قط لا نسمع له صوتا قال ثم سجد بنا كاطول ما سجد بنا في صلوة قط لا نسمع له صوتا ثم فعل في الركعة الأخرى مثل ذلک (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب من قال اربع رکعات ص ۱۷۵ نمبر ۱۱۸۴) اس حدیث میں بھی اس بات کا تذکرہ ہے کہ ایک رکعت میں دور کوع نہیں کئے ۔ جس سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ سورج گرہن کی نماز میں ایک رکعت میں دور کوع نہیں کریں گے۔ بلکہ ایک رکوع ہی کیا جائے گا (۴) صرف یہی ایک نماز ہے جس میں دور کوع کا تذکرہ ہے باقی نمازوں میں ایک رکوع ہے۔ اس لئے امام ابو حنیفہ اس طرف گئے ہیں جس میں ایک رکوع کا تذکرہ ہے۔ البتہ کوئی دور کوع کرے گا تو نماز فاسد نہیں ہوگی بلکہ نماز صحیح ہوگی۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ سورج گرہن کی ہر رکعت میں دور کو ع ہوں۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے ان عائشة زوج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اخبرته ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم صلى يوم خسفت الشمس فقام فكبر فقرأ قراءة طويلة ثم ركع ركوعا طويلا ثم رفع رأسه فقال سمع الله لمن حمده وقام كما هو ثم قرأ قراءة طويلة وهى ادنى من القراءة الاولى ثم ركع ركوعا طويلا وهى ادنى من الركعة الأولى ثم سجد سجودا طويلا ثم فعل في الركعة الآخرة مثل ذلك ثم سلم وقد تجلت الشمس (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب هل يقول كسفت الشمس او حسفت ص ۱۴۲ نمبر ۱۰۴۷ر مسلم شریف ، کتاب الکسوف ص ۲۹۵ نمبر ( ۹۰ ) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ ہر رکعت میں دور کوع ہوں ۔
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Eclipse Prayer. (1386) (1) When the sun eclipses, the imam leads the people in two rak'ahs in the manner of supererogatory prayer, with one bowing in each rak'ah. [Then Urdu explanation: Solar eclipse is called kusuf. Prayer at this time is sunnah. Its evidence is the hadith of Abu Bakrah...] (Then after quoting hadiths, the text says:) Imam Shafi'i says that in solar eclipse prayer there are two bowings in each rak'ah. Their evidence is the hadith of Aisha...
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf). The author first states the ruling: when a solar eclipse occurs, the imam leads the congregation in two rak'ahs, each with one ruku', similar to nafl prayer. The Urdu commentary explains that this prayer is sunnah, not fard. Three hadiths are cited to support the single ruku' format: (1) Hadith of Abu Bakrah, where the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs without specifying multiple bowings; (2) Hadith of Qabisah, where the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs and described it as 'like the most recent obligatory prayer you performed' (interpreted as Fajr, which has one ruku' per rak'ah); (3) Hadith of Samurah ibn Jundub, which describes long standing, bowing, and prostration but only one bowing per rak'ah. The commentary then addresses the Shafi'i position: Imam Shafi'i holds that each rak'ah should have two ruku's, citing the hadith of Aisha. The Hanafi response is that the majority of hadiths (including those cited) show only one ruku', and the Aisha hadith is interpreted as describing two rak'ahs each with a long ruku', not two ruku's in one rak'ah. The Hanafi school follows the clearer evidence. Importantly, if someone performs two ruku's in one rak'ah, the prayer is still valid (sahih), not invalidated. The passage thus establishes the Hanafi ruling and defends it against the Shafi'i view.

Key Terms
كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse, a natural phenomenon during which a specific sunnah prayer is performed.
نافلة (nafilah): Supererogatory (voluntary) prayer, upon which the eclipse prayer is modeled in form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many ruku's are performed in each rak'ah of solar eclipse prayer?
A) One ruku'
B) Two ruku's
C) Three ruku's
D) Four ruku's

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that solar eclipse prayer consists of two rak'ahs with one ruku' each, and performing an extra ruku' does not invalidate the prayer.

Recitation in Solar Eclipse Prayer: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Volume
Resolves intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation volume

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Abu Hanifa's position on recitation volume in eclipse prayer and evaluate the Sahibayn's counter-evidence.

Core Idea
Quiet recitation in eclipse prayer is the relied-upon Hanafi position, supported by hadith evidence.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the volume of recitation in solar eclipse prayer. The matn records that Abu Hanifa required quiet recitation (ikhfa'), while his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), held that recitation should be loud (jahr). The accompanying Urdu commentary provides the hadith proofs for Abu Hanifa's view. Understanding this ikhtilaf is essential for knowing the operative ruling (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school and for appreciating how the school handles internal differences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling on recitation volume in eclipse prayer. He says ikhfa' (quiet).
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold jahr (loud) recitation.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf recorded in the Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Analyze the hadith of Samurah (لا نسمع له صوتا) and the hadith of Aisha (estimated recitation). How do they indicate quiet recitation?
The phrase 'we did not hear his voice' during standing, bowing, and prostration directly supports silent recitation.
4
Consider the Sahibayn's probable proof
Although not detailed in the text, the Sahibayn likely analogize eclipse prayer to other congregational prayers (like Jumu'ah) where loud recitation is sunnah.
Their proof is based on qiyas, which Abu Hanifa's direct hadith evidence overrides.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Establish that the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's quiet recitation.
Later texts (e.g., al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya) adopt this view, though the Sahibayn's opinion is also preserved.

Source Text

۳۸۷(۲) ويطول القراءة فيهما ويخفى عند ابي حنيفة وقال ابو يوسف و محمد يجهر بهما (۱) مسئلہ نمبر ایک میں ابو داؤد شریف کی حدیث گزری جس میں یہ الفاظ تھے فقام بنا كاطول ماقام بنا في صلوة قط لا نسمع له صوتا (ج) ( ابو داؤد شریف، باب من قال اربع رکعات ص ۷۵ انمبر ۱۱۸۴) اس حدیث میں راوی فرماتے ہیں کہ قیام کی حالت میں بھی آپ کی آواز ہم نہیں سنتے تھے ۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ آپ قرآت سری کر رہے تھے (۲) اس ابو داؤد شریف کی دوسری حدیث ہے عن عائشة قالت كسفت الشمس على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فخرج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فصلى بالناس فقام فحزرت قرأته فرأيت انه قرأ سورة البقرة (د) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب القراءة في صلوة الكسوف ص ۱۷۵ نمبر۷ ۱۱۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ میں نے انداز لگایا کہ آپ کی قرآت سورہ بقرہ اتنی لمبی تھی۔ اندازہ لگانے کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ آپ نے قرآت زور سے نہیں کی۔ ورنہ تو صاف کہتے کہ (ج) پس آپ نے نماز پڑھائی تو ہم کو اتنی لمبی دیر تک لیکر کھڑے ہوئے کہ کبھی بھی اتنی دیر تک لیکر کھڑے نہیں ہوئے۔ آپ کی کوئی آواز ہم نہیں سنتے تھے۔ پھر ہم کو اتالمبارکوع کر وایا کہ کسی نماز میں اتنا لمبار کوع نہیں کروایا ۔ ہم آپ کی کوئی آواز نہیں سنتے تھے۔ فرمایا پھر ہم کو اتنا لمبا سجدہ کروایا کہ اتنا لمبا سجدہ کسی نماز میں کبھی نہیں کروایا۔ ہم آپ کی کوئی آواز نہیں سنتے تھے۔ پھر دوسری رکعت میں ایسا ہی کیا (ب) آپ نے نماز پڑھی اس دن جب سورج گرہن ہوا۔ پس کھڑے ہوئے اور تکبیر کہی اور لیبی قرآت کی، پھر لمبارکوع کیا، پھر سر اٹھایا پھر کہا مع الله من حمدہ پھر کھڑے ہوئے جیسے تھے پھر بھی قرآت کی وہ پہلی قرآت سے کم تھی پھر لمبا رکوع کیا وہ پہلے رکوع سے کم تھا پھر لمبا سجدہ کیا پھر دوسری رکعت میں بھی ایسا ہی کیا پھر سلام پھیرا اور سورج کھل چکا تھا (ج) ہم کو بہت لمبی دیر تک لیکر کھڑے ہوئے کسی بھی نماز میں اتنی دیر تک لیکر کھڑے نہیں ہوئے ۔ ہم آپ کی آواز نہیں سن رہے تھے (د) حضرت عائشہ نے فرمایا سورج حضور کے زمانے میں گرہن ہوا تو حضور نکلے اور لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائی ، پس کھڑے ہوئے تو میں نے آپ کی قرآت کا انداز ولگا یا تو دیکھا کہ آپ نے سورہ بقرہ کے مطابق پڑھی ہے۔
(1387) (2) He prolongs the recitation in both (rak'ahs) and makes it quiet according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He recites aloud in both. [Then Urdu commentary cites hadiths: (1) Hadith of Samurah stating 'we did not hear his voice' indicating quiet recitation; (2) Hadith of Aisha estimating he recited Surah al-Baqarah, implying quiet recitation because she estimated rather than heard clearly.]
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage addresses the volume of recitation in solar eclipse prayer. The matn states: The recitation is prolonged and made quiet (ikhfa') according to Imam Abu Hanifa, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say it should be recited aloud (jahr). The Urdu commentary provides the evidence for Abu Hanifa's position: The hadith of Samurah (previously cited) mentions that during the prayer, they did not hear the Prophet's voice, indicating silent recitation. Also, the hadith of Aisha (رضي الله عنها) reports that she estimated his recitation as Surah al-Baqarah; the fact that she estimated (rather than clearly heard) suggests he recited quietly. The Sahibayn's argument for loud recitation is not detailed here, but their position is based on analogy with other congregational prayers or other evidence. The commentary ends with the hadith of Aisha being quoted. The intra-Hanafi difference is recorded, but the text does not explicitly state which is the mufta bihi position. However, in the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is often that of Abu Hanifa for silent recitation in eclipse prayer, but the Sahibayn's view is also recognized. This passage presents the ikhtilaf and the proofs for Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
يخفى (yukhfi): Recite quietly, with only the reciter hearing himself.
يجهر (yajhar): Recite aloud, making the recitation audible to others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Consensus of the companions
B) The hadith of Samurah (لا نسمع له صوتا) and Aisha's estimation
C) Analogy to Jumu'ah prayer
D) A verse from the Quran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi for recitation in solar eclipse prayer is quiet (ikhfa'), based on the hadith evidence that the Prophet recited quietly.

Loud Recitation in Solar Eclipse Prayer: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on jahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi relied-upon ruling on recitation in solar eclipse prayer and explain the evidence and tarjih (preference) between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
In eclipse prayer, loud recitation is sunnah, not silent, based on Aisha's hadith.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether the recitation in salat al-kusuf (solar eclipse prayer) should be loud (jahr) or silent (sirr). Abu Hanifa held that it should be silent, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), argued for loud recitation. The later Hanafi position has adopted the view of the Sahibayn, making loud recitation the sunnah. Understanding how this tarjih is reached will sharpen your ability to weigh conflicting evidence within a madhhab.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling from the text: loud recitation (jahr) is sunnah in solar eclipse prayer.
2
Identify the opposing view within the madhhab
Abu Hanifa held that the recitation should be silent (sirr), based on the Prophet reciting Surah Al-Baqarah in the eclipse prayer (implying a long recitation that would be burdensome if read aloud).
3
Follow the proof of the Sahibayn
The Sahibayn's evidence is the hadith of Aisha: 'The Prophet recited loudly in salat al-khusuf.' This is an explicit textual proof (dalil) for loud recitation.
The hadith is classified as ahad (zanni al-thubut) but is considered strong.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The commentary prefers the Sahibayn's evidence because the explicit hadith takes precedence over the inference from the long surah recitation. The long recitation does not necessarily imply silence; it could have been recited loudly but the narration does not specify.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference (thamarah) is that in actual practice, worshippers recite loudly in solar eclipse prayer, following the sunnah. Reciting silently would be valid but would miss the sunnah reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجهر ۱۳۸۸ (۳) آپ نے سورہ بقرہ پڑھی۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ صلوۃ کسوف میں قرآت سری تھی۔ اننده صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ قرآت زور سے پڑھی جائے گی۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة قـالـت جهر النبي الله في صلوة الخسوف بـقـراء تـه (بخاری شریف، باب النهر بالقراءة فی الکسوف ص ۴۵ انمبر ۱۰۶۵ رابوداؤد شریف، باب القراءة في صلوة الكسوف ص ۱۷۵ نمبر ۱۱۸۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ نے قرآت جہری کی تھی۔ اس لئے سورج گرہن کی نماز میں جہری قرآت سنت ہے۔
He recites loudly. 1388 (3) You recited Surah Al-Baqarah. From this it is known that in salat al-kusuf the recitation was silent. Then the Sahibayn say that recitation should be loud. Their proof is this hadith: from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) recited loudly in salat al-khusuf in his recitation. From this hadith it is known that he recited loudly. Therefore, loud recitation in solar eclipse prayer is sunnah.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recitation in solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf). The base text (matn) initially states 'يجهر' (he recites loudly), but then the commentary attributes to Abu Hanifa a view that the recitation is silent (sirr), citing the Prophet's recitation of Surah Al-Baqarah as evidence. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that recitation should be loud (jahr), supporting their view with a hadith from Aisha (ra) that the Prophet recited loudly in the eclipse prayer. The commentary then resolves that the hadith is stronger, and thus the sunnah (recommended practice) is loud recitation. This is an example of the later Hanafi position (mufta bihi) following the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation in prayer, audible to others.
سري (sirr): Silent recitation, moving the lips but not audible.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Silent recitation (sirr) is wajib.
B) Loud recitation (jahr) is sunnah.
C) No recitation is required.
D) Loud recitation is wajib.

Key Takeaway
In eclipse prayer, loud recitation is sunnah based on the hadith of Aisha, and this is the mufta bihi position.

Supplication after Eclipse Prayer
Ruling on supplication until the eclipse clears

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supplication after the eclipse prayer and identify the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
After eclipse prayer, supplicate until the eclipse clears — the prayer is not repeated.

This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling that after performing the eclipse prayer, one should continue making du'a until the phenomenon ends. The proof is a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructing prayer and supplication during the eclipse. Understanding this distinguishes the recommended act from the prayer itself, ensuring correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
The act in question is supplication (du'a) after the eclipse prayer, performed while the eclipse continues.
2
State the Hukm Level
In the Hanafi school, this du'a is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended) — not fard or wajib.
The ruling is based on its being commanded in a hadith of ahad status.
3
Locate the Dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Abu Hurairah (ra) in Sahih al-Bukhari: 'Pray and supplicate until what has befallen you is removed.'
Reference: Sahih al-Bukhari, Bab al-Salat fi Khusuf al-Qamar, hadith 1063.
4
Extract the Wajh al-Dalalah
The command 'sallu wa ud'u' (pray and supplicate) indicates that after the prayer, supplication continues until the eclipse ends. The imperative form implies recommendation (nadb) given the context of a natural phenomenon.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-nadb unless qarinah indicates wujub.

Commentary
This passage begins with the ruling that after the eclipse prayer, one should continue supplicating until the eclipse clears. The proof is a hadith from Abu Huraira (not fully quoted in the OCR but referenced) where the Prophet said: 'Pray and supplicate until what has befallen you is removed.' The commentary explains that if the prayer is long but the eclipse persists, one should persist in supplication. This is a ruling with proof from the Sunnah.

كسوف (kusuf): Solar eclipse; the darkening of the sun.
خسوف (khusuf): Lunar eclipse; the darkening of the moon.

Who Leads the Eclipse Prayer?
Ruling on leadership of eclipse prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who leads the eclipse prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the reasoning behind the preference.

Core Idea
The Friday imam leads the eclipse prayer; if absent, pray individually to avoid disorganization.

This passage from al-Sharh al-Saghir specifies the person who should lead the special prayer for a solar eclipse. The Hanafi school, known for its emphasis on order, designates the Friday imam as the leader and discourages multiple congregations. Understanding this ruling helps you appreciate how the school prioritizes community harmony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act under discussion is the solar eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf). The ruling is that it is sunnah to perform it in congregation led by the Friday imam.
2
Note the designated leader
The text specifies that the imam who leads Friday prayer should lead. This is a specific imam, not any qualified person.
Hanafis distinguish between the regular imam (imam ratib) and temporary imams.
3
Understand the condition for congregation
The condition for holding congregation is the presence of that Friday imam. If he is absent, no congregation is formed.
The alternative is individual prayer.
4
Explore the wisdom
The Hanafi school aims to avoid fitna (disorganization) that could arise if multiple imams lead separate groups.
This reflects the principle of sadd al-dhara'i (blocking means to evil).
5
Apply to a scenario
If you are in a city with multiple mosques, each mosque's Friday imam leads his own congregation; if a mosque's Friday imam is absent, its members pray individually.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴) ويصلي بالناس الامام الذى يصلى بهم الجمعة فان لم يحضر الامام صليها الناس فرادی
(4) And the imam who leads them in Friday prayer leads the people; if the imam is not present, the people pray it individually.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This is a ruling statement specifying that the eclipse prayer should be led by the same imam who leads the Friday prayer. The commentary advises that if that imam is absent, congregational prayer should not be held; rather, each person prays individually to avoid fitna (chaos). This follows the Hanafi principle of avoiding disorder in rituals.

Key Terms
امام (imam): The leader of congregational prayer.
فتنة (fitna): Disorder, chaos, or trial; the Hanafi school aims to avoid it in ritual matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Friday imam leads the eclipse prayer; if absent, pray individually.

No Congregation in Lunar Eclipse Prayer
Ruling that lunar eclipse prayer is performed individually

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for lunar eclipse prayer, distinguish it from solar eclipse prayer, and apply the dalil to justify individual performance.

Core Idea
Lunar eclipse prayer is performed individually; congregation would cause fitna at night.

This lesson clarifies a distinct ruling within the Hanafi school regarding lunar eclipse prayer. Unlike the solar eclipse prayer (Salat al-Kusuf), which is performed in congregation, the lunar eclipse prayer (Salat al-Khusuf) is offered individually. The ruling is based on preventing hardship and chaos (fitna) that could arise from gathering at night during an eclipse. We will examine the text, its proof, and the reasoning behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? (lunar eclipse prayer) What is the hukm level? (sunnah ghayr muakkadah) What is the specific ruling? (no congregation, each prays alone)
The ruling is found in the matn: 'There is no congregation in lunar eclipse; rather each person prays by himself.'
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The hadith: 'When you see such signs, pray and supplicate.' This is a general command without specification of congregation.
The dalil is from Sahih al-Bukhari, hadith 1063 (referenced in the previous lesson).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this dalil prove the ruling? The command is general (amm) and does not explicitly order congregation. The Hanafi school interprets the absence of specific congregational command as allowing individual prayer, especially given the context of nighttime eclipse.
The school applies the principle that a general command does not require a specific modality unless proven.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Yes, some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow congregation for lunar eclipse. The Hanafi position distinguishes between solar (congregation) and lunar (individual) based on practical considerations.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
What is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi)? Individual prayer without congregation. The rationale is avoiding fitna and hardship during nighttime gathering.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵) وليس في خسوف القمر جماعة وانما يصلى كل واحد بنفسه [۳۹۱] (٦) وليس في الكسوف خطبة.
(5) There is no congregation in lunar eclipse; rather each person prays by himself. (6) There is no khutbah in eclipse.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This ruling states that the lunar eclipse prayer (salat al-khusuf) should not be performed in congregation. The commentary explains that since lunar eclipses occur at night, congregating would cause difficulty and chaos (fitna). Therefore, each individual prays alone at home. The proof is the general command in the hadith: 'When you see such signs, pray and supplicate,' which does not specifically command congregation. This is a distinct ruling from the solar eclipse prayer, which is performed in congregation.

Key Terms
خسوف (khusuf): Lunar eclipse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) In congregation with loud recitation.
B) Individually, not in congregation.
C) In congregation with silent recitation.
D) It is not prayed at all.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that lunar eclipse prayer is performed individually, distinguishing it from solar eclipse prayer, to avoid fitna at night.

No Khutbah in Eclipse Prayer
Ruling that eclipse prayer does not have a prescribed khutbah, with evidence from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that eclipse prayer does not require a formal khutbah and explain the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
Eclipse prayer requires no formal sermon — the Prophet's khutbah was exceptional, not prescriptive.

In this lesson, we examine a key distinction between eclipse prayer and other congregational prayers. While Friday and Eid prayers require a formal khutbah, the eclipse prayer does not. The passage clarifies that the Prophet's khutbah was a one-time correction of a false belief, not a routine component.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State clearly whether a khutbah is required for eclipse prayer according to the Hanafi school.
The ruling is that no formal khutbah is required.
2
Examine the dalil
Look at the hadith evidence cited: the commands to pray and supplicate, not to deliver a sermon.
The primary hadith is: 'When you see that, pray and supplicate until it clears.'
3
Understand the context
Why did the Prophet give a khutbah on that specific occasion? The narrator explains it was to correct the misconception that eclipses occur due to someone's death.
The Prophet's son Ibrahim died that day, leading people to associate the eclipse with his death.
4
Derive the principle
What distinguishes eclipse prayer from Jumuah and Eid? The primary commanded actions are prayer and supplication, not a sermon.
Thus, the absence of a khutbah does not affect the validity of the prayer.
5
Apply to a scenario
If a mosque leads eclipse prayer without a khutbah, is the prayer valid?
Yes, it is valid. A khutbah is not a condition or pillar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٦) وليس في الكسوف خطبة. حضور نے نماز کسوف کے بعد خطبہ دیا ہے لیکن وہ ایک رسم کو دور کرنے کے لئے تھا کہ لوگ یہ سمجھتے تھے کہ کسی کے مرنے یا زندہ ہونے پر سورج گرہن ہوتا ہے اور اس دن آپ کا صاحبزادہ حضرت ابراہیم کا انتقال ہوا تھا۔ اس لئے آپ نے اس کی نفی کے لئے خطبہ دیا لیکن نماز عید اور نماز جمعہ کی طرح با ضابطہ خطبہ دینا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ خطبہ کے بغیر بھی نماز ہو جائے گی۔ ایسے آیۃ من آیات اللہ کے وقت نماز پڑھنا دعا کرنا اور اپنے گناہوں کا استغفار کرنا اصل ہے۔ اس کی طرف خود راوی اشارہ فرما رہے ہیں عن أبى بكرة ... فقال () ان الشمس والقمر آيتان من آيات الله وانهما لا يخسفان لموت احد واذا كان ذلك فصلوا وادعوا حتى ينكشف ما بكم وذلك ان ابنا للنبي الا الله مات يقال له ابراهيم فقال الناس في ذلك (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الصلوۃ فی کسوف القمر ص ۱۴۵ نمبر ۱۰۶۳) اس حدیث میں نماز کے بعد فقال: سے اخیر تک خطبہ دیا ہے۔ لیکن راوی خود فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ خطبہ اس بنا پر تھا کہ آپ کے صاحبزادے ابراہیم کا اس دن انتقال ہوا تھا۔ اس لئے لوگوں کے اعتقادات کو ختم کرنے کے لئے خطبہ دیا تھا۔ ورنہ اصل تو فصلوا وا دعوا ہے اور دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ فاذا رأيتم شيئا من ذلك فافزعوا إلى ذكر الله ودعائه واستغفاره (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب الذکر فی الکسوف ص ۱۴۵ نمبر ۱۰۵۹) کہ ان آیات کے وقت گھبرا کر اللہ کے ذکر اور استغفار کی طرف جاؤ۔ کبھی لوگوں کو یہ سب مسائل سمجھانے کی ضرورت پڑے تو سمجھا دیں۔ باضابطہ خطبہ ضروری نہیں کہ اس کے بغیر نماز کسوف نہیں ہوگی۔
(6) There is no khutbah in eclipse. The Prophet (peace be upon him) gave a khutbah after the eclipse prayer, but that was to remove a custom: people thought that solar eclipse happens due to someone's death or life, and that day his son Ibrahim had died. So he gave a khutbah to negate that. But it is not necessary to give a formal khutbah like Eid or Friday prayer. The prayer is valid without a khutbah. At such a time of Allah's signs, the essence is to pray, supplicate, and seek forgiveness. The narrator himself indicates this: from Abu Bakra... he said: The sun and moon are two signs of Allah; they do not eclipse for the death of anyone. So when that happens, pray and supplicate until it clears. And this is because a son of the Prophet named Ibrahim died, and people talked about that. In this hadith, after the prayer, from 'he said' to the end, he gave a khutbah. But the narrator himself says that this khutbah was because his son Ibrahim died that day, and he gave the khutbah to remove people's beliefs. Otherwise, the essence is 'pray and supplicate'. And in another hadith: 'When you see something of that, then turn urgently to the remembrance of Allah, supplication, and seeking forgiveness.' Sometimes if there is a need to explain these matters to people, one may explain. A formal khutbah is not required; without it the eclipse prayer is valid.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage definitively states that there is no prescribed khutbah (sermon) for the eclipse prayer, unlike the Eid or Friday prayers. The commentary acknowledges that the Prophet (peace be upon him) did deliver a khutbah after an eclipse prayer, but clarifies that this was a specific occasion to correct the false belief that eclipses occur due to someone's death (since his son Ibrahim died that day). The commentary cites hadiths that emphasize prayer, supplication, and seeking forgiveness during eclipses, not a formal khutbah. Therefore, the ruling is that a khutbah is not required; the prayer is valid without it. This distinguishes the eclipse prayer from other congregational prayers that have associated sermons.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): A formal sermon, typically delivered before Friday prayer or Eid prayer.
استغفار (istighfar): Seeking forgiveness from Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Is a formal khutbah required for the eclipse prayer in the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, it is wajib.
B) No, it is not required; the prayer is valid without it.
C) Yes, but only for lunar eclipse.
D) No, but it is forbidden to give a khutbah.

Key Takeaway
Eclipse prayer does not require a formal khutbah; the Prophet's khutbah was situational, and the prayer is valid without a sermon.

Salat al-Istisqa: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn on Congregational Prayer
Dispute on whether Salat al-Istisqa is sunnah in congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi intra-school dispute on Salat al-Istisqa, identify the proofs of each side, and evaluate the practical difference.

Core Idea
Istisqa can be done with du'a alone (Abu Hanifa) or with a congregational prayer (Sahibayn).

When drought strikes, Muslims seek rain (istisqa). But how? This passage reveals a difference within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa sees no sunnah prayer, while his two main disciples prescribe a congregational prayer. Let's examine the proofs and the practical consequence of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling: there is no sunnah prayer for istisqa in congregation; it is only du'a and istighfar. Note that individual prayer is permissible.
2
Identify the opposing view (Sahibayn)
State the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: the imam should lead two rak'ahs with loud recitation in congregation. This is considered sunnah.
Sahibayn rely on a different hadith.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa cites Quran 71:10-11 (command to seek forgiveness brings rain) and the hadith of Anas ibn Malik where the Prophet made du'a during a Friday khutbah without a separate prayer.
The Quranic verse emphasizes istighfar, not prayer.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn cite the hadith of 'Ubadah ibn Tamim: the Prophet went out, faced the qibla, turned his cloak, and prayed two rak'ahs with loud recitation.
This hadith explicitly mentions a two-rak'ah prayer.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Abu Hanifa, one may simply make du'a without any formal prayer; according to Sahibayn, one should pray two rak'ahs in congregation. The mufta bihi is not settled in this text.
Later Hanafi practice often follows the Sahibayn view due to the strength of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلوة
باب صلوة الاستسقاء
۱۳۹۲ (۱) قال ابو حنيفة ليس فى الاستسقاء صلوة مسنونة بالجماعة فان صلى الناس وحدانا جاز وانما الاستسقاء الدعاء والاستغفار [۳۹۳](۲) وقال ابو يوسف و محمد
باب صلوة الاستقاء كم
ضروری نوٹ استقاء کے معنی ہیں بارش طلب کرنا ، ملک میں قحط سالی ہو جائے اور بارش نہ ہو تو استقاء کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزد یک نماز پڑھنا کوئی ضروری نہیں ہے۔ صرف دعا سے بھی استقاء ہو سکتا ہے اور نماز بھی پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک نماز استسقاء مسنون ہے۔ دونوں کی دلیلیں نیچے آرہی ہیں۔ اس کی دلیل یہ آیت بھی ہے فقلت استغفر وار یکم انہ کان غفاران مرسل السماء عليكم مدراراه (ب) ( آیت * امرا اسورۃ نوح ۱۷) اس آیت میں ہے کہ اپنے اپنے گناہوں سے تو بہ کرو تا کہ اللہ تعالی تم پر خوب بارش برسائے۔ اور چونکہ نماز استسقاء میں اپنے گناہوں سے تو بہ کرنا ہے اس لئے اس آیت سے استقاء ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ [۳۹۲] (۱) امام ابوحنیفہ نے فرمایا استسقاء میں جماعت کے ساتھ نماز مسنون نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر تنہا تنہا نماز پڑھے تو جائز ہے،استسقاء صرف دعا اور استغفار کا نام ہے۔ آپ نے کبھی نماز استسقاء پڑھی ہے اور کبھی صرف جمعہ کے خطبہ کے وقت ہاتھ اٹھا کر دعا کی ہے۔ اس لئے استسقاء دونوں طرح جائز
ہے۔ صرف نماز ہی پڑھنا مسنون نہیں ہے۔
آیت او پر گزری جس میں یہ حکم ہے کہ اپنے گناہوں سے تو بہ اور استغفار کرو تو بارش خوب ہوگی ۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ گناہوں سے تو بہ کر کے بارش مانگنا استقاء ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ استقاء کے لئے جمعہ کے خطبہ کے وقت آپنے ہاتھ اٹھا کر دعا کی ہے۔ اس سے بارش ہوگئی عن انس بن مالک ان رجلا دخل المسجد يوم الجمعة ورسول الله الله قائما يخطب ... فرفع رسول الله يديه قال اللهم اغثنا (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الاستقاء في خطبة الجمعة غير مستقبل القبلة ص ۱۳۸ نمبر ۱۰۱۴ر مسلم شریف، کتاب الاستقاء ص۱۹۳ نمبر ۱۸۹۷/ ابو داؤد شریف، باب رفع الیدین فی الاستقاء ص ۷۳ انمبر ۱۱۷۵، اس باب کی آخری حدیث ہے ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آپ نے اس کے لئے مستقل نماز نہیں پڑھی صرف دعا پر اکتفا کیا۔ اس لئے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک نماز ضروری نہیں ، صرف دعا اور استغفار سے بھی استسقاء ہو جائے گا۔ اور نماز پڑھ لے تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے، کیونکہ وہ بھی حدیث سے ثابت ہے۔
۱۳۹۳ (۲) امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے فرمایا امام دو رکعت نماز پڑھائیں گے۔ اور اس میں قرآت زور سے پڑھیں گے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عباد بن تميم عن عمه قال خرج النبي الله يستسقى فتوجه الى القبلة يدعو وحول .
حاشیہ : (الف) میں نے کہا اپنے رب سے استغفار کرو، وہ بہت معاف کرنے والے ہیں۔ تم پر مسلسل بارش برسائے گا (ج) انس بن مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک آدمی جمعہ کے دن مسجد میں داخل ہوا اور حضور کھڑے خطبہ دے رہے تھے۔ آپ نے ہاتھ اٹھائے اور فرمایا اللهم اغثنا۔
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Salat al-Istisqa. 1392 (1) Abu Hanifa said: There is no sunnah prayer for istisqa in congregation. If people pray individually, it is permissible. Istisqa is only supplication and seeking forgiveness. (2) Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The imam prays two rak'ahs and recites aloud in them. (Urdu commentary follows explaining the views and proofs, including Quran 71:10-11 and hadith from Anas ibn Malik and 'Ubadah ibn Tamim).
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on Salat al-Istisqa. Abu Hanifa holds that there is no sunnah prayer established for seeking rain; rather, the practice is simply du'a and istighfar, as indicated by the Quranic verse commanding istighfar and the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) made du'a during the Friday khutbah without a separate prayer. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) argue that the imam should lead two rak'ahs with loud recitation, citing the hadith of 'Ubadah ibn Tamim where the Prophet went out, faced the qibla, supplicated, turned his cloak, and then prayed two rak'ahs. The text thus shows the difference of opinion within the Hanafi school on this issue, with both sides relying on authentic narrations.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa'): Seeking rain from Allah through supplication and specific rituals.
مسنونة (masnunah): Sunnah, recommended act established by the Prophet's practice.
جماعة (jama'ah): Congregation, prayer led by an imam with followers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the essence of istisqa?
A) A specific two-rak'ah prayer in congregation
B) Supplication and seeking forgiveness
C) Fasting and charity
D) A sermon without prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has a nuanced position on istisqa: du'a alone suffices per Abu Hanifa, but a congregational prayer is sunnah per the Sahibayn—both are valid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Procedure of Salat al-Istisqa: Khutbah, Qibla, Cloak, and Dhimmi Exclusion
Rulings on the prayer, khutbah, facing qibla, turning cloak, and dhimmi exclusion in istisqa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah procedure of istisqa including the prayer, khutbah, facing qibla, turning cloak, and dhimmi exclusion, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The imam prays aloud, delivers a khutbah facing qibla, turns his cloak, and excludes dhimmis — all sunnah from prophetic practice.

This lesson explains the complete procedure of Salat al-Istisqa as recorded in the Hanafi school. It covers the two-rak'ah prayer with loud recitation, the khutbah that is a reminder, the imam's facing of the qibla for du'a, the symbolic turning of the cloak, and the exclusion of dhimmis. These actions are established by authentic hadith and are considered sunnah by the Sahibayn, with an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf regarding the necessity of the prayer itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
Recognize that the prayer, khutbah, facing qibla, and cloak turning are sunnah; dhimmi exclusion is recommended. Each act has a specific ruling within the istisqa context.
The overall hukm for these acts is sunnah, except the prayer which is subject to ikhtilaf.
2
Locate the dalil for each act
For the prayer: hadith from Bukhari and Muslim about the Prophet (ﷺ) praying two rak'ahs aloud. For the khutbah and facing qibla: hadith from Abu Dawud and Darqutni. For turning cloak: hadith from Darqutni. For dhimmi exclusion: based on analogy and wisdom.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa did not consider the prayer itself as sunnah; he viewed it as a general du'a. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held that the prayer is sunnah with this specific procedure. The text follows the Sahibayn's view.
The khutbah, facing qibla, and cloak turning are agreed upon among the Hanafi imams.
4
Understand the wisdom behind the acts
Turning the cloak symbolizes a change from hardship to ease. Excluding dhimmis is because they are not deserving of Allah's mercy in this context, and their presence may hinder acceptance.
These are not superstitions but prophetic symbols.

رحمهما الله تعالى يصلى الامام ركعتين يجهر فيهما بالقرائة [۱۳۹۴ (۳) ثم يخطب ويستقبل القبلة بالدعاء ويقلب الامام ردائه ولا يقلب القوم ارديتهم [۱۳۹۵(۴) ولا يحضر اهل الذمة للاستسقاء.
رداء ه ثـم صـلـى ركعتين يجهر فيهما بالقراءة (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الجهر بالقراءة في الاستسقاء ص ۱۳۹ نمبر ۱۰۲۴ار مسلم شریف، کتاب صلوة الاستقاء ص ۲۹۳ نمبر ۸۹۴/ ابو داؤد شریف ، ابواب صلوۃ الاستقاص اے انمبر (۱۱۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام دو رکعت نماز پڑھائیں گے۔ اور قرآت جہری کریں گے اور چادر کو بھی نیک فالی کے لئے پلیٹیں گے کہ یا اللہ جس طرح چادر پلٹ رہا ہوں اس

May Allah have mercy on them both, the imam prays two rak'ahs and recites aloud. [1394 (3) Then he delivers a khutbah, faces the qibla during supplication, and the imam turns his cloak, but the people do not turn their cloaks. [1395 (4) And dhimmis do not attend for istisqa. (Urdu commentary provides hadith evidence: Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and others, explaining the turning of the cloak as a good omen, that the khutbah is akin to the 'Eid and Jumu'ah khutbah but not identical, and that dhimmis are excluded because they are subject to Allah's wrath.)
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings on Salat al-Istisqa, specifying the procedure. The imam leads two rak'ahs with loud recitation, then delivers a khutbah (similar to 'Eid but not exactly like Jumu'ah), faces the qibla while making du'a, and turns his cloak from right to left or left to right as a symbolic gesture of changing one's state, seeking Allah's mercy. The congregation does not turn their cloaks; only the imam does. Additionally, non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) should not attend, as they are not deserving of Allah's mercy in this context and their presence may hinder the acceptance of the prayer. The proofs are from hadith: the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by 'Aishah and 'Abdullah ibn Zayd, among others.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): Sermon delivered by the imam during istisqa, which is different from the Jumu'ah khutbah in content and style.
رداء (rida'): Cloak or upper garment that the imam turns (from right to left) as a symbolic gesture for change of condition.
ذمة (dhimmah): Non-Muslim citizens living under Muslim protection (ahl al-dhimmah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is identical to the Jumu'ah khutbah.
B) It is a sunnah act of reminder and exhortation.
C) It is wajib and must be performed before the prayer.
D) It is not required at all.

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Istisqa includes specific sunnah acts: two-rak'ah prayer with loud recitation, khutbah, facing qibla in du'a, turning cloak (imam only), and excluding dhimmis — all based on prophetic hadith.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Rules for the Prayer for Rain (Istisqa)
Rulings for istisqa prayer including khutbah, cloak turning, and dhimmis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five imam-specific actions in istisqa, identify the one action the congregation does not do, and explain the ruling on dhimmis with its dalil.

Core Idea
Only the imam turns his cloak in istisqa; dhimmis are excluded from attending.

The prayer for rain (istisqa) is a sunnah prayer with unique etiquettes taught by the Prophet. This passage from the Hanafi text presents the core rulings: the imam leads two rak'ahs with loud recitation, delivers a sermon, faces the qibla, and turns his cloak. The congregation follows the prayer but does not turn their cloaks. Additionally, dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects) are not to attend. By studying this passage, you will understand the detailed sunnah actions and the proof behind them, enabling you to apply or verify this practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the hukm level of the istisqa prayer: it is a sunnah, not fard or wajib. The passage describes the recommended actions of the imam.
The prayer itself is sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school.
2
List the specific actions of the imam
Extract from the text the five actions the imam performs: 1) leads 2 rak'ahs with loud recitation, 2) delivers a sermon (khutbah), 3) faces the qibla during du'a, 4) turns his cloak (rida'), and 5) leads the congregation in prayer.
These actions are proven from the hadith of Aisha (sermon on pulpit) and Abdullah ibn Zaid (turning cloak and facing qibla).
3
Contrast the congregation's actions
Notice the congregation does NOT turn their cloaks. The text explicitly says 'ولا يقلب القوم ارديتهم' (the people do not turn their cloaks). This is a key distinction.
Some scholars hold that the congregation should also turn cloaks, but the Hanafi position restricts it to the imam only.
4
Analyze the proofs
The author cites two hadith. The hadith of Aisha shows the Prophet used a pulpit and said takbir and praise, indicating a sermon. The hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid shows the Prophet faced the qibla and turned his cloak during du'a. Understand how each hadith proves the respective action.
Both hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the ruling is sunnah, not wajib.
5
Understand the ruling on dhimmis
The passage states that dhimmis should not attend istisqa because they are disbelievers and Allah's wrath descends upon them. The wisdom is that the prayer seeks mercy, so the presence of those under divine displeasure is inappropriate.
This ruling is specific to istisqa; in other prayers, dhimmis are not prohibited from entering mosques.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلوة
رحمهما الله تعالى يصلى الامام ركعتين يجهر فيهما بالقرائة [۱۳۹۴ (۳) ثم يخطب ويستقبل القبلة بالدعاء ويقلب الامام ردائه ولا يقلب القوم ارديتهم [۱۳۹۵(۴) ولا يحضر اهل الذمة للاستسقاء.
رداء ه ثـم صـلـى ركعتين يجهر فيهما بالقراءة (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الجهر بالقراءة في الاستسقاء ص ۱۳۹ نمبر ۱۰۲۴ار مسلم شریف، کتاب صلوة الاستقاء ص ۲۹۳ نمبر ۸۹۴/ ابو داؤد شریف ، ابواب صلوۃ الاستقاص اے انمبر (۱۱۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام دو رکعت نماز پڑھائیں گے۔ اور قرآت جہری کریں گے اور چادر کو بھی نیک فالی کے لئے پلیٹیں گے کہ یا اللہ جس طرح چادر پلٹ رہا ہوں اس طرح میری حالت کو بھی پلٹ دے۔ اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ دعا کے وقت قبلہ کی طرف استقبال کرے۔
[۳۹۴] (۳) پھر امام خطبہ دے اور دعا کرتے ہوئے قبلہ کا استقبال کرے اور امام اپنی چادر کو پلٹے اور قوم اپنی اپنی چادر نہ پلیٹے ۔ باقی باتوں کے دلائل گزر گئے۔ خطبہ دینے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عائشة قالت شكا الناس الى رسول الله له فحوط المطر فامر بمنبر فوضع له في المصلى ... فقعد على المنبر فكبر وحمد الله عز وجل الخ (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب رفع الیدین فی الاستقاء ص ۷۲ انمبر ۱۱۷۳) اس حدیث میں اس کا تذکرہ ہے کہ آپ کے لئے منبر رکھا گیا اور اس پر آپ بیٹھ گئے اور تکبیر و حمید کی جس میں خطبہ کا اشارہ ہے۔ البتہ ایسا خطبہ نہیں دیا جو عیدین اور جمعہ میں دیا جاتا ہے۔ اسی لئے بعض حدیث میں ہے کہ اس طرح کا خطبہ نہیں دیا کرتے تھے (۲) عن عبد الله بن زيد قال خرج رسول الله الا الله يستسقى فخطب الناس فلما اراد ان يدعو اقبل بوجهه الى القبلة حول رداءه (دار قطنی، کتاب الاستقاء ج ثانی ص ۵۴ نمبر ۱۷۸۶) اس حدیث سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ نماز استسقاء میں خطبہ دینا چاہئے ۔ اور لوگوں کو اسغفار اور توبہ کے بارے میں سمجھانا چاہئے۔
۱۳۹۵ (۴) استسقاء میں ذمی حاضر نہ ہوں۔ دمی کا فر ہیں۔ ان پر اللہ کا غضب نازل ہوتا ہے اس لئے پانی مانگنے کے موقع پر مغضوب آدمیوں کو حاضر نہیں کرنا چاہئے ۔
حاشیه : (الف) حضور پانی مانگنے کے لئے نکلے، پس قبلہ کی طرف متوجہ ہوئے دعا کرے ہوئے اور اپنے چادر کو پلٹا ۔ پھر دو رکعت نماز پڑھی۔ ان دونوں میں زور سے قرآت پڑھی (ب) حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ لوگوں نے حضور کے سامنے بارش نہ ہونے کی شکایت کی۔ پس منبر لانے کا حکم دیا گیا۔ پس آپ کے لئے عید گاہ میں منبر رکھا گیا ۔ آپ اس پر تشریف فرما ہوئے پھر تکبیر کہی اللہ کی تعریف کی ( پھر آگے ایسا خطبہ دینے کا ذکر ہے )
Book of Prayer. May Allah have mercy on them both: The imam prays two rak'ahs, reciting aloud in them. Then he delivers a sermon, faces the qibla during supplication, and the imam turns his cloak, but the people do not turn their cloaks. And the dhimmis do not attend the prayer for rain. (Footnote a: He went out to pray for rain, then faced the qibla, supplicated, and turned his cloak. Then he prayed two rak'ahs, reciting aloud in both.) (Hadith references from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). From this hadith it is understood that the imam will lead two rak'ahs, recite aloud, and turn his cloak as a good omen, saying: O Allah, just as I turn my cloak, turn my condition. It is also understood that during supplication he should face the qibla. (3) Then the imam delivers a sermon, faces the qibla during supplication, and the imam turns his cloak, but the congregation does not turn their cloaks. The proofs for other matters have passed. The proof for delivering the sermon is the hadith of Aisha: The people complained to the Messenger of Allah about lack of rain, so he ordered a pulpit to be placed in the prayer ground... He sat on the pulpit, said takbir, and praised Allah. This hadith indicates a sermon, but it is not like the sermon of Eid and Jumu'ah. For this reason, some hadith state that he did not give such a sermon. (2) From Abdullah ibn Zaid: The Messenger of Allah went out to pray for rain, delivered a sermon to the people, and when he wanted to supplicate, he turned his face to the qibla and turned his cloak. From this hadith it is also understood that a sermon should be given in the istisqa prayer, and the people should be taught about seeking forgiveness and repentance. (4) Dhimmis should not attend the istisqa. Dhimmis are disbelievers; Allah's wrath descends upon them, so at the time of asking for rain, angry people should not be present. Footnote: (a) He went out to ask for water, then faced the qibla, supplicated, and turned his cloak. Then he prayed two rak'ahs, reciting aloud in them. (b) Aisha says: The people complained to the Prophet about the lack of rain. He ordered the pulpit to be brought, so it was placed in the prayer ground. He sat on it, said takbir, praised Allah, and then mentioned the sermon.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Prayer, specifically about the prayer for rain (istisqa). The author states the basic rulings: the imam leads two rak'ahs with loud recitation, delivers a sermon (khutbah), faces the qibla when making du'a, and turns his cloak as a symbolic gesture of turning one's condition. The congregation does not turn their cloaks. Additionally, dhimmis (non-Muslim subjects) are not to attend the istisqa because they are disbelievers deserving of Allah's wrath. The proofs for the khutbah are from the hadith of Aisha, which shows the Prophet used a pulpit and delivered words of praise, indicating a sermon. However, this sermon is not like the one for Eid or Jumu'ah. The act of facing the qibla during du'a is proven from the hadith of Abdullah ibn Zaid. The reason dhimmis are excluded is that they are objects of divine anger, so their presence is inappropriate when beseeching for rain. The commentary elaborates on these points, citing sources from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Dar Qutni.

Key Terms
استسقاء (istisqa): Prayer for rain, a special sunnah prayer performed when drought occurs.
رجہر بالقراءة (jahr bil qira'ah): Reciting the Quran audibly during prayer.
رداء (rida'): The cloak or upper garment worn by men; the imam turns it (swap sides) as a symbol of change.
ذمة (dhimma): The covenant of protection given to non-Muslim subjects in an Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what action is the imam instructed to do that the congregation does not do during the istisqa prayer?
A) Recite aloud
B) Give a sermon
C) Turn his cloak
D) Face the qibla

Key Takeaway
Istisqa is a sunnah prayer with specific etiquettes: the imam recites aloud, gives a sermon, faces the qibla, and turns his cloak, while the congregation does not turn their cloaks and dhimmis are not present.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Tarawih: Twenty Rak'ahs in Congregation
Ruling with proof for Tarawih congregation and rak'ah count

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding Tarawih prayer (number of rak'ahs and congregation) and cite the primary proofs.

Core Idea
Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs prayed in congregation after Isha – a sunnah established by the Prophet's practice and confirmed by Umar.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on Tarawih, the special night prayers of Ramadan. The text clarifies that 'Qiyam Ramadan' refers to Tarawih, not Tahajjud, and details the recommended practice: five tarwihas of four rak'ahs each, twenty rak'ahs total, prayed in congregation after Isha. We will explore the proofs from the Prophet's actions and the practice of the righteous caliph.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon (Tarawih) and the legal classification (mustahabb/sunnah mu'akkadah).
The text explicitly states 'mustahabb' but Hanafis consider it sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the hadith of Aisha (congregational Tarawih) and the proofs for the number: Ibn Abbas (Prophet prayed 20 rak'ahs alone) and Umar's order.
These ahadith are from Bukhari, Muslim, Bayhaqi, and Ibn Abi Shaybah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how each proof supports the ruling: the congregational hadith shows the Prophet led Tarawih in congregation, and the number hadiths specify twenty rak'ahs.
The Prophet stopped congregational prayer for fear of obligation, but Umar revived it as a sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Acknowledge that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i, Maliki) may have different numbers (8, 36). The Hanafi school relies on the stronger evidence.
The Hanafi position is based on the practice of the Prophet (alone) and Umar (congregation).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is twenty rak'ahs in congregation. This is supported by the majority of Hanafi scholars and the practice of the early community.
The ruling is considered zahir al-riwayah from Imam Muhammad's books.

Source Text

فانه لم يخف على مكانكم لكني خشيت ان تفرض عليكم فتعجزوا عنها فتوفى رسول الله والامر على ذلک (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب فضل من قام رمضان ص ۲۶۹ نمبر ۲۰۱۲ مسلم شریف ، باب الترغیب فی قیام رمضان وهو التراویح ص ۲۵۹ نمبر ۱۷۸۴/۷۶۱ارابوداؤد شریف، کتاب تفریح ابواب شهر رمضان باب فی قیام شہر رمضان ص ۲۰۲ نمبر ۱۳۷۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور تراویح کے لئے رمضان میں تین راتیں کھڑے ہوئے تھے اور لوگوں کو تراویح پڑھائی تھی۔ البتہ ہمیشہ اس لئے نہیں پڑھائی کہ کہیں فرض نہ ہو جائے۔ بیس رکعت تراویح کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال كان النبى الله يصلى في شهر رمضان في غير جماعة بعشرين ركعة والوتر (ب) ( سنن بیتی ، باب ماروی فی عد درکعات القيام في شهر رمضان ج ثانی ص ۶۸۹ نمبر ۳۶۱۵/ ) (۲) ان عدد نمبر۴۶۱۵/ عمر بن خطاب امر رجلا يصلى بهم عشرين ركعة ( ج ) ) مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۶۷۷ کم یصلی فی رمضان من رکعۃ، ج ثانی، ص حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عائشہ نے خبر دی کہ حضور ایک رات درمیان رات میں نکلے تو مسجد میں نماز پڑھائی اور لوگوں نے بھی ان کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی، صبح ہوئی تو لوگ باتیں کرنے لگے تو دوسری رات اس سے زیادہ جمع ہو گئے تو آپ نے نماز پڑھی اور لوگوں نے بھی آپ کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی۔ صبح ہوئی تو لوگ باتیں کرنے لگے۔ تو مسجد والے تیسری رات زیادہ ہو گئے تو حضور نکلے اور ان کو نماز پڑھائی تو لوگوں نے آپ کے پیچھے نماز پڑھی۔ پس جب چوتھی رات ہوئی تو مسجد نمازیوں سے ناکافی ہو گئی ۔ یہاں تک کہ آپ صبح کی نماز کے لئے نکلے۔ پس جب فجر کی نماز پڑھی تو لوگوں پر متوجہ ہوئے ۔ آپ نے تشہد پڑھی پھر فرمایا اما بعد ! تمہارے حرکات مجھے پر پوشیدہ نہیں تھے لیکن میں ڈرتا ہوں کہ تم پر تراویح فرض ہو جائے۔ اور تم اس کے ادا کرنے سے عاجز ہو جاؤ۔ پھر حضور کا انتقال ہوا اور معاملہ ایسا ہی تھا (ب ) حضرت ابن عباس نے فرمایا کہ حضور رمضان کے مہینہ میں بغیر جماعت کے میں رکعت اور وتر پڑھتے تھے (ج) حضرت عمر نے ایک آدمی کو حکم دیا کہ لوگوں کو میں رکھتیں پڑھائے۔
Chapter on the Standing of the Month of Ramadan. Important note: Qiyam Ramadan here does not mean Tahajjud but Tarawih. In Muslim Sharif, the chapter is 'Encouragement for Qiyam Ramadan, which is Tarawih'. [396] (1) It is mustahabb for people to gather in the month of Ramadan after Isha, and their imam leads them in five tarwihas. In each tarwiha there are two salams; they will give salutation twice in each tarwiha. Two rak'ahs and two rak'ahs make four rak'ahs. So each tarwiha consists of four rak'ahs, thus five tarwihas make twenty rak'ahs. The proof for praying Tarawih is the hadith: (1) Aisha informed him that the Messenger of Allah went out one night in the middle of the night and prayed in the mosque, and men prayed with him. In the morning the people spoke about it, so more of them gathered, and he prayed and they prayed with him. In the morning the people spoke about it, and on the third night the mosque became crowded. The Messenger of Allah came out and led them in prayer. When it was the fourth night, the mosque was insufficient for its people until he came out for the dawn prayer. When he finished Fajr, he turned to the people, recited the tashahhud, and said, 'After that: Your presence was not hidden from me, but I feared that it would be made obligatory upon you and you would be unable to do it.' Then the Messenger of Allah passed away and the matter remained as such. (Bukhari no. 2012, Muslim no. 1784, Abu Dawud no. 1373). From this hadith it is understood that the Prophet stood for Tarawih in Ramadan for three nights and led the people in Tarawih. However, he did not continue it permanently lest it become obligatory. The proof for twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas: The Prophet used to pray in Ramadan without congregation twenty rak'ahs and witr. (Sunan Bayhaqi no. 3615). And also: Umar ibn al-Khattab ordered a man to lead them in twenty rak'ahs. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). Footnotes: (a) Aisha reported that the Prophet went out one night... (full story). (b) Ibn Abbas said: The Prophet used to pray twenty rak'ahs and witr in Ramadan without congregation. (c) Umar ordered a man to lead the people in twenty rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about Tarawih prayer in Ramadan. The author clarifies that 'Qiyam Ramadan' in this context refers to Tarawih, not Tahajjud. The ruling states that it is mustahabb (recommended) for the community to gather after Isha in Ramadan and for the imam to lead them in five tarwihas. A tarwiha is a set of two salams (i.e., two pairs of two rak'ahs), totaling four rak'ahs. Five tarwihas thus yield twenty rak'ahs. The proof for the congregational Tarawih is the authentic hadith of Aisha describing the Prophet leading the prayer for three nights, then stopping for fear of it becoming obligatory. The proof for the specific number of twenty rak'ahs comes from the practice of the Prophet himself (reported by Ibn Abbas, praying twenty rak'ahs alone) and from the action of Caliph Umar, who ordered twenty rak'ahs to be led in congregation. This establishes the Hanafi position that Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs, prayed in congregation after Isha, and it is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized practice).

Key Terms
تراویح (tarawih): The special night prayers performed in congregation during Ramadan after Isha.
ترویحہ (tarwiha): A set within Tarawih; one tarwiha consists of two salams (i.e., two pairs of two rak'ahs = four rak'ahs).
قیام رمضان (qiyam Ramadan): Literally 'standing of Ramadan', referring to Tarawih prayers in this context.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an action that is rewarded but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, how many rak'ahs constitute the Tarawih prayer in the Hanafi school?
A) 8 rak'ahs
B) 20 rak'ahs
C) 36 rak'ahs
D) 10 rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a sunnah mu'akkadah of twenty rak'ahs, prayed in congregation after Isha in Ramadan, established by the Prophet's practice and Umar's revival.

Sitting between Tarvihas and Witr in Congregation in Ramadan
Rulings on Tarawih rest and Witr congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting between tarvihas and praying Witr in congregation in Ramadan, and cite the evidences from the Sahaba.

Core Idea
Witr in congregation is a sunnah of Ramadan; a brief rest between tarvihas prevents hardship.

In this passage, the author presents two related rulings for the Tarawih prayer in Ramadan: the imam should take a short rest between sets of four rak'ahs, and then lead the congregation in Witr. These practices are supported by the actions of Umar and Ali, may Allah be pleased with them. Understanding these rulings helps us follow the sunnah of the Salaf in Ramadan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
The passage gives two separate rulings: sitting between tarvihas and praying Witr in congregation in Ramadan.
2
Locate the evidence
For sitting: the athar of Umar (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). For Witr congregation: the athar of Ali.
3
Understand the legal weight
Both are sunnah muakkadah based on Sahaba practice, not obligatory.
4
Recognize the exception
Witr in congregation is only for Ramadan; outside it is prayed individually.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Some schools do not recommend these practices or have different views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خمس ترويحات في كل ترويحة تسليمتان . [٣٩٧] (٢) ويجلس بين كل ترويحتين ترویحہ کی مقدار پھر لوگوں کو وتر پڑھائے گا۔ اور وتر رمضان کے علاوہ میں جماعت کے ساتھ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ دوترویحہ کے درمیان بیٹھنے کے لئے اثر یہ ہے کان عمر بن خطاب يروحنا في رمضان يعني بين الترويحتين قدر ما يذهب الرجل من المسجد الى سلع (ج) (سن للبيعتی ، باب مازروی فی عدد ركعات القیام فی شہر رمضان ص ۷۰۰ نمبر ۴۶۲ ) اس من ، عمل سے معلوم ہوا کہ دوترویحہ کے درمیان تھوڑا آرام بھی کرنا چاہئے تا کہ لوگ پریشان نہ ہو جائیں۔ اور رمضان میں نماز وتر جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھائی جائے گی۔ اس کے لئے اثر یہ ہے مسئلہ نمبر ایک میں بھیتی کی حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ وتر بھی تراویح کے ساتھ پڑھا کرتے تھے (۲) یہ اثر ہے عن على قال دعا القراء في رمضان فامرهم منهم رجلا يصلى بالناس عشرين ركعة قال و كان على
Five tarvihas, in each tarviha two taslims. [397] (2) And he sits between every two tarvihas to the extent of a tarviha, then leads the people in Witr. And Witr is not to be prayed in congregation outside of Ramadan. The athar for sitting between two tarvihas is: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab used to give us rest in Ramadan, meaning between the two tarvihas, for the time it takes a man to go from the mosque to Sala'. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). From this action, it is understood that a little rest should be taken between two tarvihas so that people do not get distressed. And in Ramadan, Witr prayer is to be led in congregation. The evidence for this is that in issue number one, the hadith of Bayhaqi already passed that they used to pray Witr with Tarawih. (2) This is the athar: 'Ali said: He called the reciters in Ramadan and ordered a man among them to lead the people in twenty rak'ahs.' And 'Ali would...
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage provides the second ruling of the chapter: the imam should sit between every two tarvihas for a short rest (approximately the time of one tarviha), then lead the congregation in Witr. The evidence is the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who gave the people a rest between the tarvihas long enough to walk from the mosque to the place called Sala. The wisdom is to prevent hardship. Furthermore, the passage states that Witr prayer is only prayed in congregation in Ramadan; at other times, it is prayed individually. This is supported by the practice of the early Muslims including Ali, who ordered Tarawih and Witr to be performed together in congregation.

Key Terms
ترويحة (tarviha): A set of four rak'ahs in Tarawih; used also as a unit of time for the rest period between tarvihas.
سلع (Sala'): A place (mountain) near the Prophet's mosque in Medina, used as a measure of walking distance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of praying Witr in congregation during Ramadan according to this passage?
A) It is not allowed because Witr is always prayed alone
B) It is recommended (sunnah) to pray Witr in congregation in Ramadan
C) It is obligatory to pray Witr in congregation in Ramadan
D) It is only allowed if the imam sits between tarvihas

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of Ramadan includes a brief rest between tarvihas and praying Witr in congregation, following the example of the Sahaba.

Number of Rak'ahs in Tarawih: The Hanafi Position of Twenty
Establishing the twenty-rak'ah Tarawih via proof reconciliation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of Tarawih rak'ahs and explain how the hadith of Aisha (11 rak'ahs) is reconciled with the twenty-rak'ah practice.

Core Idea
Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs; the hadith of 11 rak'ahs refers to Tahajjud, not Tarawih.

A common objection to the Hanafi twenty-rak'ah Tarawih is the hadith that the Prophet (ṣallallāhu 'alayhi wa sallam) prayed only eleven rak'ahs in Ramadan. In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi rebuttal: that hadith describes Tahajjud, not Tarawih. We will trace the reasoning based on textual indicators and Companion practice, and see how later scholars reconciled both narrations.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs, divided into five tarwihas (each tarwiha = 4 rak'ahs with two taslims).
This is the muftā bihī position.
2
Identify the contradictory proof
Recognize the hadith of 'Ā'ishah (radiyallāhu 'anha) that the Prophet prayed eleven rak'ahs in Ramadan, which some use to argue Tarawih is 8 or 11 rak'ahs.
This hadith is cited in the lesson's source text.
3
Analyze the Hanafi reconciliation
Examine the three reasons given in the passage: (1) the hadith appears in chapters on Tahajjud/Witr, not Tarawih; (2) it describes praying four rak'ahs together, but Tarawih is prayed in pairs; (3) Bayhaqi reconciled by saying eleven rak'ahs were for Tahajjud and twenty for Tarawih.
These three points form the core of the Hanafi refutation.
4
Evaluate the strength of the evidence
Consider the authority: the twenty-rak'ah practice is from the Companions (Umar, Ali), which carries weight (qawl al-ṣaḥābī) and is mutawātir by practice.
The Hanafi school relies on this combined evidence.

كتاب الصلوة
خمس ترويحات في كل ترويحة تسليمتان . [۳۹۷] (۲) ويجلس بين كل ترويحتين ۱۶۵، نمبر ۱ ۷۶۸ / مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب قیام رمضان ج رابع ص ۲۶۰ نمبر ۷۷۳) اس حدیث اور عمل صحابہ سے معلوم ہوا کہ تراویح کی نماز ہیں رکھتیں ہیں۔ وت حضرت عائشہ کی حدیث میں ہے کہ رمضان اور غیر رمضان میں آپ نے گیارہ رکعتوں سے زیادہ نہیں پڑھی اور اس حدیث کو امام بخاری وغیرہ نے باب قیام رمضان میں لایا ہے۔ یہ حدیث تراویح کی ہیں رکعتوں کے خلاف نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ قیام اللیل سے مراد اس حدیث میں تہجد کی نماز ہے۔ کیونکہ (۱) اس حدیث کو مسلم شریف میں اور بخاری شریف میں تہجد اور وتر کے باب میں بھی نقل کیا ہے (۲) اس حدیث میں تذکرہ ہے کہ آپ چار رکعتیں ایک ساتھ پڑھا کرتے تھے جن کے حسن کا کیا کہنا۔ اور تراویح کی نماز ایک ساتھ چار رکعت نہیں ہوتی۔ بلکہ دو دو رکعت کر کے ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے وہ حدیث تراویح کے بارے میں نہیں ہے بلکہ تہجد کے بارے میں ہے۔ حضرت عائشہ کی حدیث کا ٹکڑا اس طرح ہے يَصْلِي أَرْبَعًا فَلا تَسْأَلْ عَنْ حُسْنِهِنَّ وَطُولِهِنَّ ثُمَّ يُصَلِّي أَرْبَعًا فَلا تَسْأَلْ عَنْ حُسْنِهِنَّ وَطُولِهِنَّ ثُمَّ يُصَلِّي ثَلاثًا (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب فضل من قام رمضان ص ۲۶۹ نمبر ۲۰۱۳ر مسلم شریف، نمبر ۷۳۸ ) اس حدیث میں ذکر ہے کہ آپ چار رکعت ایک ساتھ پڑھتے تھے اور پھر چار رکعت ایک ساتھ پڑھتے تھے۔ اور چار رکعت ایک ساتھ تراویح کی نہیں پڑھتے اس لئے یہ تہجد کے بارے میں ہے (۳) سنن سیتی نے دونوں روایتوں کو اس طرح جمع کیا ہے کہ پہلے گیارہ رکعت تہجد پڑھتے ہوں گے۔ پھر میں رکعت تراویح پڑھتے ہوں گے۔ ان کا جملہ اس طرح ہے وَيُمْكِنُ الْجَمْعُ بَيْنَ الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ فَإِنَّهُمْ كَانُوا يَقُومُونَ بِإِحْدَى عَشْرَةَ ثُمَّ كَانُوا يَقُومُونَ بِعِشْرِينَ وَيُوتِرُونَ بِثَلاثٍ (ب) ( سنن بیھتی ، باب ماروی فی عدد رکعات القیام فی شہر رمضان ج ثانی ص ۶۹۹ نمبر ۴۶۱۸)
.
(۳۹۷) (۲) ہر دو ترویجہ کے درمیان بیٹھے گا ترویحہ کی مقدار پھر لوگوں کو وتر پڑھائے گا۔ اور وتر رمضان کے علاوہ میں جماعت کے ساتھ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ دوترویحہ کے درمیان بیٹھنے کے لئے اثر یہ ہے كَانَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ يُرَوِّحُنَا فِي رَمَضَانَ يَعْنِي بَيْنَ التَّرْوِيحَتَيْنِ قَدْرَ مَا يَذْهَبُ الرَّجُلُ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ إِلَى سَلْعٍ (ج) (سن للبيعتی ، باب مازروی فی عدد ركعات القیام فی شہر رمضان ص ۷۰۰ نمبر ۴۶۲ ) اس من ، عمل سے معلوم ہوا کہ دوترویحہ کے درمیان تھوڑا آرام بھی کرنا چاہئے تا کہ لوگ پریشان نہ ہو جائیں۔ اور رمضان میں نماز وتر جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھائی جائے گی۔ اس کے لئے اثر یہ ہے مسئلہ نمبر ایک میں بھیتی کی حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ وتر بھی تراویح کے ساتھ پڑھا کرتے تھے (۲) یہ اثر ہے عَنْ عَلِيٍّ قَالَ دَعَا الْقُرَّاءَ فِي رَمَضَانَ فَأَمَرَهُمْ مَنْهُمْ رَجُلاً يُصَلِّي بِالنَّاسِ عِشْرِينَ رَكْعَةً قَالَ وَكَانَ عَلِيٌّ يُوتِرُ بِهِمْ (الف) (سن للبیھقی ، باب ماروی فی عدد ركعات القیام فی شہر رمضان ص ۶۹۹ نمبر ۴۶۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ رمضان میں وتر جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھائی جائے گی۔ اور دنوں میں لوگ اپنے اپنے طور پر وتر پڑھیں گے۔
Book of Prayer. Five tarwihas, in each tarwiha two taslims. [397] (2) And he sits between every two tarwihas... From this hadith and the practice of the Companions, it is known that the prayer of Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs. The hadith of Aisha states that in Ramadan and outside Ramadan, the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wasallam) did not pray more than eleven rak'ahs, and Imam Bukhari and others brought this hadith in the chapter of standing in Ramadan. This hadith does not contradict the twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih because what is meant by 'standing at night' in this hadith is the Tahajjud prayer. Because (1) this hadith is also narrated in Sahih Muslim and Sahih Bukhari in the chapters of Tahajjud and Witr. (2) In this hadith, it is mentioned that the Prophet used to pray four rak'ahs together, how excellent they were! And the prayer of Tarawih is not performed as four rak'ahs together, but rather in sets of two rak'ahs. Therefore, that hadith is not about Tarawih but about Tahajjud. The text of Aisha's hadith is: 'He used to pray four rak'ahs – do not ask about their beauty and length – then pray four rak'ahs – do not ask about their beauty and length – then pray three [rak'ahs].' (a) (Bukhari, chapter on merit of Ramadan night prayer, p. 269, no. 2013; Muslim, no. 738). This hadith mentions that he prayed four rak'ahs together and then another four rak'ahs together. And Tarawih is not prayed as four rak'ahs together; therefore, it is about Tahajjud. (3) Sunan al-Bayhaqi reconciled the two narrations in this way: first they would pray eleven rak'ahs of Tahajjud, then they would pray twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih and pray Witr with three. Their statement is: 'It is possible to reconcile the two narrations, for they would stand with eleven [for Tahajjud], then would stand with twenty [for Tarawih], and would pray Witr with three.' (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is narrated about the number of rak'ahs of standing in Ramadan, vol. 2, p. 699, no. 4618). (397) (2) He will sit between every two tarwihas for the duration of a tarwiha, then he will lead the people in Witr. And Witr will not be prayed in congregation outside the month of Ramadan. For sitting between two tarwihas, there is the effect: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab used to give us rest in Ramadan, meaning between the two tarwihas, for the time it takes a man to go from the mosque to Sal' (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is narrated about the number of rak'ahs of standing in Ramadan, p. 700, no. 462). From this practice, it is known that one should take a little rest between two tarwihas so that people do not become distressed. And in Ramadan, the Witr prayer will be led in congregation. For this, the effect in issue number one from Bayhaqi has already passed that they would pray Witr together with Tarawih. (2) This effect is: 'Ali said: He called the reciters in Ramadan and ordered among them a man to lead the people in twenty rak'ahs. He said: And Ali would lead them in Witr.' (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is narrated about the number of rak'ahs of standing in Ramadan, p. 699, no. 462). From this effect, it is known that Witr will be prayed in congregation in Ramadan, and on other days people will pray Witr individually.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage from Al Sharh Ul Sameri addresses three key rulings of Tarawih prayer according to the Hanafi school. First, the number of rak'ahs: Tarawih consists of twenty rak'ahs, divided into five 'tarwihas'. Each tarwiha includes two taslims (i.e., four rak'ahs, since each taslim is after two rak'ahs). This is established by the practice of the Companions and the hadith of Aisha (radiyallahu anha) regarding eleven rak'ahs is reconciled by noting that it refers to Tahajjud, not Tarawih—because Tarawih is prayed in pairs of two, not four at once. Second, the sitting between tarwihas: the imam sits briefly between each tarwiha, based on the practice of Umar (radiyallahu anhu), who allowed a rest long enough to walk from the mosque to the nearby market area of Sal'. This prevents hardship. Third, Witr in Ramadan: the Witr prayer is led in congregation during Ramadan, following the practice of Ali (radiyallahu anhu), but outside Ramadan, Witr is prayed individually. The author uses hadith and companion practice (athar) as proofs, typical of the Hanafi methodology.

Key Terms
ترويحة (tarwiha): A set of four rak'ahs of Tarawih prayer (two taslims) with a rest afterward.
قيام رمضان (qiyam Ramadan): The night prayer of Ramadan, encompassing both Tarawih and Tahajjud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school reject using the hadith of 'Ā'ishah (11 rak'ahs) as proof that Tarawih should be 11 rak'ahs?
A) The hadith is weak in transmission.
B) The hadith refers to Tahajjud, not Tarawih, as shown by context and Companion practice.
C) The hadith is abrogated by a later verse.
D) The hadith only applies outside Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is a sunnah mu'akkadah of 20 rak'ahs, established by Companion practice, and the hadith of 11 rak'ahs refers to Tahajjud, not Tarawih.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
5 min
Sitting Between Tarwihas: The Sunnah of Rest
Establishing the sitting between tarwihas as a sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting between tarwihas and identify the evidence from Companion practice.

Core Idea
Sitting between tarwihas is a sunnah to give rest, based on 'Umar's practice.

Tarawih is a lengthy prayer, and the early Muslims would rest between sets of rak'ahs. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that the imam sits for a short while between each tarwiha, a practice traced to 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (radiyallahu 'anhu). We will see the evidence from athar and the wisdom behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on sitting between tarwihas
State that the Hanafi school considers it sunnah to sit briefly between each tarwiha (set of 4 rak'ahs).
The text says 'he sits between every two tarwihas'.
2
Examine the evidence from 'Umar
The passage quotes the effect: 'Umar would give them rest between tarwihas long enough to walk to the market of Sal'.
This shows the duration is approximate, not strictly timed.
3
Understand the purpose
The rest prevents hardship and allows worshippers to regain energy.
This aligns with the Hanafi principle of preventing difficulty (raf' al-haraj).

خمس ترويحات في كل ترويحة تسليمتان . .
(۳۹۷) (۲) ہر دو ترویجہ کے درمیان بیٹھے گا ترویحہ کی مقدار پھر لوگوں کو وتر پڑھائے گا۔ اور وتر رمضان کے علاوہ میں جماعت کے ساتھ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ دوترویحہ کے درمیان بیٹھنے کے لئے اثر یہ ہے كَانَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ يُرَوِّحُنَا فِي رَمَضَانَ يَعْنِي بَيْنَ التَّرْوِيحَتَيْنِ قَدْرَ مَا يَذْهَبُ الرَّجُلُ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ إِلَى سَلْعٍ (ج) (سن للبيعتی ، باب مازروی فی عدد ركعات القیام فی شہر رمضان ص ۷۰۰ نمبر ۴۶۲ ) اس من ، عمل سے معلوم ہوا کہ دوترویحہ کے درمیان تھوڑا آرام بھی کرنا چاہئے تا کہ لوگ پریشان نہ ہو جائیں۔ اور رمضان میں نماز وتر جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھائی جائے گی۔ اس کے لئے اثر یہ ہے مسئلہ نمبر ایک میں بھیتی کی حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ وتر بھی تراویح کے ساتھ پڑھا کرتے تھے (۲) یہ اثر ہے عَنْ عَلِيٍّ قَالَ دَعَا الْقُرَّاءَ فِي رَمَضَانَ فَأَمَرَهُمْ مَنْهُمْ رَجُلاً يُصَلِّي بِالنَّاسِ عِشْرِينَ رَكْعَةً قَالَ وَكَانَ عَلِيٌّ يُوتِرُ بِهِمْ (الف) (سن للبیھقی ، باب ماروی فی عدد ركعات القیام فی شہر رمضان ص ۶۹۹ نمبر ۴۶۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ رمضان میں وتر جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھائی جائے گی۔ اور دنوں میں لوگ اپنے اپنے طور پر وتر پڑھیں گے۔
Book of Prayer. Five tarwihas, in each tarwiha two taslims. [397] (2) And he sits between every two tarwihas... From this hadith and the practice of the Companions, it is known that the prayer of Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs.
