This hadith does not contradict the twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih because what is meant by 'standing at night' in this hadith is the Tahajjud prayer. Because (1) this hadith is also narrated in Sahih Muslim and Sahih Bukhari in the chapters of Tahajjud and Witr. (2) In this hadith, it is mentioned that the Prophet used to pray four rak'ahs together, how excellent they were! And the prayer of Tarawih is not performed as four rak'ahs together, but rather in sets of two rak'ahs. Therefore, that hadith is not about Tarawih but about Tahajjud. The text of Aisha's hadith is: 'He used to pray four rak'ahs – do not ask about their beauty and length – then pray four rak'ahs – do not ask about their beauty and length – then pray three [rak'ahs].' (a) (Bukhari, chapter on merit of Ramadan night prayer, p. 269, no. 2013; Muslim, no. 738). This hadith mentions that he prayed four rak'ahs together and then another four rak'ahs together. And Tarawih is not prayed as four rak'ahs together; therefore, it is about Tahajjud. (3) Sunan al-Bayhaqi reconciled the two narrations in this way: first they would pray eleven rak'ahs of Tahajjud, then they would pray twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih and pray Witr with three. Their statement is: 'It is possible to reconcile the two narrations, for they would stand with eleven [for Tahajjud], then would stand with twenty [for Tarawih], and would pray Witr with three.' (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is narrated about the number of rak'ahs of standing in Ramadan, vol. 2, p. 699, no. 4618). (397) (2) He will sit between every two tarwihas for the duration of a tarwiha, then he will lead the people in Witr. And Witr will not be prayed in congregation outside the month of Ramadan. For sitting between two tarwihas, there is the effect: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab used to give us rest in Ramadan, meaning between the two tarwihas, for the time it takes a man to go from the mosque to Sal' (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is narrated about the number of rak'ahs of standing in Ramadan, p. 700, no. 462). (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is narrated about the number of rak'ahs of standing in Ramadan, p. 699, no. 462). From this effect, it is known that Witr will be prayed in congregation in Ramadan, and on other days people will pray Witr individually.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage from Al Sharh Ul Sameri addresses three key rulings of Tarawih prayer according to the Hanafi school. First, the number of rak'ahs: Tarawih consists of twenty rak'ahs, divided into five 'tarwihas'. Each tarwiha includes two taslims (i.e., four rak'ahs, since each taslim is after two rak'ahs). This is established by the practice of the Companions and the hadith of Aisha (radiyallahu anha) regarding eleven rak'ahs is reconciled by noting that it refers to Tahajjud, not Tarawih—because Tarawih is prayed in pairs of two, not four at once. Second, the sitting between tarwihas: the imam sits briefly between each tarwiha, based on the practice of Umar (radiyallahu anhu), who allowed a rest long enough to walk from the mosque to the nearby market area of Sal'. This prevents hardship. Third, Witr in Ramadan: the Witr prayer is led in congregation during Ramadan, following the practice of Ali (radiyallahu anhu), but outside Ramadan, Witr is prayed individually. The author uses hadith and companion practice (athar) as proofs, typical of the Hanafi methodology.

Key Terms
ترويحة (tarwiha): A set of four rak'ahs of Tarawih prayer (two taslims) with a rest afterward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the sunnah of sitting between tarwihas?
A) A direct command from the Prophet in a hadith.
B) The practice of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab.
C) Analogy to the sitting in the Friday sermon.
D) A consensus of the four schools.

Key Takeaway
Sitting between tarwihas is a sunnah to provide rest, established by the practice of 'Umar.

Witr in Congregation During Ramadan
Specifying the congregation for Witr to Ramadan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Witr is prayed in congregation only during Ramadan and identify the evidence from Companion practice.

Core Idea
Witr is prayed in congregation during Ramadan, but individually outside it.

The third ruling in this passage deals with the special status of Witr in Ramadan. In the Hanafi school, Witr is prayed in congregation during Ramadan, following the practice of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib (radiyallahu 'anhu). Outside Ramadan, Witr is performed individually. This lesson examines the evidence and the wisdom behind this distinction.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on Witr congregation
Identify: In Ramadan, Witr is prayed in congregation after Tarawih. In other months, it is prayed individually.
This is the muftā bihī position.
2
Examine the evidence from 'Ali
The passage quotes the effect: 'Ali called the reciters in Ramadan and appointed a man to lead 20 rak'ahs; then 'Ali himself led them in Witr.
This shows the Caliph's practice.
3
Understand the wisdom
Why only Ramadan? Because the congregation is already gathered for Tarawih, so it is convenient. Outside Ramadan, Witr is a personal prayer.
This reflects the principle of ease.

(۳۹۷) (۲) ہر دو ترویجہ کے درمیان بیٹھے گا ترویحہ کی مقدار پھر لوگوں کو وتر پڑھائے گا۔ اور وتر رمضان کے علاوہ میں جماعت کے ساتھ نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ دوترویحہ کے درمیان بیٹھنے کے لئے اثر یہ ہے كَانَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ يُرَوِّحُنَا فِي رَمَضَانَ يَعْنِي بَيْنَ التَّرْوِيحَتَيْنِ قَدْرَ مَا يَذْهَبُ الرَّجُلُ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ إِلَى سَلْعٍ (ج) (سن للبيعتی ، باب مازروی فی عدد ركعات القیام فی شہر رمضان ص ۷۰۰ نمبر ۴۶۲ ) اس من ، عمل سے معلوم ہوا کہ دوترویحہ کے درمیان تھوڑا آرام بھی کرنا چاہئے تا کہ لوگ پریشان نہ ہو جائیں۔ اور رمضان میں نماز وتر جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھائی جائے گی۔ اس کے لئے اثر یہ ہے مسئلہ نمبر ایک میں بھیتی کی حدیث گزر چکی ہے کہ وتر بھی تراویح کے ساتھ پڑھا کرتے تھے (۲) یہ اثر ہے عَنْ عَلِيٍّ قَالَ دَعَا الْقُرَّاءَ فِي رَمَضَانَ فَأَمَرَهُمْ مَنْهُمْ رَجُلاً يُصَلِّي بِالنَّاسِ عِشْرِينَ رَكْعَةً قَالَ وَكَانَ عَلِيٌّ يُوتِرُ بِهِمْ (الف) (سن للبیھقی ، باب ماروی فی عدد ركعات القیام فی شہر رمضان ص ۶۹۹ نمبر ۴۶۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ رمضان میں وتر جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھائی جائے گی۔ اور دنوں میں لوگ اپنے اپنے طور پر وتر پڑھیں گے۔
Book of Prayer. Five tarwihas, in each tarwiha two taslims. [397] (2) And he sits between every two tarwihas... From this hadith and the practice of the Companions, it is known that the prayer of Tarawih is twenty rak'ahs. The hadith of Aisha states that in Ramadan and outside Ramadan, the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wasallam) did not pray more than eleven rak'ahs, and Imam Bukhari and others brought this hadith in the chapter of standing in Ramadan. This hadith does not contradict the twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih because what is meant by 'standing at night' in this hadith is the Tahajjud prayer. Because (1) this hadith is also narrated in Sahih Muslim and Sahih Bukhari in the chapters of Tahajjud and Witr. (2) In this hadith, it is mentioned that the Prophet used to pray four rak'ahs together, how excellent they were! And the prayer of Tarawih is not performed as four rak'ahs together, but rather in sets of two rak'ahs. Therefore, that hadith is not about Tarawih but about Tahajjud. The text of Aisha's hadith is: 'He used to pray four rak'ahs – do not ask about their beauty and length – then pray four rak'ahs – do not ask about their beauty and length – then pray three [rak'ahs].' (a) (Bukhari, chapter on merit of Ramadan night prayer, p. 269, no. 2013; Muslim, no. 738). This hadith mentions that he prayed four rak'ahs together and then another four rak'ahs together. And Tarawih is not prayed as four rak'ahs together; therefore, it is about Tahajjud. (3) Sunan al-Bayhaqi reconciled the two narrations in this way: first they would pray eleven rak'ahs of Tahajjud, then they would pray twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih and pray Witr with three. Their statement is: 'It is possible to reconcile the two narrations, for they would stand with eleven [for Tahajjud], then would stand with twenty [for Tarawih], and would pray Witr with three.' (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is narrated about the number of rak'ahs of standing in Ramadan, vol. 2, p. 699, no. 4618). (397) (2) He will sit between every two tarwihas for the duration of a tarwiha, then he will lead the people in Witr. And Witr will not be prayed in congregation outside the month of Ramadan. For sitting between two tarwihas, there is the effect: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab used to give us rest in Ramadan, meaning between the two tarwihas, for the time it takes a man to go from the mosque to Sal' (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is narrated about the number of rak'ahs of standing in Ramadan, p. 700, no. 462). From this practice, it is known that one should take a little rest between two tarwihas so that people do not become distressed. And in Ramadan, the Witr prayer will be led in congregation. For this, the effect in issue number one from Bayhaqi has already passed that they would pray Witr together with Tarawih. (2) This effect is: 'Ali said: He called the reciters in Ramadan and ordered among them a man to lead the people in twenty rak'ahs. He said: And Ali would lead them in Witr.' (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is narrated about the number of rak'ahs of standing in Ramadan, p. 699, no. 462). From this effect, it is known that Witr will be prayed in congregation in Ramadan, and on other days people will pray Witr individually.
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage from Al Sharh Ul Sameri addresses three key rulings of Tarawih prayer according to the Hanafi school. First, the number of rak'ahs: Tarawih consists of twenty rak'ahs, divided into five 'tarwihas'. Each tarwiha includes two taslims (i.e., four rak'ahs, since each taslim is after two rak'ahs). This is established by the practice of the Companions and the hadith of Aisha (radiyallahu anha) regarding eleven rak'ahs is reconciled by noting that it refers to Tahajjud, not Tarawih—because Tarawih is prayed in pairs of two, not four at once. Second, the sitting between tarwihas: the imam sits briefly between each tarwiha, based on the practice of Umar (radiyallahu anhu), who allowed a rest long enough to walk from the mosque to the nearby market area of Sal'. This prevents hardship. Third, Witr in Ramadan: the Witr prayer is led in congregation during Ramadan, following the practice of Ali (radiyallahu anhu), but outside Ramadan, Witr is prayed individually. The author uses hadith and companion practice (athar) as proofs, typical of the Hanafi methodology.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Tarawih in Ramadan, prayed in congregation according to Hanafi practice.

Witr Congregation: Specific to Ramadan
States ruling on Witr congregation in Ramadan and provides supporting athar from Ali.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational Witr and cite the evidence from Ali's practice.

Core Idea
Congregational Witr is a sunnah specific to Ramadan; outside Ramadan it is prayed individually.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on praying Witr in congregation. While Witr itself is wajib, its congregation is restricted to the nights of Ramadan. We will explore the textual evidence from the practice of Ali ibn Abi Talib and understand the distinction from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the ruling statement: 'Witr is not prayed in congregation outside the month of Ramadan.' Note the restriction.
The ruling is clear: congregational Witr only in Ramadan.
2
Locate the evidence
Identify the athar from Ali. It mentions that during Ramadan, Ali led the people in Witr after twenty rak'ahs of taraweeh.
The athar is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
3
Determine the scope
Understand that the ruling applies to the congregation itself, not the individual obligation of Witr.
Outside Ramadan, one may pray Witr alone or in congregation? The text says no congregation, so it is makruh tanzihan.
4
Note cross-madhhab difference
Contrast with the Shafi'i school, which permits congregational Witr throughout the year.
This highlights a legitimate ikhtilaf.

مقدار ترويحة ثم يوتر بهم ولا يصلى الوتر بجماعة في غير شهر رمضان. يوترهم (الف) (سن للبیھقی ، باب ماروی فی عدد ركعات القیام فی شہر رمضان ص ۶۹۹ نمبر ۴۶۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ رمضان میں وتر جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھائی جائے گی۔ اور دنوں میں لوگ اپنے اپنے طور پر وتر پڑھیں گے۔ (الف) حضرت علی نے قراء کو بلایا رمضان میں اور ان میں سے ایک آدمی کو حکم دیا کہ لوگوں کو بیس رکعت نماز پڑھائے ۔فرمایا کہ حضرت علی ان کو وتر پڑھایا کرتے تھے۔
The amount of taraweeh, then he leads them in Witr, and Witr is not prayed in congregation outside the month of Ramadan. He leads them in Witr. (a) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: what has been narrated regarding the number of rak'ahs of qiyam in the month of Ramadan, p. 699, no. 462). From this athar it is understood that in Ramadan Witr will be prayed with congregation. And on other days people will pray Witr individually. Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement concerning the congregation of Witr prayer. The author states the rule: the imam leads the people in taraweeh (the prescribed number of rak'ahs) and then leads them in Witr, but Witr is not prayed in congregation outside the month of Ramadan. The commentary then provides an athar (tradition) from Ali ibn Abi Talib to support the practice. The athar indicates that during Ramadan, Ali appointed a person to lead the people in twenty rak'ahs of taraweeh, and he (Ali) would lead them in Witr. This establishes that congregational Witr is a sunnah specific to Ramadan. Outside Ramadan, individuals should pray Witr alone. This is the Hanafi position: congregational Witr is only performed during Ramadan nights.

Key Terms
وتر (Witr): The odd-numbered prayer (last prayer of the night) that is wajib in the Hanafi school.
جماعة (Jama'ah): Congregational prayer led by an imam.
ترويحة (Taraweeh): The night prayers performed in Ramadan after Isha, which are sunnah muakkadah.

Fear Prayer: Method and the Abrogation Dispute
Presents the ruling and method of Salat al-Khawf and addresses the dispute over its validity after the Prophet's time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf and evaluate the evidence for its validity after the Prophet's time.

Core Idea
The fear prayer remains a valid sunnah; its method is a concession for safety.

Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer) is a special form of prayer during battle. This passage from al-Sharh al-Sameri outlines its method and addresses a key dispute: whether it was abrogated after the Prophet's death. We will examine the Hanafi position and its proof, and see how the practice of a Companion confirms its continuity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding the validity of Salat al-Khawf after the Prophet's death.
The passage clearly states that the jumhur (majority) of imams, including Hanafis, consider it valid.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that some scholars argue the fear prayer was abrogated after the Prophet.
These scholars are referred to as 'بعض ائمہ' (some imams).
3
Follow the opposing proof
Examine the evidence used by the opposing scholars: the Quranic verse 4:102 that directly addresses the Prophet.
They interpret 'واذا كنت فيهم' (when you are among them) as specific to the Prophet.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafis rebut this proof: the verse is a general command, and the practice of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari after the Prophet confirms it is not abrogated.
The athar from Bayhaqi is cited: Abu Musa led the fear prayer in Isfahan.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of the dispute: if abrogated, Muslims cannot use this method; if valid, they can.
The Hanafi position allows the fear prayer to be performed in dangerous situations.

باب صلوة الخوف
[۳۹۸ (۱) اذا اشتد الخوف جعل الامام الناس طائفتين طائفة الى وجه العدو وطائفة خلفه فيصلى بهذه الطائفة ركعة وسجدتين فاذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية مضت هذه باب صلوۃ الخوف )
ضروری نوت نماز خوف کی صورت یہ ہے کہ تمام آدمی ایک ہی امام کے پیچھے نماز پڑھنا چاہتے ہوں تو امام دو جماعتیں بنا دیں گے۔ اور ہر ایک جماعت کو آدھی آدھی نماز پڑھائیں گے۔ لیکن اگر دو امام ہوں تو ہر ایک جماعت الگ الگ امام کے پیچھے پوری پوری نماز پڑھیں گے ۔ پھر آدھی آدھی نماز پڑھنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ بعض ائمہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جب تک حضور حیات رہے تو ہر ایک آدمی اپنی آخری نماز آپ کے پیچھے پڑھنا چاہتا تھا اس لئے آپ کی حیات میں نماز خوف تھی۔ لیکن آپ کے بعد اب اس طرح نماز پڑھنا منسوخ ہے۔ اب دو الگ الگ امام ہوں گے اور دونوں جماعتیں الگ الگ امام کے پیچھے نماز پڑھے گی۔ ان کا استدلال اس آیت سے ہے جو صلوۃ خوف کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے۔ واذا كنت فيهم فاقم لهم الصلوة فلتقم طائفة منهم معك وليأخذوا اسلحتهم فاذا سجدوا فليكونوا من ورائكم ولتأت طائفة اخرى لم يصلوا فليصلوا معك وليأخذوا حذرهم واسلحتهم (الف ) ( آیت ۱۰۲ سورۃ النساء (۴) اس آیت میں حضور کو خطاب ہے کہ آپ موجود ہوں تو لوگوں کو نماز خوف پڑھا ئیں۔ جس کا مطلب یہ نکل سکتا ہے کہ آپ کے بعد نماز خوف اس طرح نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔
جمہور ائمہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت ابو موسی اشعری نے لوگوں کو نماز خوف پڑھائی ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بعد میں بھی صلوۃ خوف جائز ہے عن ابـي الـعـالية قال صلى بنا ابو موسى الاشعرى باصبهان صلوة الخوف (ب) (سن للبیھقی ، باب الدليل على ثبوت صلوة الخوف وانها لم تخرج ثالث ص ۱۳۵۸ نمبر ۶۰۰۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بعد میں بھی نماز خوف پڑھائی جاسکتی ہے۔
اوپر کی آیت اور یہ حدیث صلوۃ خوف کے جواز کی دلیل ہے۔ [۳۹۸] (۱) جب خوف سخت ہو جائے تو امام لوگوں کو دو جماعت بنائے گا۔ ایک جماعت دشمن کے مقابلہ میں اور دوسر جماعت امام کے پیچھے۔ پس امام پہلی جماعت کو ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے پڑھائے گا، پس جب کہ دوسرے سجدہ سے سر اٹھائے پہلی جماعت چلی جائے گی دشمن کے مقابلہ پر ، اور دوسری جماعت آئے گی تو اس کو امام نماز پڑھائے گا ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے۔ اور امام تشہد پڑھے گا اور سلام پھیرے گالیکن دوسری جماعت سلام نہیں پھیرے گی بلکہ چلی جائے گی دشمن کے مقابلہ پر۔ اور پہلی جماعت آئے گی اور وہ ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے اکیلے نماز پڑھے گی بغیر قرآت کے ( کیونکہ وہ لاحق ہے اور لاحق پر قرآت نہیں ہے اس لئے وہ قرآت نہیں کرے گی ) اور تشہد پڑھے گی اور سلام پھیرے
حاشیہ : (الف) جب آپ لوگوں میں موجود ہوں تو آپ ان کے لئے نماز قائم کیجئے۔ تو ایک جماعت ان میں سے آپ کے ساتھ کھڑی ہونی چاہئے اور ان کو اپنے ہتھیار لینے چاہئے۔ پس جب وہ سجدہ کر لیں تو وہ آپ کے پیچھے ہو جائیں اور دوسری جماعت آئے۔ جس نے نماز نہیں پڑھی ہے تو وہ آپ کے ساتھ نماز پڑھے اور اپنا بچاؤ اختیار کریں اور ہتھیار لیں (ب) ابوالعالیہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ہم کو ابوموسی اشعری نے اصفہان میں نماز خوف پڑھائی۔
Chapter of the Fear Prayer
[398 (1) When fear is intense, the imam makes the people into two groups: a group facing the enemy and a group behind him. He prays with this group one rak'ah and two prostrations. When he raises his head from the second prostration, this group goes... (end of matn)
Necessary note: The form of the fear prayer is that if all people want to pray behind one imam, the imam will make two congregations and will lead each congregation in half of the prayer. But if there are two imams, each congregation will pray the complete prayer behind its own imam, and there is no need to pray half. Some imams say: As long as the Prophet was alive, every person wanted to pray his last prayer behind him, so during his lifetime the fear prayer existed. But after him, praying in this manner is abrogated. Now there will be two separate imams and both congregations will pray behind separate imams. Their evidence is the verse that was revealed about the fear prayer: 'When you are among them and lead them in prayer, let a group of them stand with you and let them take their arms; when they prostrate, let them be behind you, and let another group who have not prayed come and pray with you, and let them take their caution and their arms.' (Verse 102 of Surah al-Nisa) In this verse, the address is to the Prophet: when you are present, lead the people in the fear prayer. This can mean that after you, the fear prayer will not be prayed in this manner.
The majority of imams say that Abu Musa al-Ash'ari led the people in the fear prayer, which means that after (the Prophet) the fear prayer is also permissible. From Abu al-Aliyah: Abu Musa al-Ash'ari led us in the fear prayer in Isfahan. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter: evidence for the establishment of the fear prayer and that it did not cease to be valid, p. 1358, no. 6008). From this athar, it is understood that the fear prayer can be led even after (the Prophet).
The above verse and this hadith are evidence for the permissibility of the fear prayer. [398] (1) When fear is intense, the imam will make the people into two congregations: one congregation facing the enemy and the other congregation behind the imam. Then the imam leads the first congregation in one rak'ah and two prostrations. When he raises his head from the second prostration, the first congregation goes to face the enemy, and the second congregation comes. Then the imam leads them in one rak'ah and two prostrations. The imam recites the tashahhud and says the salam, but the second congregation does not say salam; rather, they go to face the enemy. The first congregation comes and prays one rak'ah and two prostrations alone without recitation (because they are lahiq, and recitation is not required for the lahiq), then they recite the tashahhud and say the salam.
Footnote: (a) 'When you are among them and stand to lead them in prayer, let a group of them stand with you and let them take their arms. When they prostrate, let them be behind you, and let another group who have not prayed come and pray with you, and let them take their caution and their arms.' (b) Abu al-Aliyah said: Abu Musa al-Ash'ari led us in the fear prayer in Isfahan.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is the chapter on Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer). It begins with a ruling: when fear is intense, the imam divides the people into two groups – one facing the enemy and one behind him. He prays one rak'ah with the first group, then they go to the enemy, and the second group comes and he prays one rak'ah with them. Then the imam sits for tashahhud and says salam, but the second group does not say salam; they go to the enemy, and the first group returns to complete their remaining rak'ah without recitation (as they are 'lahiq' - followers who missed part) and then say tashahhud and salam. The commentary then discusses a dispute: some scholars hold that Salat al-Khawf was only for the Prophet's lifetime, arguing from the verse 'When you are among them...' which addresses the Prophet. However, the majority of imams (jumhur) including the Hanafis maintain it is still valid, citing the practice of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari who led the fear prayer in Isfahan after the Prophet's death. Thus the Hanafi position is that Salat al-Khawf remains permissible. The footnote provides the full verse and the hadith from Bayhaqi. This passage thus presents both the practical method and the legal dispute regarding its continuity.

Key Terms
صلوۃ الخوف (Salat al-Khawf): The fear prayer performed during battle or when in danger, with a special method.
طائفة (Ta'ifah): A group of people; in this context, one of two groups in the fear prayer.
لاحق (Lahiq): A person who missed part of the prayer and joins later; in this method, they complete without recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the Hanafi position on the validity of Salat al-Khawf after the Prophet's death?
A) It is abrogated and no longer valid.
B) It is valid, as demonstrated by the practice of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari.
C) It is only valid if the imam is the Prophet.
D) It is valid but only for two rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Khawf is a valid sunnah after the Prophet, as evidenced by the practice of Abu Musa and the general command in the Quran.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Method and Proof of the Fear Prayer (Salat al-Khawf)
Describes the Hanafi method and proof for the fear prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method for Salat al-Khawf and identify its Quranic and Hadith proofs.

Core Idea
The fear prayer is prayed in two groups, each praying one rak'ah with the imam, then completing alone without recitation.

This lesson explains the specific method of Salat al-Khawf preferred by the Hanafi school, its scriptural basis, and the reasoning behind its form. You will learn how the imam divides the congregation, the roles of the two groups, and the proofs from the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its level
Determine the legal classification of the described method from the Hanafi perspective. Is it fard, wajib, sunnah, or mustahab?
The text explicitly says 'mustahab' (preferred).
2
Outline the method step by step
Follow the sequence: imam divides people into two groups, leads one group in one rak'ah, that group leaves, second group joins for one rak'ah, imam completes his prayer, first group completes alone, second group completes with recitation.
Pay attention to the terms 'lahiq' and 'masbuq'.
3
Locate the Quranic proof (4:102) and its implication
The verse is cited as the primary dalil. Note the imperative verbs and how they indicate the method.
The verse addresses the Prophet, but the school extends it to all Muslims.
4
Note the dispute about abrogation and the Hanafi response
Some scholars argue the fear prayer was specific to the Prophet's lifetime. The Hanafis counter with the practice of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari and the general applicability of the verse.
This is the key ikhtilaf discussed in the passage.
5
Understand the reasons for the Hanafi preference
The commentary gives three reasons: (1) the verse implies delayed completion, (2) rule-based order, (3) avoiding imam waiting.
These explain why this method is chosen over others.

باب صلوة الخوف
[۳۹۸ (۱) اذا اشتد الخوف جعل الامام الناس طائفتين طائفة الى وجه العدو وطائفة خلفه فيصلى بهذه الطائفة ركعة وسجدتين فاذا رفع رأسه من السجدة الثانية مضت هذه
ضروری نوت نماز خوف کی صورت یہ ہے کہ تمام آدمی ایک ہی امام کے پیچھے نماز پڑھنا چاہتے ہوں تو امام دو جماعتیں بنا دیں گے۔ اور ہر ایک جماعت کو آدھی آدھی نماز پڑھائیں گے۔ لیکن اگر دو امام ہوں تو ہر ایک جماعت الگ الگ امام کے پیچھے پوری پوری نماز پڑھیں گے ۔ پھر آدھی آدھی نماز پڑھنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ بعض ائمہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جب تک حضور حیات رہے تو ہر ایک آدمی اپنی آخری نماز آپ کے پیچھے پڑھنا چاہتا تھا اس لئے آپ کی حیات میں نماز خوف تھی۔ لیکن آپ کے بعد اب اس طرح نماز پڑھنا منسوخ ہے۔ اب دو الگ الگ امام ہوں گے اور دونوں جماعتیں الگ الگ امام کے پیچھے نماز پڑھے گی۔ ان کا استدلال اس آیت سے ہے جو صلوۃ خوف کے بارے میں نازل ہوئی ہے۔ واذا كنت فيهم قاقمت لهم الصلوة فلتقم طائفة منهم معك وليأخذوا اسلحتهم فاذا سجدوا فليكونوا من ورائكم ولتأت طائفة اخرى لم يصلوا فليصلوا معك وليأخذوا حذرهم واسلحتهم (الف ) ( آیت ۱۰۲ سورۃ النساء (۴) اس آیت میں حضور کو خطاب ہے کہ آپ موجود ہوں تو لوگوں کو نماز خوف پڑھا ئیں۔ جس کا مطلب یہ نکل سکتا ہے کہ آپ کے بعد نماز خوف اس طرح نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔
نا جمہور ائمہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت ابو موسی اشعری نے لوگوں کو نماز خوف پڑھائی ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ بعد میں بھی صلوۃ خوف جائز ہے عن ابـي الـعـالية قال صلى بنا ابو موسى الاشعرى باصبهان صلوة الخوف (ب) (سن للبیھقی ، باب الدليل على ثبوت صلوة الخوف وانها لم تخرج ثالث ص ۱۳۵۸ نمبر ۶۰۰۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ بعد میں بھی نماز خوف پڑھائی جاسکتی ہے۔
نوں اوپر کی آیت اور یہ حدیث صلوۃ خوف کے جواز کی دلیل ہے۔ [۳۹۸] (۱) جب خوف سخت ہو جائے تو امام لوگوں کو دو جماعت بنائے گا۔ ایک جماعت دشمن کے مقابلہ میں اور دوسر جماعت امام کے پیچھے۔ پس امام پہلی جماعت کو ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے پڑھائے گا، پس جب کہ دوسرے سجدہ سے سر اٹھائے پہلی جماعت چلی جائے گی دشمن کے مقابلہ پر ، اور دوسری جماعت آئے گی تو اس کو امام نماز پڑھائے گا ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے۔ اور امام تشہد پڑھے گا اور سلام پھیرے گالیکن دوسری جماعت سلام نہیں پھیرے گی بلکہ چلی جائے گی دشمن کے مقابلہ پر۔ اور پہلی جماعت آئے گی اور وہ ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے اکیلے نماز پڑھے گی بغیر قرآت کے ( کیونکہ وہ لاحق ہے اور لاحق پر قرآت نہیں ہے اس لئے وہ قرآت نہیں کرے گی ) اور تشہد پڑھے گی اور سلام پھیرے

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاوّل)
كتاب الصلوة
[PAGE_269 continuation: وجائت الطائفة الاخرى و تشهد وسلم ولم يسلموا وذهبوا الى وجه العدوو جائت الطائفة الاولى فصلوا وحدانا ركعة وسجدتين بغير قراءة و تشهد وا وسلموا ومضوا الى وجه العدو وجائت الطائفة الاخرى
گی اور چلی جائے گی دشمن کے مقابلہ پر۔ اور دوسری جماعت آئے اور وہ ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے نماز پڑھیں قرآت کے ساتھ (اس لئے کہ یہ مسبوق ہیں اور مسبوق اپنی نماز پوری کرتے وقت قرآت کریں گے ) اور تشہد پڑھیں اور سلام پھیر دیں۔ پس اگر امام مقیم ہو تو پہلی جماعت کو دو رکعت نماز پڑھائے گا اور دوسری جماعت کو دو رکعت ۔ صلوۃ خوف کا جواز اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتا ہے۔ ان عبد الله بن عمر قال غزوت مع رسول الله له قبل نجد فوازينا العـدو فـصـاففنا لهم فقام رسول الله يصلى لنا فقامت طائفة معه و اقبلت طائفة على العدو وفركع رسول الله الا الله بمن معه وسجد سجدتين ثم انصرفوا مكان الطائفة التى لم تصل فجاء وافركع رسول الله بهم ركعة وسجد سجدتين ثم سلم فقام كل واحد منهم فركع لنفسه ركعة وسجد سجدتين (الف) ( بخاری شریف، ابواب صلوۃ الخوف ص ۱۲۸ نمبر ۹۴۲ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب من قال يصلى بكل طائلة رکعة ثم يسلم ص ۱۸۴، ابواب صلوۃ الخوف نمبر ۱۲۴۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز خوف میں دو جماعتیں بنائے گا اور امام ہر جماعت کو ایک ایک رکعت پڑھائے گا۔ اور باقی ایک رکعت خود اپنے اپنے طور پر پڑھیں گے۔
نماز خوف پڑھنے کا جو طریقہ اوپر ذکر ہوا یہ حنفیہ کے یہاں مستحب ہے۔ اگر اس کے خلاف اور طریقے جو حدیث میں منقول ہیں ان کے مطابق نماز پڑھ لی تو نماز ہو جائے گی۔ اس طریقہ کے اختیار کرنے کی وجہ یہ ہیں (۱) امام ابو حنیفہ کی نظر آیت کے اس جملہ کی طرف گئی ہے فاذا سجدوا فيليكونوا من ورائكم ولتات طائفة اخرى لم يصلوا (ب) (آیت ۱۰۲ سورۃ النساء ۴ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ پہلی جماعت ایک رکعت کا سجدہ کر لے تو اس کو پیچھے چلے جانا چاہئے جس میں اشارہ ہے کہ دوسری رکعت اس کو فورا نہیں پڑھنی چاہئے وہ بعد میں پوری کرے گی (۲) قاعدہ کے اعتبار سے حنفیہ کی بتائی ہوئی صورت میں پہلی جماعت نماز سے پہلے فارغ ہوگی اور دوسری جماعت بعد میں فارغ ہوگی اور قاعدہ کا تقاضا بھی یہی ہے (۳) اس صورت میں امام کو مقتدیوں کا انتظار کرنا پڑتا نہیں ہے اور اگر پہلی جماعت دوسری رکعت فورا پوری کرے تو امام کو اتنی دیر تک دوسری جماعت کے آنے کا انتظار کرنا ہوگا۔ اور یہ امامت کے عہدے کے خلاف ہے۔ اس لئے پہلی جماعت
حاشیہ : (الف) عبداللہ بن عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے حضور کے ساتھ غزوہ کیا نجد کی جانب تو ہم نے دشمن کا سامنا کیا تو ان کے لئے صف بنائی تو حضور کھڑے ہو کر ہمیں نماز پڑھانے لگے تو ایک جماعت ان کے ساتھ کھڑی ہوئی اور دوسری جماعت دشمن کے سامنے ہوئی تو حضور نے ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے ان لوگوں کو پڑھائے جو ان کے ساتھ تھے۔ پھر وہ لوگ پھر کر اس جماعت کی جگہ پر گئے جنہوں نے نماز نہیں پڑھی تھی۔ پھر وہ لوگ آئے اور حضور نے ان کو ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے پڑھائے۔ پھر حضور نے سلام پھیرا پھر ان میں سے ہر ایک کھڑے ہوئے اور اپنی اپنی ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے پورے کئے (ب) پس جب کہ پہلی جماعت سجدہ کرلے تو ان کو پیچھے ہو جانا چاہئے اور دوسری جماعت آئے جس نے نماز نہیں پڑھی۔
The Thamari Commentary, Volume One. Book of Prayer. Chapter of the Fear Prayer. [398 (1)] When fear is intense, the imam makes the people into two groups: a group facing the enemy and a group behind him. He prays with this group one rak'ah and two prostrations. When he raises his head from the second prostration, this [group] goes... [Urdu: Important note: The form of the fear prayer is that if all people want to pray behind one imam, the imam will make two congregations and teach half the prayer to each congregation. But if there are two imams, each congregation will pray the complete prayer behind its own imam; there is no need for half prayer. Some imams say that as long as the Prophet was alive, every person wanted to pray his last prayer behind him, so during his lifetime the fear prayer was [valid]. But after him, praying in this way is abrogated; now there will be two separate imams and both congregations will pray behind separate imams. Their argument is from the verse revealed about the fear prayer: 'And when you are among them, and lead them in prayer, let a group of them stand with you and let them take their arms; when they prostrate, let them be behind you and let another group who have not prayed come and pray with you, and let them take their precautions and arms.' (Surah An-Nisa 4:102, label (a)) In this verse, the Prophet is addressed that when you are present, you should teach the people the fear prayer; this can imply that after you, the fear prayer will not be prayed in this way. But the majority of imams say that Abu Musa al-Ash'ari taught people the fear prayer, meaning that after [the Prophet] the fear prayer is still permissible. From Abu al-‘Aliyah: 'Abu Musa al-Ash'ari led us in the fear prayer in Isfahan' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on the proof of the fear prayer and that it did not go out, p. 1358, no. 6008). This effect shows that the fear prayer can be taught later. So the above verse and this hadith are proof of the permissibility of the fear prayer. [398] (1) When fear is intense, the imam will make the people into two groups: one group facing the enemy and the other behind the imam. Then the imam will teach the first group one rak'ah and two prostrations; when he raises his head from the second prostration, the first group will go to face the enemy, and the second group will come and the imam will teach them one rak'ah and two prostrations. The imam will recite the tashahhud and say the salutation, but the second group will not say salutation; rather they will go to face the enemy. The first group will come and they will pray one rak'ah and two prostrations alone without recitation (because they are latecomers (lahiq) and there is no recitation upon the latecomer, so they will not recite) and they will recite tashahhud and say the salutation. Footnote (a): When you are among them, establish prayer for them; let a group of them stand with you and let them take their arms; then when they prostrate, let them be behind you, and let the other group who have not prayed come and pray with you and let them take their precautions and arms. (b) Abu al-‘Aliyah said: Abu Musa al-Ash'ari led us in the fear prayer in Isfahan. [Continuation from page 269 in Arabic and Urdu: The second group came and he recited tashahhud and said salutation, but they did not say salutation and went to face the enemy. The first group came and they prayed alone one rak'ah and two prostrations without recitation, and recited tashahhud and said salutation. They went to face the enemy and the second group came and they prayed one rak'ah and two prostrations with recitation (because they were those who were preceded (masbuq) and those preceded will recite when completing their prayer). Then they recited tashahhud and said salutation. Then if the imam is a resident, he will teach the first group two rak'ahs and the second group two rak'ahs. The permissibility of the fear prayer is also from this hadith: 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar said: I participated in a battle with the Messenger of Allah towards Najd. We encountered the enemy and lined up facing them. The Messenger of Allah stood to pray for us. A group stood with him and a group faced the enemy. He bowed and his companions... and he performed two prostrations. Then they dispersed to the place of the group which had not prayed, and they came, and the Messenger of Allah bowed with them one rak'ah and two prostrations, then he said salutation. Then each one of them stood and he performed for himself one rak'ah and two prostrations. (Bukhari, chapters on the fear prayer, p. 128, no. 942; Abu Dawud, chapter of who said teach with each group one rak'ah then say salutation, p. 184, no. 1244). This hadith shows that in the fear prayer he would make two groups and the imam would teach each group one rak'ah, and the remaining one rak'ah they would pray on their own. The method mentioned above for the fear prayer is mustahabb (preferred) according to the Hanafis. If they pray according to other methods transmitted in hadith, the prayer will be valid. The reasons for adopting this method are: (1) Imam Abu Hanifah looked at the following phrase of the verse: 'Then when they prostrate, let them be behind you and let another group who have not yet prayed come' (Surah An-Nisa 4:102, label (b)). This verse indicates that when the first group performs one rak'ah and prostrates, they should go behind, indicating that they should not pray the second rak'ah immediately; they will complete it later. (2) By rule, in the method taught by the Hanafis, the first group will finish the prayer first and the second group later, and the rule requires this. (3) In this form, the imam does not have to wait for the followers, whereas if the first group completes the second rak'ah immediately, the imam would have to wait for the second group to come, and this is contrary to the station of imamah. Therefore, the first group [leaves]. Footnote (a): 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar said: I participated in a battle with the Messenger of Allah towards Najd. We encountered the enemy and lined up facing them. The Messenger of Allah stood to pray for us. A group stood with him and a group faced the enemy. Then he bowed and his companions... and he performed two prostrations. Then they went to the place of the group which had not prayed. Then they came and the Messenger of Allah bowed with them one rak'ah and two prostrations. Then he said salutation. Then each one of them stood and he performed for himself one rak'ah and two prostrations. (b) Then when the first group prostrates, they should go behind and let the other group come who have not prayed.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage from the Thamari Commentary is an expansion on the method of Salat al-Khawf (Fear Prayer) according to the Hanafi school. It begins with the matn stating the case when fear is intense: the imam divides the people into two groups—one facing the enemy and one behind him. He leads the second group in one rak'ah (with two sajdahs). Then that group moves to the front, and the other group comes and he leads them in one rak'ah. The imam performs tashahhud and salutations, but the second group does not; they go to battle. The first group then comes back and completes their prayer alone without recitation (because they are considered lahiq—latecomers—for whom recitation is not required). They recite tashahhud and say salutations, then go to the enemy. The second group returns and prays their second rak'ah with recitation (as they are masbuq—those who came late—and recite when completing). If the imam is a resident (muqim), he leads each group in two rak'ahs (i.e., he performs the prayer as full). The passage then provides proofs: (1) The Quranic verse (4:102) addressing the Prophet, which some scholars argue limits the fear prayer to his time, and (2) the hadith of Ibn Umar narrated in Bukhari and Abu Dawud showing the Prophet praying in this manner. The commentary addresses a disagreement: some say the fear prayer was abrogated after the Prophet, but the majority (including the Hanafis) hold it is still permissible, citing the practice of Abu Musa al-Ash'ari (reported by al-Bayhaqi). The Hanafi position is that the specific method described is mustahabb (preferred), but other methods from hadith are also valid. The commentary gives three reasons for this preference: (1) The verse implies the first group should not pray the second rak'ah immediately; (2) By rule, the first group should finish first; (3) This method avoids the imam having to wait for the second group. The passage thus establishes the ruling, its proof, and the Hanafi choice of method.

Key Terms
صلوة الخوف (Salat al-Khawf): The prayer performed during battle or when fear of the enemy is intense, according to a specific method dividing the congregation into two groups.
طائفة (Ta'ifah): A group or division of the people, in this context one of the two groups in the fear prayer.
لاحق (Lahiq): A person who joins the imam late and catches part of the prayer, but here refers to the first group who completes their prayer alone without recitation.
مسبوق (Masbuq): A person who joins the imam after the prayer has started, and completes the missed portion with recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf, what does the first group do after praying one rak'ah with the imam?
A) They wait for the imam to complete the salutation.
B) They go to face the enemy while the second group comes.
C) They recite the remaining rak'ah immediately.
D) They leave the mosque entirely.

Key Takeaway
The fear prayer remains a valid and preferred form of congregational prayer in times of danger, based on the Quran and Sunnah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Salat al-Khawf: Hanafi Method, Proofs, and Ruling on Fighting
Explains the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf, its proofs, inter-madhhab dispute, and prohibition of fighting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf, explain the proofs from Quran and Hadith, evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument, and state the ruling on fighting during the prayer.

Core Idea
Hanafi Salat al-Khawf: each group prays one rak'ah with the Imam, completes the rest individually; fighting invalidates the prayer.

The prayer of fear (Salat al-Khawf) is prescribed during battle. The Hanafi school has a preferred method supported by Quran 4:102 and a hadith of Ibn Umar. This lesson covers the method, its proofs, the differing opinion of the Shafi'i school, and the prohibition of fighting during the prayer. Understanding this ensures correct practice in times of danger.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Hanafi method
The Imam divides the congregation into two groups. He leads the first group in one rak'ah, then that group goes to face the enemy. The second group comes and prays one rak'ah with the Imam, then the Imam says salam. Each group then completes their remaining rak'ah individually. For a resident Imam, in a 4-rak'ah prayer, he prays two rak'ahs with each group; for Maghrib, two with the first and one with the second.
2
Examine the proofs
The Quranic verse (4:102) indicates that the first group should leave after prostrating (i.e., after one rak'ah), implying they complete later. The hadith of Ibn Umar (Bukhari, Abu Dawud) demonstrates this method: the Imam led one rak'ah with each group, then each completed individually. The athar from Ibrahim through Abu Hanifa (Kitab al-Athar) supports it.
The hadith is narrated by Ibn Umar: 'We were with the Prophet in the direction of Najd...'
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
The Shafi'i school disagrees, relying on a hadith in Abu Dawud (no. 1240) where each group completes their own rak'ahs immediately after the Imam's salam for that group. The Hanafi response is that their method avoids requiring the Imam to wait unnecessarily and aligns with the apparent meaning of the Quranic verse.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is the timing of completing the remaining rak'ahs.
4
Conclude with the prohibition of fighting
The passage states that fighting during Salat al-Khawf invalidates the prayer because it constitutes excessive movement (amal kathir). This is supported by evidence that any such action nullifies the prayer.

كتاب الصلوة
الطائفة الى وجه العدو وجائت تلك الطائفة فيصلى بهم الامام ركعة و سجدتين و تشهد وسلم ولم يسلموا وذهبوا الى وجه العدوو جائت الطائفة الاولى فصلوا وحدانا ركعة وسجدتين بغير قراءة و تشهد وا وسلموا ومضوا الى وجه العدو وجائت الطائفة الاخرى گی اور چلی جائے گی دشمن کے مقابلہ پر۔ اور دوسری جماعت آئے اور وہ ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے نماز پڑھیں قرآت کے ساتھ (اس لئے کہ یہ مسبوق ہیں اور مسبوق اپنی نماز پوری کرتے وقت قرآت کریں گے ) اور تشہد پڑھیں اور سلام پھیر دیں۔ پس اگر امام مقیم ہو تو پہلی جماعت کو دو رکعت نماز پڑھائے گا اور دوسری جماعت کو دو رکعت ۔ صلوۃ خوف کا جواز اس حدیث سے بھی ہوتا ہے۔ ان عبد الله بن عمر قال غزوت مع رسول الله له قبل نجد فوازينا العـدو فـصـاففنا لهم فقام رسول الله يصلى لنا فقامت طائفة معه و اقبلت طائفة على العدو وفركع رسول الله الا الله بمن معه وسجد سجدتين ثم انصرفوا مكان الطائفة التى لم تصل فجاء وافركع رسول الله بهم ركعة وسجد سجدتين ثم سلم فقام كل واحد منهم فركع لنفسه ركعة وسجد سجدتين (الف) ( بخاری شریف، ابواب صلوۃ الخوف ص ۱۲۸ نمبر ۹۴۲ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب من قال يصلى بكل طائلة رکعة ثم يسلم ص ۱۸۴، ابواب صلوۃ الخوف نمبر ۱۲۴۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز خوف میں دو جماعتیں بنائے گا اور امام ہر جماعت کو ایک ایک رکعت پڑھائے گا۔ اور باقی ایک رکعت خود اپنے اپنے طور پر
پڑھیں گے۔
نماز خوف پڑھنے کا جو طریقہ اوپر ذکر ہوا یہ حنفیہ کے یہاں مستحب ہے۔ اگر اس کے خلاف اور طریقے جو حدیث میں منقول ہیں ان کے مطابق نماز پڑھ لی تو نماز ہو جائے گی۔ اس طریقہ کے اختیار کرنے کی وجہ یہ ہیں (۱) امام ابو حنیفہ کی نظر آیت کے اس جملہ کی طرف گئی ہے فاذا سجدوا فيليكونوا من ورائكم ولتات طائفة اخرى لم يصلوا (ب) (آیت ۱۰۲ سورۃ النساء ۴ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ پہلی جماعت ایک رکعت کا سجدہ کر لے تو اس کو پیچھے چلے جانا چاہئے جس میں اشارہ ہے کہ دوسری رکعت اس کو فورا نہیں پڑھنی چاہئے وہ بعد میں پوری کرے گی (۲) قاعدہ کے اعتبار سے حنفیہ کی بتائی ہوئی صورت میں پہلی جماعت نماز سے پہلے فارغ ہوگی اور دوسری جماعت بعد میں فارغ ہوگی اور قاعدہ کا تقاضا بھی یہی ہے (۳) اس صورت میں امام کو مقتدیوں کا انتظار کرنا پڑتا نہیں ہے اور اگر پہلی جماعت دوسری رکعت فورا پوری کرے تو امام کو اتنی دیر تک دوسری جماعت کے آنے کا انتظار کرنا ہوگا۔ اور یہ امامت کے عہدے کے خلاف ہے۔ اس لئے پہلی جماعت
حاشیہ : (الف) عبداللہ بن عمر فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نے حضور کے ساتھ غزوہ کیا نجد کی جانب تو ہم نے دشمن کا سامنا کیا تو ان کے لئے صف بنائی تو حضور کھڑے ہو کر ہمیں نماز پڑھانے لگے تو ایک جماعت ان کے ساتھ کھڑی ہوئی اور دوسری جماعت دشمن کے سامنے ہوئی تو حضور نے ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے ان لوگوں کو پڑھائے جو ان کے ساتھ تھے۔ پھر وہ لوگ پھر کر اس جماعت کی جگہ پر گئے جنہوں نے نماز نہیں پڑھی تھی۔ پھر وہ لوگ آئے اور حضور نے ان کو ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے پڑھائے۔ پھر حضور نے سلام پھیرا پھر ان میں سے ہر ایک کھڑے ہوئے اور اپنی اپنی ایک رکعت اور دو سجدے پورے کئے (ب) پس جب کہ پہلی جماعت سجدہ کرلے تو ان کو پیچھے ہو جانا چاہئے اور دوسری جماعت آئے جس نے نماز نہیں پڑھی۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاول
۲۶۵
كتاب الصلوة
وصلوا ركعة وسجدتين بقراءة وتشهدوا وسلموا فان كان مقيما صلى بالطائفة الاولى ركعتين وبالثانية ركعتين (۳۹۹) (۲) ويصلى بالطائفة الاولى ركعتين من المغرب وبالثانية ركعة [۴۰۰](۳) ولا يقاتلون في حال الصلوة فان فعلوا ذلك بطلت صلوتهم ایک رکعت پڑھ کر دشمن کے سامنے جائے پھر دوسری جماعت ایک رکعت پڑھ کر دشمن کے سامنے جائے اور پہلی جماعت آکر دوسری رکعت پوری کرے۔ اس کے پورا کرنے کے بعد وہ دشمن کے سامنے جائے اور دوسری جماعت بعد میں اپنی پہلی رکعت پوری کرے(۳) مـحـمـد قال اخبرنا ابو حنيفة عن حماد عن ابراهيم في صلوة الخوف قال اذا صلى الامام باصحابه فلتقم طائفة منهم مع الامام وطائفة بازاء العدو فيصلى الامام بالطائفة الذين معه ركعة ثم تنصرف الطائفة الذين صلوا مع الامام من غير ان يتكلموا حتى يقوموا مقام اصحابهم وتأتى الطائفة الاخرى فيصلون مع الامام الركعة الأخرى ثم ينصرفون من غير ان يتـكـلـمـوا حـتـى يـقـوموافي مقام اصحابهم و تأتى الطائفة الاولى حتى يصلوا ركعة وحدانا ثم ينصرفون فيقومون مقام اصحابهم وتأتى الطائفة الاخرى حتى يقضوا الركعة التي بقيت عليهم وحدانا (الف) (كتاب الآثار لامام محمد ، باب صلوۃ الخوف ص ۱۳۹، نمبر ۱۹۴) اس اثر سے حنفیہ کی تائید ہوتی ہے۔
تان امام شافعی اور دیگر ائمہ کے نزدیک ابوداؤد شریف کی حدیث کی وجہ سے یہ ہے کہ پہلی جماعت امام کے ساتھ ایک رکعت پڑھنے کے بعد دوسری رکعت اسی وقت پوری کر لے اور سلام پھیر دے۔ پھر دشمن کے سامنے جائے اور امام اتنی دیر دوسری جماعت کا انتھار کریں گے۔ پھر دوسری جماعت آئے اور امام کے ساتھ ایک پڑھ کر امام سلام پھیریں گے اور دوسری جماعت دوسری رکعت پوری کر کے سلام پھیرے گی (ابو داؤد، باب صلوۃ الخوف ص ۱۸۱ نمبر ۱۲۴۰ میں یہ حدیث موجود ہے )
[۳۹۹) (۲) اور نماز پڑھائے گا پہلی جماعت کو مغرب کی دورکعتیں اور دوسری جماعت کو ایک رکعت۔ تین رکعت کا آدھا نہیں ہوتا اس لئے پہلی جماعت کو امام صاحب دور کعتیں نماز پڑھائیں گے۔ اور دوسری جماعت کو ایک رکعت نماز پڑھائیں گے۔ [۴۰۰] (۳) اور نماز کی حالت میں قتال نہیں کریں گے۔ پس اگر قتال، کیا تو ان کی نماز باطل ہو جائے گی۔ (۱) قتال کرنا عمل کثیر ہے اس لئے قتال کرنے سے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ اور دوبارہ نماز پڑھنا ہوگی (۲) اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے
حاشیہ : (الف) امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ مجھ کو ابوحنیفہ نے حماد سے اور وہ ابراہیم سے خبر دی نماز خوف کے بارے میں کہا جب امام اپنے ساتھی کو نماز پڑھائے تو ان میں سے ایک جماعت امام کے ساتھ کھڑی ہو۔ اور ایک جماعت دشمن کے مقابلہ پر ۔ تو امام نماز پڑھائے گا اس جماعت کو جو اس کے ساتھ ہے ایک رکعت، پھر وہ جماعت جس نے امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھی پھر جائے گی بغیر کلام کئے ہوئے یہاں تک کہ اپنے ساتھی کی جگہ پر کھڑی ہو جائے اور دوسری جماعت آئے اور امام کے ساتھ دوسری رکعت پڑھے۔ پھر واپس لوٹ جائے بغیر کلام کئے ہوئے یہاں تک کہ اپنے ساتھی کی جگہ پر کھڑی ہو جائے ۔ اور پہلی جماعت آئے یہاں تک کہ وہ ایک رکعت علیحدہ علیحدہ ہوکر نماز پڑھے۔ پھر واپس لوٹیں اپنے ساتھی کی جگہ پر کھڑے ہو جائیں۔ اور دوسری جماعت آئے وہ رکعت پوری کرے جو اس پر باقی ہے علیحدہ علیحدہ ہوکر ۔
The first group faces the enemy, then that group comes and the Imam prays with them one rak'ah, two prostrations, tashahhud, and salam, but they do not say salam. They go to face the enemy. Then the first group comes and they pray individually one rak'ah and two prostrations without recitation, and do tashahhud and salam. Then they go to face the enemy, and the other group comes... If the Imam is a resident, he prays two rak'ahs with the first group and two with the second. For Maghrib, he prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one with the second. They do not fight during the prayer; if they do, their prayer becomes invalid. The hadith of Ibn Umar is cited: 'I fought with the Messenger of Allah [؟] towards Najd...' The Urdu commentary explains the Hanafi method, its proofs from Quran (4:102) and hadith, and the disagreement with Shafi'i who hold that each group completes their own rak'ahs immediately. The footnote provides the full hadith of Ibn Umar and the athar from Imam Muhammad.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage from al-Sharh al-Thamiri discusses Salat al-Khawf (the prayer of fear) according to the Hanafi school. It begins by describing the method: two groups are formed; the Imam leads one group in one rak'ah, then that group goes to face the enemy while the second group comes and prays one rak'ah with the Imam. Each group then completes the remaining rak'ahs individually. If the Imam is a resident (muqeem), he prays two rak'ahs with each group for prayers other than Maghrib; for Maghrib, he prays two rak'ahs with the first group and one with the second, because three cannot be split evenly. The text notes that this method is mustahabb (recommended) in the Hanafi school; other valid methods from hadith are acceptable. The Hanafi position is supported by the Quranic verse (4:102) which implies that the first group should leave after the first rak'ah, and by the principle that the first group finishes before the second. The Shafi'i school, relying on a different hadith, holds that each group completes its own rak'ahs immediately after the Imam's salam. The passage also states that fighting during the prayer invalidates it, as it constitutes excessive movement (amal kathir). The proofs include hadith from Bukhari and Abu Dawud, and an athar from Imam Muhammad through Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): The prayer performed during battle or when in fear of the enemy, with a specific method of dividing the congregation into two groups.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended but not obligatory; performing it is rewarded, omitting it is not sinful.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joins the prayer late and must complete missed rak'ahs after the Imam's salam. Here, each group is considered masbuq for the rak'ah they missed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi method of Salat al-Khawf, if the Imam is a resident (muqeem) and the prayer is Maghrib, how many rak'ahs does he pray with each group?
A) Two rak'ahs with the first group and one with the second
B) One rak'ah with each group
C) Three rak'ahs with the first group and none with the second
D) Two rak'ahs with each group

Key Takeaway
Salat al-Khawf is valid with various methods, but the Hanafi recommended method avoids waiting and fighting invalidates the prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Hanafi Method of Salat al-Khawf (Maghrib) and the Shafi'i Dispute
Explains Hanafi method for Maghrib and contrasts with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method for Maghrib in Salat al-Khawf and explain the key difference with the Shafi'i method, citing the primary evidence for each.

Core Idea
In Maghrib Salat al-Khawf, the Hanafi imam prays two rak'ah with the first group and one with the second; each group completes individually.

Salat al-Khawf (the prayer of fear) is a concession for Muslims engaged in battle. This lesson focuses on the Hanafi method for Maghrib, which has three rak'ah. We will examine the precise steps, the evidence from the early scholars (the narration of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i through the chain of Abu Hanifa), and how the Hanafi position differs from that of Imam al-Shafi'i. The practical difference centres on whether the imam divides the odd-numbered prayer unevenly between the two groups.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact sequence: the imam prays two rak'ah with the first group, then one rak'ah with the second. Each group completes the missing rak'ah individually (wihdan) after the imam finishes with that group.
Maghrib is three rak'ah, so the division is 2+1.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
According to Imam al-Shafi'i, the first group prays one rak'ah with the imam, then completes the remaining two rak'ah immediately and says salam. The imam waits, then the second group prays one rak'ah with him, completes the remaining two, and says salam. Thus the imam's prayer is complete with each group.
The imam effectively prays the full prayer twice, but without duplication of intention.
3
Analyse the Hanafi evidence
The Hanafi proof is the mursal narration from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i via Abu Hanifa, recorded in Kitab al-Athar. This narration explicitly describes the imam leading one rak'ah with each group, then each group completing individually.
The chain is Abu Hanifa → Hammad → Ibrahim. It is a mursal because Ibrahim was a Tabi'i, not a Sahabi.
4
Analyse the Shafi'i evidence
The Shafi'i rely on a hadith in Sunan Abi Dawood (no. 1240) where the first group completes both rak'ah after the imam's first rak'ah, and the second group does likewise after the imam's first rak'ah with them.
This hadith is a marfu' report (attributed to the Prophet ﷺ) and is considered stronger in terms of chain continuity by many muhaddithin.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical consequence: in the Hanafi method, the imam's prayer is divided unevenly (2+1); in the Shafi'i method, the imam prays a full three-rak'ah prayer with each group. The Hanafi tarjih relies on the narration from Ibrahim, which the Hanafi jurists consider more consistent with the principle of not excessively delaying the face-off with the enemy.
The Hanafi school gives weight to the practice of the early Kufan scholars, considering it a reliable transmission even if mursal.

پر کھڑے ہو جائیں۔ اور دوسری جماعت آئے وہ رکعت پوری کرے جو اس پر باقی ہے علیحدہ علیحدہ ہوکر ۔
And he prays with the first group two rak'ah of Maghrib and with the second one rak'ah. And they do not fight during prayer; if they do that, their prayer is invalidated. (Urdu explanation: He prays two rak'ah and goes before the enemy, then the second group prays one rak'ah and goes before the enemy, and the first group comes and completes the second rak'ah. After completion, they go before the enemy, and the second group later completes their first rak'ah.) Muhammad said: Abu Hanifa informed us from Hammad from Ibrahim regarding Salat al-Khawf: he said: When the imam prays with his companions, let a group stand with the imam and a group facing the enemy. The imam prays with the group with him one rak'ah, then the group that prayed with the imam departs without speaking until they stand in the place of their companions. Then the other group comes and prays with the imam the other rak'ah, then they depart without speaking until they stand in the place of their companions. Then the first group comes and prays one rak'ah individually, then they depart and stand in the place of their companions. Then the other group comes and completes the rak'ah that remained for them individually. (Kitab al-Athar of Imam Muhammad, chapter on Salat al-Khawf, p. 139, no. 194) This effect supports the Hanafi view. Then: As for Imam Shafi'i and other imams, due to the hadith in Abu Dawood, the first group after praying one rak'ah with the imam completes the second rak'ah immediately and says salam, then goes to face the enemy, and the imam waits for the second group. Then the second group comes and prays one rak'ah with the imam, then the imam says salam, and the second group completes the second rak'ah and says salam. (Abu Dawood, chapter on Salat al-Khawf, p. 181, no. 1240) Footnote: Imam Muhammad said: Abu Hanifa informed me from Hammad from Ibrahim about Salat al-Khawf: he said: When the imam prays with his companions, let one group stand with the imam and one group facing the enemy. Then the imam prays one rak'ah with the group that is with him, then that group departs without speaking until they stand in the place of their companions. Then the other group comes and prays with the imam the second rak'ah. Then they return without speaking until they stand in the place of their companions. Then the first group comes and prays one rak'ah individually. Then they return and stand in the place of their companions. Then the other group comes and completes the rak'ah that remained for them individually.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on Salat al-Khawf, focusing on the method for Maghrib prayer during battle. The imam prays two rak'ah with the first group and one rak'ah with the second group, because Maghrib has an odd number of rak'ah. The text also explains that fighting during prayer invalidates it, as it is excessive action. Then it cites a narration from Ibrahim through Abu Hanifa, detailing the sequence of prayer: each group prays one rak'ah with the imam, then completes the remaining rak'ah individually. This is the Hanafi method. The passage then contrasts the Shafi'i method, which is based on a hadith in Abu Dawood where the first group completes both rak'ah immediately after the imam's first rak'ah, then the second group does the same. The Hanafi school relies on the narration from Ibrahim to support its position. The footnote further clarifies the narration.

Key Terms
صلاة الخوف (salat al-khawf): A special prayer performed during battle or extreme fear.
وحدانا (wihdān): Praying individually, not in congregation.
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where the chain misses a Companion; a Tabi'i reports directly from the Prophet.
مرفوع (marfu'): A hadith attributed directly to the Prophet ﷺ with a complete chain to a Companion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how does the imam lead the Maghrib prayer in Salat al-Khawf?
A) He prays one rak'ah with the first group and then one with the second group, each complete individually.
B) He prays two rak'ah with the first group and one with the second group.
C) He prays the entire Maghrib prayer with each group separately.
D) He prays one rak'ah with each group, then completes the remaining rak'ah individually.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method for Maghrib in Salat al-Khawf divides the odd number of rak'ah unevenly between groups (2+1), based on a narration from Ibrahim through Abu Hanifa.

Extreme Fear Prayer: Gestures and Dropping Conditions
Rules for prayer during extreme fear with gestures and without facing qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for prayer in extreme fear (shiddat al-khawf) and identify which conditions are dropped and how gestures are performed.

Core Idea
In extreme fear, prayer is valid with head gestures, dropping standing and facing qibla.

Imagine being in a battle where every second counts. You cannot stand still, face a fixed direction, or perform normal bowings. Does Allah require the impossible? No. In extreme fear, the law of necessity (darura) lightens the obligation. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling: how prayer remains valid through gestures (īmā’) on foot or riding, based on clear Quranic and prophetic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation (shiddat al-khawf)
Understand what qualifies as extreme fear: a genuine threat to life or limb that prevents normal prayer conditions (e.g., intense battle). The ruling applies only when one cannot safely perform the usual acts.
The Hanafis define it as a situation where one cannot safely perform the normal prayer.
2
Recognize the dropped conditions and the method
In such fear, standing (qiyam) and facing the qibla are dropped. Instead, the worshipper prays on foot (walking) or riding, making gestures with the head for ruku and sujud. One may face any direction.
Gestures (īmā’) replace the physical pillars of bowing and prostration.
3
Trace the evidence (dalil)
The primary proof is Quran 2:239: 'If you fear, then pray on foot or riding.' The Prophet ﷺ and Companions acted on this: during the Battle of the Trench, they delayed prayer due to fighting, but when fear was manageable, they prayed with gestures. The hadith of Umar and Anas illustrate the principle.
The verse implies dropping conditions that conflict with the state of fear.
4
Understand the rationale
The prayer is never abandoned; only its conditions are relaxed. The obligation remains, but the manner adapts to the circumstance. This balances religious duty with human limitation.
This is a manifestation of the Hanafi principle of istihsan (juristic preference) based on necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اشتد الخوف صلوا ركبانا وحدانا يومؤن بالركوع والسجود الى اى وجه شاءوا اذا لم يمكنهم استقبال القبلة. قال جاء عمر يوم الخندق فجعل يسب كفار قريش ويقول يا رسول الله ما صليت العصر حتى كادت الشمس ان تغيب فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وانا والله ما صليتها بعد قال فنزل الى بطحان فتوضأ وصلى العصر بعد ما غابت الشمس ثم صلى المغرب بعدها (بخاری شریف با الصلوة عند مناهضته الحصون ولقاء العدوص ۱۲۹ نمبر ۹۴۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ قتال چل رہا تھا اس لئے نماز نہیں پڑھی۔ اسی طرح نماز پڑھ رہا ہو اور قتال شروع ہو گیا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی قال انس بن مالك حضرت عند مناهضة حصن تستر عند اضائة الفجر واشتد اشتغال القتال فلم يقدروا على الصلوة فلم نصل الا بعد ارتفاع النهار (بخاری شریف با الصلوة عند مناهضته الحصون ولقاء العدوص ۱۲۹ نمبر ۹۴۵) اس اثر سے بھی معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ جنگ اور قتال کے وقت نماز نہیں پڑھی جائے گی۔ بلکہ نماز مؤخر کر دی جائے گی۔ فاذا اشتد الخوف صلوا ركبانا وحدانا يومؤن بالركوع والسجود إلى أي وجه شاءوا إذا لم يمكنهم استقبال القبلة. وإن اشتد الخوف ولم يمكن النزول، صلى على الراحلة وأومأ بالركوع والسجود. كما يصلي النفل على الراحلة، فيسقط القيام ويومئ بالركوع والسجود، ويسقط استقبال القبلة لعذر الخوف. ودليله قوله تعالى: فان خفتم فرجالا او ركبانا. وعن ابن سيرين انه كان يقول في صلوة المسايغة يومى ايماء حيث كان وجهه (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة 746 في الاصلوة عند المسايغة)
And if fear becomes intense, they pray riding and individually, gesturing with ruku and sujud towards whatever direction they wish if they cannot face the qibla. He said: Umar came on the day of the Khandaq and began to curse the disbelievers of Quraish and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I have not prayed Asr until the sun almost set.' The Prophet ﷺ said, 'By Allah, I have not prayed it yet.' He said: Then he descended to Bathan, performed wudu, and prayed Asr after the sun had set, then prayed Maghrib after it. (Bukhari, chapter on prayer at the time of approaching fortresses and meeting the enemy, no. 945) In this hadith, it is mentioned that because fighting was ongoing, they did not pray. Similarly, if one is praying and fighting starts, the prayer becomes invalid. Anas ibn Malik said: I was present during the assault on the fort of Tustar at the break of dawn, and the fighting became very intense, so they were not able to pray. We did not pray until after the sun had risen high. (Bukhari, same reference) This effect also shows that during war and fighting, prayer should not be performed; rather, it should be delayed. So if fear becomes intense, they pray riding and individually, gesturing with ruku and sujud towards whatever direction they wish if they cannot face the qibla. And if fear becomes intense and it is not possible to dismount, he prays on the mount and gestures for ruku and sujud, just as he prays the optional prayer on the mount. Thus, standing is dropped and he gestures for ruku and sujud, and facing the qibla is dropped due to the excuse of fear. Its proof is the verse: 'And if you fear, then on foot or riding.' And from Ibn Sirin: he used to say regarding the prayer of danger: he gestures where his face is. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 746, chapter on prayer at the time of danger)
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling for prayer when fear is so intense that normal prayer conditions cannot be met. The Hanafi school teaches that in such extreme fear (shiddat al-khawf), worshippers may pray individually while walking or riding, making gestures with the head for ruku and sujud, and may face any direction if facing the qibla is impossible. The passage also references events from the life of the Prophet ﷺ and the Companions where prayer was delayed due to battle, and then provides the Quranic proof from Surah Al-Baqarah: 'If you fear, then pray on foot or riding.' The method is likened to how one prays optional prayers on a mount, where standing and facing the qibla are not required. This shows that the normal conditions are dropped due to the excuse of intense fear.

Key Terms
إيماء (īmā’): Gesture made with the head for ruku and sujud when unable to perform full movements.
شدة الخوف (shiddat al-khawf): Extreme fear that prevents normal prayer, such as during intense battle.
ركبانا (rukbānan): Riding (on horseback, etc.) during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In extreme fear (shiddat al-khawf), what is the ruling regarding facing the qibla?
A) Must face qibla at all costs.
B) It is dropped; one may face any direction.
C) One must face qibla for the first rak'ah only.
D) It is recommended but not required.

Key Takeaway
In extreme fear, the prayer obligation remains; only the conditions that conflict with safety (standing, facing qibla) are replaced with gestures and flexibility.

Rider’s Prayer Without Qibla: Permissibility and Gestures
Ruling for a rider indicating prayer when facing Qibla is difficult

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a rider who cannot face the Qibla and explain how the prayer is performed by gestures (ima).

Core Idea
When unable to face Qibla, a rider may pray in any direction with gestures.

This lesson addresses a specific concession in prayer for a rider (or traveler) who is unable to face the Qibla due to circumstances like travel or illness. The Shariah grants ease by allowing the prayer to be performed in any direction and by gestures (ima) instead of full bowing and prostration. Understanding this ruling helps us appreciate the principle of removing hardship (raf‘ al-haraj) in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and condition
Recognize that the ruling applies to a rider (ركبانا) who is unable to face the Qibla. The condition is genuine inability, not mere inconvenience.
The term 'ركبانا' includes those on any riding animal or vehicle.
2
State the permitted action
The rider may pray in any direction they wish (جهة شائوا). The Qibla requirement is lifted due to hardship.
3
Clarify the method of prayer
The prayer is performed by gestures (يومون) for bowing and prostration instead of full physical movements. The rider indicates with head or body movements.
Gestures (ima) are also used by the sick when unable to perform normal postures.
4
Note the underlying rationale
The concession is based on the principle of removing hardship (رفع الحرج). The Shariah does not oblige what is beyond one's capacity.
This is consistent with Quran 2:286: 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

رکبانا : سوار ہوکر، یومون : اشارہ کرتے ہوئے۔
In whatever direction they wish when they are unable to face the Qibla. Riders: while riding, they indicate: by gestures.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage type is a ruling statement. It addresses the situation of a person praying while riding (rider) who cannot face the Qibla due to circumstances such as travel or illness. The ruling states that such a person may pray in any direction they choose and can perform the prayer by means of gestures (ima) instead of full physical movements. This is based on the ease permitted in Shariah for those with valid excuses. The Urdu words clarify that 'ركبانا' means 'while riding' and 'يومون' means 'they indicate by gestures'.

Key Terms
جهة شائوا (jihatu shā’ū): In any direction they wish, i.e., the rider may choose the direction to face for prayer.
ركبانا (rukbānan): While riding; indicates the state of the person praying.
يومون (yuumūna): They indicate, i.e., perform the prayer by gestures instead of full movements.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A rider unable to face the Qibla may pray in any direction by gestures.

Facing the Qibla at the Time of Death: Sunnah, Not Obligation
Ruling on turning the dying person towards the Qibla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on turning a dying person to face the Qibla and explain the evidence from the hadith, distinguishing between Sunnah and fard.

Core Idea
Turning the dying to face Qibla is Sunnah, not fard — following the fitrah.

This passage from the Book of Funerals (Kitab al-Jana'iz) addresses the recommended practice at the moment of death. The author draws an analogy between sleeping facing the Qibla (which is Mustahabb/Sunnah) and the dying person's posture. A hadith from Abu Qatadah confirms that the Prophet ﷺ approved of this practice, declaring it to be upon the fitrah. Thus, the Hanafi school holds that turning the dying person onto their right side facing the Qibla is a confirmed Sunnah (sunnah muakkadah), not an obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text explicitly states that when a man is in the throes of death (ihtadara), he should be turned to face the Qibla on his right side. Determine the legal classification: is it fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.?
The author likens it to sleeping posture, which is Mustahabb/Sunnah.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith: from Abu Qatadah, where a man instructed he be turned towards the Qibla at death, and the Prophet said 'He is upon the fitrah.' This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi; it is ahad, thus zanni in both transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's statement 'He is upon the fitrah' indicates approval. 'Fitrah' refers to the natural disposition which inclines towards good. Since turning towards the Qibla is part of that natural disposition, it is recommended but not obligatory.
The proof lies in the Prophet's tacit approval (taqrir) and the link to fitrah.
4
Note the absence of ikhtilaf
The Hanafi position is consistent with other schools; there is no major disagreement. All schools consider turning the dying towards the Qibla as recommended (Sunnah/Mustahabb).
The cross-madhhab status is muttafaq alayh.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that it is Sunnah muakkadah to turn the dying person to face the Qibla on the right side. It is not fard; if omitted, no sin but loss of reward.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجنائز
[ ۴٠٢ ] (۱) اذا احتضر الرجل وجه الى القبلة على شقه الايمن [۴۰۳] (۳) ولقن الشهادتين [ ۴۰۴] (۳) واذا مات شدوا لحييه وغضوا عينيه.
ضروری نوٹ جنائز جمع ہے جنازہ کی جیم کے فتحہ کے ساتھ ۔ میت کو جنازہ کہتے ہیں۔ نماز جنازہ کا ثبوت اس آیت سے ہوتا ہے لا تصل على احد منهم مات ابدا ولا تقم على قبره (الف) ( آیت ۸۴ سورۃ التوبہ ) اس آیت میں منافق کی نماز پڑھنے سے منع کیا ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مومن کی نماز جنازہ پڑھنا چاہئے۔ چنانچہ نماز جنازہ پڑھنی فرض کفایہ ہے۔

Book of Funerals. [402] (1) When a man is in the throes of death, he should be turned to face the Qibla on his right side. [403] (2) And he should be prompted with the two testimonies. [404] (3) And when he dies, they should tie his jaw and close his eyes. Necessary note: 'Jana'iz' is the plural of 'janaza' with the fatha on the jim. The deceased is called janaza. The proof for the funeral prayer is from this verse: 'Do not ever pray for any of them who dies, nor stand at his grave' (Surah at-Tawbah, verse 84). In this verse, praying for the hypocrite is forbidden, from which it is understood that the funeral prayer for a believer should be performed. Accordingly, performing the funeral prayer is a communal obligation (fard kifayah). (402) (1) When a person's time of death approaches, he should be turned on his right side towards the Qibla. Sleeping facing the Qibla is Mustahabb and Sunnah, therefore at the time of death too, one should face the Qibla. (2) There is a hadith: From Abu Qatadah from his father... they said, 'He passed away and bequeathed one-third to you, O Messenger of Allah, and he instructed that he be turned towards the Qibla when in agony.' The Messenger of Allah said, 'He is upon the fitrah.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on what is recommended of turning towards the Qibla, vol. 3, p. 539, no. 6604). From this hadith, it is known that at the time of death, the deceased should be turned towards the Qibla.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Funerals. It states that when a person is in the death throes (ihtidar), it is Mustahabb/Sunnah to turn them onto their right side facing the Qibla. The author draws an analogy from the Sunnah of sleeping in that position and provides a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) confirmed that this practice is in accordance with the natural disposition (fitrah). The commentary clarifies that the funeral prayer is a fard kifayah, established by the Quranic prohibition of praying for hypocrites, implying that praying for believers is required. The ruling on facing Qibla at death is based on this hadith.

Key Terms
احتضر (ihtadara): The state of being in the throes of death, when death is imminent.
القبلة (al-qiblah): The direction of the Ka'bah in Makkah towards which Muslims pray.
فطرة (fitrah): The natural disposition innate in humans, which inclines towards Islam and its practices.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on turning a dying person to face the Qibla?
A) It is a fard (obligation).
B) It is a Sunnah (recommended).
C) It is mubah (permissible).
D) It is makruh (disliked).

Key Takeaway
Facing the Qibla at the time of death is a sunnah muakkadah, not a fard, confirmed by the Prophet's approval and analogy with sleeping posture.

Prompting the Dying with the Shahadah (Talqin)
Ruling on prompting the dying with shahadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talqin, identify its dalil, and explain the caution against commanding the dying person.

Core Idea
Prompt gently, do not command: the shahadah should be offered softly, not imposed.

This passage presents a beautiful sunnah that eases the final moments of a Muslim. It is not about forcing a recitation but about creating an environment of faith. The hadith guides us to prompt, while Hanafi fiqh adds a crucial nuance: avoid commanding, as a refusal could lead to a tragic end.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the recommended action? What is its legal status (hukm)?
The act is talqin, and the ruling is sunnah (recommended).
2
Locate the dalil
Find the hadith cited and note its source and wording.
Hadith from Muslim and Abu Dawud: 'لقنوا موتاكم لا اله الا الله'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith indicate the ruling? Why is it a recommendation and not an obligation?
The imperative form is interpreted as nadb (recommendation) because the context is easing death, not imposing a duty.
4
Note the caution
What additional instruction does the author give about the manner of talqin?
Do not command the dying person to recite; simply recite softly so they may hear and repeat voluntarily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۰۳] (۲) شہادتین کی تلقین کرے۔
موت کے وقت حاضرین مجلس کو چاہئے کہ دھیمی آواز میں کلمہ لا الہ الا للہ محمد رسول اللہ پڑھے۔ تا کہ میت کو بھی پڑھنے کی توفیق ہو جائے اور ایمان پر خاتمہ ہو۔ حدیث میں اس کی ترغیب ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله لقنوا موتاكم لا اله الا الله (ج) ( مسلم شریف، کتاب الجنائز، فصل في تلقين الختصر لا الہ الا للہ ص ۳۰۰ نمبر ۹۱۷ را بود او د شریف، باب فی التلقین ج ثانی ص ۸۸ نمبر ۳۱۱۷)
اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ میت کو تلقین کرنا چاہئے۔ البتہ اس کو پڑھنے کے لئے نہیں کہنا چاہئے کیونکہ انکار کر دیا تو کفر پر خاتمہ ہوگا۔
[403] (2) Prompt (talqin) with the two testimonies. At the time of death, those present should recite in a low voice the kalimah 'La ilaha illallah Muhammadur Rasulullah', so that the dying person may also be enabled to recite it and end with faith. There is a hadith encouraging this: From Abu Hurairah, who said: The Messenger of Allah said, 'Prompt your dying ones with La ilaha illallah.' (Muslim, Kitab al-Jana'iz, chapter on talqin; Abu Dawud, chapter on talqin). From this hadith, it is understood that talqin should be done. However, one should not say 'recite it' to the dying person, because if he refuses, he would end in disbelief.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding talqin (prompting) at the time of death. It is recommended for those present to softly recite the shahadah so that the dying person may repeat it and die upon faith. The hadith from Abu Hurairah explicitly commands: 'Prompt your dying ones with La ilaha illallah.' The author notes a crucial caution: do not command the dying person to recite, as they may refuse in a stubborn state, leading to a bad end. Instead, just prompt gently.

Key Terms
تلقين (talqin): Prompting or coaching a dying person to recite the shahadah in a gentle manner.
شهادتين (shahadatayn): The two testimonies of faith: La ilaha illallah and Muhammadur Rasulullah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is fard (obligatory).
B) It is Sunnah (recommended).
C) It is bid'ah (innovation).
D) It is only for those who are conscious.

Key Takeaway
Talqin is a recommended act of mercy; gently prompt the shahadah but never command, as it may lead to a tragic refusal.
