Binding the Jaw and Closing the Eyes after Death
Rulings on immediate post-death care

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah ruling for tying the jaw and closing the eyes of the deceased, identify the prophetic evidence, and explain the practical wisdom.

Core Idea
Tying the jaw and closing the eyes are recommended sunnah, not obligatory, based on the Prophet's practice.

When a Muslim passes away, immediate care includes actions to maintain dignity. Two key actions are tying the jaw to keep the mouth closed and closing the eyes. This lesson explores the ruling, its evidence, and wisdom behind these practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Actions
Read the passage to find the two actions prescribed for the deceased immediately after death.
Focus on 'jaw tied' and 'eyes closed'.
2
Determine the Ruling Level
Using the Hanafi school, determine whether these actions are obligatory (fard/wajib) or recommended (sunnah/mustahabb).
The text implies recommendation, not obligation.
3
Locate the Evidence
Find the hadith cited and note its source. Understand how the Prophet's action and statement serve as proof.
Hadith from Umm Salamah in Sahih Muslim.
4
Understand the Wisdom
Reflect on the reasons given: to prevent an unsightly appearance and show respect for the deceased.
5
Apply the Ruling
Consider how you would advise someone who has just lost a relative regarding these actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۴۰۲) (۳) اگر انتقال ہو جائے تو اس کی ڈاڑھی باندھ دی جائے اور اس کی آنکھیں بند کر دی جائیں۔
انتقال کے وقت منہ کھلا رہ جاتا ہے جس کی وجہ سے دیکھنے والوں کو کراہیت ہوتی ہے اس لئے ڈاڑھی کو سر کے ساتھ لگا کر باندھ دیا جائے گا تو منہ کھلا ہوا نہیں رہے گا اور بدنما معلوم نہیں ہوگا اس لئے ڈاڑھی باندھ دی جائے گی۔ اسی طرح موت کے وقت آنکھیں کھلی رہ جاتی ہیں جو بدنما معلوم ہوتی ہیں اس لئے آنکھیں بھی فورا بند کر دی جائیں۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ام سلمة قـالـت دخل رسول الله على ابى سلمة وقد شق بصره فاغمضه ثم قال ان الروح اذا قبض تبعه البصر (الف) (مسلم شریف ،فصل في القول الخير عند المتضر ص ۳۰۰ کتاب الجنائز نمبر ۹۲۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ موت کے وقت میت کی آنکھی بند کردینی چاہئے۔
(402) (3) If he passes away, then his jaw should be tied and his eyes closed. At the time of death, the mouth remains open, which causes unpleasantness for onlookers. Therefore, the beard should be tied up to the head so that the mouth is not left open and does not appear unsightly. Thus the jaw is tied. Similarly, at death, the eyes remain open, which appears unsightly, so the eyes should be closed immediately. There is a hadith: From Umm Salamah, she said: The Messenger of Allah entered upon Abu Salamah while his eyes were open, so he closed them, then said, 'When the soul is taken, the sight follows it.' (Muslim, Kitab al-Jana'iz, chapter on good words at the time of death, no. 920). From this hadith, it is understood that the eyes of the deceased should be closed.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage gives rulings for immediate post-death actions: tying the lower jaw (to keep the mouth closed) and closing the eyes. The explanation is practical: to maintain a dignified appearance. The proof is a hadith from Umm Salamah where the Prophet (peace be upon him) closed the eyes of Abu Salamah and explained that the sight follows the soul. This indicates it is a sunnah.

Key Terms
شدا اللحيين (shaddu al-lahiyayn): Tying the two jaws (lower and upper) together to keep the mouth closed after death.
غض العينين (ghaddu al-'aynayn): Closing the eyes of the deceased.

Key Takeaway
Closing the eyes and tying the jaw of the deceased are meritorious sunnah acts, grounded in prophetic practice and aimed at preserving the dignity of the deceased.

Covering the Private Parts of the Deceased During Ghusl
Rulings on preparing the body for washing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on covering the 'awrah of the deceased and identify the evidence from the hadith and athar.

Core Idea
Covering the deceased's 'awrah is wajib, proven by a hadith prohibiting looking at the private parts of the dead.

When preparing a deceased person for washing, certain steps must be taken to preserve modesty and respect. The Hanafi school emphasizes that covering the private parts ('awrah) is obligatory, not merely recommended. This ruling is supported by clear prophetic instructions and the practice of the Companions as transmitted in authoritative sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the required preparatory actions
The text describes three actions: placing the deceased on a bench (sarir), covering the private parts with a cloth, and removing all other clothes.
The sarir allows water to drain; covering the 'awrah is the key ruling.
2
State the legal status of covering the 'awrah
According to the Hanafi school, covering the private parts of the deceased is wajib (obligatory). It is not merely recommended, as some other schools hold.
The evidence used (hadith) is zanni al-thubut but considered sufficient for wujub.
3
Analyze the primary dalil (hadith)
The hadith from Ali: 'Do not expose your thigh, nor look at the thigh of anyone alive or dead' (Abu Dawud). The explicit prohibition of looking indicates the obligation to cover.
The thigh is part of the 'awrah; the prohibition extends to both living and dead.
4
Examine the supporting athar (practice of the Companions)
The athar from Ayyub describes covering the private parts and face of the deceased. This confirms the practice of the early Muslims.
The Hanafi school uses this to reinforce the obligation.

[405] (4) When they intend to wash him, they place him on a bed (sarir) and put a cloth (khirqah) over his private parts, and remove his clothes. [406] (5) And they make wudu for him, but do not rinse his mouth nor nose. This is all to maintain modesty and respect.

Key Terms
سرير (sarir): A bench or wooden platform used for washing the deceased, allowing water to drain away.
عورة ('awrah): The private parts that must be concealed; for a male, from navel to knee; for a female, see detailed rulings.
خرقة (khirqah): A piece of cloth used to cover the private parts of the deceased during washing.

Covering the deceased's private parts is an obligatory (wajib) step in preparing the body for washing, supported by the hadith and practice of the Companions.

Performing Wudu for the Deceased without Rinsing Mouth and Nose
Ruling on making wudu for the deceased without rinsing mouth and nose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on madmadah and istinshaq for the deceased, explain the practical alternative using wet bread, and cite the supporting athar from Sa'id ibn Jubayr.

Core Idea
Wudu for the deceased omits rinsing mouth and nose to avoid water retention, using a wet cloth or bread instead.

This passage clarifies a specific difference in the wudu of the deceased compared to the living. While the living are required to rinse the mouth and nose as part of wudu, the Hanafi school modifies this for the deceased to prevent water from being trapped in cavities. The proof comes from an athar (tradition) of Sa'id ibn Jubayr, which explicitly excludes madmadah and istinshaq. Instead, a moistened piece of bread is used to simulate cleansing without the risk of difficulty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is giving wudu to the deceased. The ruling is that it is performed similarly to wudu for prayer, but with two exceptions: madmadah (rinsing mouth) and istinshaq (sniffing water into nose) are omitted.
The base ruling is from the general command to do wudu for the deceased, but the exception is specific.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an athar from Sa'id ibn Jubayr (a Tabi'i) transmitted in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: 'The deceased is given wudu like the wudu for prayer, except that his mouth is not rinsed nor water placed in his nose.' This is a mursal hadith (from a Tabi'i directly) but accepted in practical fiqh.
The thubut is zanni (probable), but the ruling is supported by istihsan (juristic preference) due to difficulty.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit phrase 'except that' (إلا أنه) clearly excludes madmadah and istinshaq from the otherwise identical wudu. This is a direct textual indication that these two acts are not required for the deceased.
The wording is a clear istithna' (exception) which overrides the general command.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may include rinsing the mouth and nose for the deceased, arguing that the general command applies fully. The Hanafi school differentiates based on practicality and the specific tradition.
The cross-madhhab status is 'mukhtalaf fih' (disagreed upon).
5
Understand the practical substitute
Since water is not used, a wet piece of bread or cloth is inserted into the mouth and nose to achieve a cleansing effect. This maintains the spirit of the Sunnah while avoiding harm.
This alternative is based on istihsan and ease (taysir).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۴۰۶] (۵) اور میت کو وضو کرائے لیکن کلی نہ کرائے اور نہ ناک میں پانی ڈالے۔ (1) کلی کرانا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا سنت ہے لیکن میت کے منہ اور ناک سے پانی نکالنا مشکل ہوگا اس لئے روٹی کو پانی سے بھگو کر منہ اور ناک میں ڈال دیا جائے تا کہ ایک طرح کی کلی اور ناک میں پانی دالنا ہو جائے۔ حیات کی طرح با ضابطہ پانی نہ ڈالا جائے۔ زندگی میں بھی ناک میں پانی ڈالنا اور کلی کرنا سنت تھا موت کے وقت اس کا طریقہ تھوڑا بدل جائے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن سعيد بن جبير قال يوضاً الميت وضوءه لصلوة الا انه لا يمضمض ولا يستنشق (مصنف ابن ابی هیته ۱۲ ما اول ما يبدأ به من غسل الميت ، ج ثانی میں ۴۴۹، نمبر ۱۰۸۹۷)
[406] (5) And they make wudu for him, but they do not rinse his mouth nor put water in his nose. (1) Rinsing the mouth (madmadah) and putting water in the nose (istinshaq) are Sunnah, but it would be difficult to extract water from the mouth and nose of the deceased. Therefore, a piece of bread should be soaked in water and placed in the mouth and nose, so that something like rinsing and sniffing is achieved. Water should not be poured in as in life. In life too, putting water in the nose and rinsing the mouth are Sunnah; after death, the method changes slightly. (2) There is an athar: from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, he said, 'The deceased is given wudu like the wudu for prayer, except that his mouth is not rinsed nor water placed in his nose.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 10897)
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage explains the method of wudu for the deceased. The deceased is given wudu similar to that for prayer, but the usual rinsing of the mouth and nose is omitted because it would be difficult to remove the water from those cavities. Instead, a moistened piece of bread is placed inside the mouth and nose to simulate the cleaning without the risk of water retention. The athar from Sa'id ibn Jubayr confirms this exception. This is a Hanafi ruling based on practical necessity.

Key Terms
مضمضة (madmadah): Rinsing the mouth with water, which is part of wudu for the living but omitted for the deceased.
استنشاق (istinshaq): Sniffing water into the nose, omitted for the deceased due to difficulty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is required as for the living.
B) It is omitted; instead, a wet cloth or bread is used.
C) It is optional.
D) It is prohibited.

Key Takeaway
Wudu for the deceased follows the standard arkan but excludes madmadah and istinshaq, replacing them with a wet cloth or bread to prevent water retention.

Pouring Water Over the Deceased: The Recommended Method
Ruling on the method of washing the deceased with water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended method for ghusl of the deceased, identify the hadith proof, and distinguish the minimum obligation from the sunnah.

Core Idea
The ghusl of the deceased must be thorough, and it is sunnah to wash in odd numbers — three, five, or seven times.

The text explains the final step of ghusl: pouring water over the deceased. While the obligation is to wash once, the sunnah is to repeat washing in odd numbers. The proof comes from the Prophet's instruction regarding his daughter's washing. This lesson will walk you through the ruling, the recommendation, and the hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being described and its legal classification. The act is pouring water over the deceased (ifadat al-ma').
The overall ghusl is fard kifayah, but this passage focuses on the method.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Umm 'Atiyyah is cited. The Prophet commanded washing his daughter 'three, five, or seven times.'
This is a hadith ahad but accepted for practice.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's command (اغسلنها) indicates a recommended action (sunnah) in the Hanafi school because the context is instruction, not obligation.
The odd numbers show flexibility, not a fixed number.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars might interpret the hadith as obligatory, but the Hanafi position holds it as sunnah mu'akkadah.
The minimum obligation is one complete wash.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling: wash at least once, but it is strongly recommended to wash in odd numbers (3, 5, or 7).
This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage describes the main ghusl of the deceased: pouring water over the entire body. It is recommended to pour water an odd number of times (three, five, seven) as indicated by the hadith from Umm 'Atiyyah regarding the washing of the Prophet's daughter. The goal is to thoroughly clean every limb. This is the final step in the ghusl procedure.

Key Terms
إِفَاضَةُ الْمَاءِ (ifadat al-ma'): Pouring water over the body, the main action of ghusl.
طاق (taaq): Odd number (1,3,5,7). It is recommended to wash the deceased an odd number of times.

Covering the Deceased’s Private Parts During Ghusl
Commentary on rules for ghusl al-mayyit with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on covering the deceased's 'awrah during washing and explain the proof from the hadith 'Do not uncover your thigh nor look at the thigh of a dead person.'

Core Idea
Covering the deceased's 'awrah is sunnah muakkadah; exposing it is prohibited by prophetic command.

This lesson focuses on a key aspect of ghusl al-mayyit: covering the deceased's private parts. The Hanafi school, citing explicit prophetic prohibitions and companion practice, rules that covering is a stressed sunnah. Understanding this ruling and its proof demonstrates how the school balances textual commands with practical necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
Recognize that the act in question is covering the private parts (satr) of the deceased during the washing (ghusl).
This is a preparatory step before the actual washing.
2
Determine the Hukm
From the hadith and athar, the Hanafi school derives that covering is a stressed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah), not wajib.
The ruling is based on the strength of the evidence.
3
Locate the Dalil
The primary proof is the hadith from Abu Dawud: 'Do not uncover your thigh and do not look at the thigh of anyone, living or dead.' Also, an athar from Ayyub shows covering with a cloth.
The hadith is ahad, thus the ruling is zanni al-thubut.
4
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The explicit prohibition (nahy) against looking at the deceased's thigh implies that the thigh must be covered; otherwise, looking would be inevitable. The command 'do not uncover' directly indicates covering.
Hanafi usul: al-nahy yufidu al-tahrim, but here it is interpreted as a prohibition of exposure, leading to a recommended covering.
5
Note the Ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school considers covering the 'awrah of the deceased as wajib, based on the same hadith but with a different usul reading.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in differing usul principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاوّل
۲۶۹
كتاب الصلوة
[۴۰۵ (۴) فاذا ارادوا غسله وضعوه على سرير وجعلوا على عورته خرقة ونزعوا ثيابه [۴۰۶] (۵) ووضوه ولا يمضمض ولا يستنشق [۴۰۷](۲) ثم يفيضون الماء عليه سلمة وقد شق بصره فاغمضه ثم قال ان الروح اذا قبض تبعه البصر (الف) (مسلم شریف ،فصل في القول الخير عند المتضر ص ۳۰۰ کتاب الجنائز نمبر ۹۲۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ موت کے وقت میت کی آنکھی بند کردینی چاہئے۔ ۴۰۵ (۴) جب میت کے غسل کا ارادہ کرے تو اس کو تخت پر رکھے اور اس کے ستر عورت پر چھوٹا سا کپڑا رکھ دے اور اس کا کپڑا کھول دے۔ غسل کے وقت تخت پر اس لئے رکھے گا تا کہ پانی نیچے گر جائے اور غسل دینے میں آسانی ہو۔ اور اس کے ستر پر چھوٹا سا کپڑا اس لئے رکھے گا تا کہ اس کا ستر نظر نہ آئے۔ البتہ غسل دینے میں پریشانی ہوگی اور کپڑا بھیگ جائے گا اس لئے دیگر تمام کپڑے کھول دیئے جائیں گے (۲) اسحدیث میں ہے کہ مردوں کا ستر غلیظہ نہیں دیکھنا چاہئے عن على ان النبی الله الله قال لا تبرز فخذك ولا تنظر الى فخذ حتى ولا ميت (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی ستر الميت عند غسلہ ج ثانی ص ۹۲ نمبر ۳۱۴۰) جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ غسل دیتے وقت میت کا ستر نہیں دیکھنا چاہئے (۳) اثر میں ہے عن ایوب قال رأيته يغسل ميتا فالقى على فرجه خرقة و على وجهه خرقة اخرى ورضاه وضوء الصلوة ثم بدأ بميامنه (ج) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب غسل میت ج ثالث ص ۳۹۸ نمبر ۶۰۸ / مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ا، فی لميت يغسل من قال يستر ولا یجرد، ج ۲، ص ۲۴۸، نمبر ۱۰۸۸۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ میت کے ستر پر چھوٹا کپڑا رکھنا چاہئے تا کہ اس کا ستر نظر نہ آئے۔
[۴۰۶] (۵) اور میت کو وضو کرائے لیکن کلی نہ کرائے اور نہ ناک میں پانی ڈالے۔ (1) کلی کرانا اور ناک میں پانی ڈالنا سنت ہے لیکن میت کے منہ اور ناک سے پانی نکالنا مشکل ہوگا اس لئے روٹی کو پانی سے بھگو کر منہ اور ناک میں ڈال دیا جائے تا کہ ایک طرح کی کلی اور ناک میں پانی دالنا ہو جائے۔ حیات کی طرح با ضابطہ پانی نہ ڈالا جائے۔ زندگی میں بھی ناک میں پانی ڈالنا اور کلی کرنا سنت تھا موت کے وقت اس کا طریقہ تھوڑا بدل جائے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن سعيد بن جبير قال يوضاً الميت وضوءه لصلوة الا انه لا يمضمض ولا يستنشق (مصنف ابن ابی هیته ۱۲ ما اول ما يبدأ به من غسل الميت ، ج ثانی میں
۴۴۹، نمبر ۱۰۸۹۷)
۴۰۷) (۶) پھر میت پر پانی بہائے ۔
غسل دینے کے لئے میت پر طاق مرتبہ پانی بہائے تا کہ ہر عضو دھل جائے۔
حدیث میں ہے عن ام عطية قالت دخل علينا رسول الله الله حين توفيت ابنته فقال اغسلنها ثلاثا او خمسا او
حاشیہ : (الف) حضور آبی سلمہ پر داخل ہوئے اور ان کی نگاہ کھلی ہوئی تھی تو آپ نے اس کو بند کر دیا۔ پھر فرمایا روح جب مقبوض ہوتی ہے تو نگاہ اس کے پیچھے دیکھتی رہتی ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا اپنی ران کو نہ کھولا اور نہ کسی زندہ یا مردہ کی ران کو دیکھو (ج) میں نے راوی کو دیکھا کہ مردے کو غسل دے رہے تھے تو اس کی شرمگاہ پر کپڑے کا ٹکڑا ڈالا اور اس کے چہرے پر دوسرا ٹکڑا ڈالا اور نماز کے وضو کی طرح وضو کرایا اور اس کی دائیں جانب سے شروع کی۔

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الاوّل)
۲۷۰
كتاب الصلوة
[۴۰۸(۷) ويجمر سريره وترا [۴۰۹] (۸) ويغلى الماء بالسدر او بالحرض فان لم يكن فالماء القراح [۱۰](۹) ويغسل رأسه ولحيته بالخطمي.
اكثر من ذلك ان رأيتن ذلك بماء وسدر واجعلن في الآخرة كافورا او شيئا من كافور (نمبر۱۲۵۳) و في حديث اخرى قال ابدان بميامنها و مواضع الوضوء منها (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب غسل الميت و وضوءه بالماء والسد رص ۶۷ نمبر ۱۲۵۴) اس حدیث سے یہ باتیں معلوم ہوئیں۔ غسل طاق مرتبہ دے، غسل میں بیری کے پتے استعمال کرے، اخیر میں میت پر کافور ڈالے تا کہ خوشبو مہکتی رہے اور جلدی کیڑے نہ لگے ہنسل دائیں جانب سے شروع کرے۔ اسی حدیث سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ میت پر پورا پانی
بہائے جس سے ہر جگہ پانی پہنچ جائے۔ (۴۰۸) (۷) تخت کو دھونی دے طاق مرتبہ۔
تخت کو دھونی دینے سے تخت پر خوشبو ہوگی تاکہ میت کی بدبو محسوس نہ ہو۔ اسی طرح کپڑے پر بھی طاق مرتبہ دھونی دے تا کہ خوشبو
رہے (۲) اثر میں موجود ہے عن اسماء بنت ابی بکر انها قالت لاهلها اجمرو ثیابی اذا انا مت ثم كفنونى ثم حنطو نی ولا تذروا علی کفنی حناطا (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الميت لا يتبع بالجمرة ج ثالث ص ۴۲۱۷ نمبر ۲ ۶۱۵ /مصنف ابن ابی شبيبة ،نمبر ۱۱۰۲۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ میت کے کپڑے کو لبان کی دھونی دینی چاہئے۔ اور اس کے تخت کو بھی دھونی دینی چاہئے ۔ البتہ دھونی
لیکر میت کے پیچھے نہیں جانا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ اس میں آگ کا اثر ہے اور لوگ اس کو بت پرستی کے مشابہ سمجھیں گے۔
[۴۰۹] (۸) پانی کو جوش دیا جائے بیری کے پتے یا اشنان گھاس سے، پس اگر یہ نہ ہوں تو خالص پانی سے۔ بیری کے پتے یا اشنان گھاس سے صفائی زیادہ ہوتی ہے۔ اس لئے ان دونوں میں سے ایک کو ڈال کر پانی کو جوش دیا جائے اور اس پانی سے میت کو غسل دیا جائے۔ اور اگر وہ نہ ملیں تو خالص پانی سے میت کو غسل دیا جائے (۲) اس کے لئے بخاری شریف کی حدیث ( نمبر ۱۲۵۳؎ مسلم شریف، باب فی غسل الميت ص ۳۰۴ نمبر ۹۳۹) مسئلہ نمبر میں بماء وسدر گزر چکی ہے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ تھا کہ بیری کے پتے ڈال کر جوش دیا جائے۔ [۴۱۰] (۹) میت کا سر اور اس کی ڈاڑھی خطمی سے دھوئی جائے۔
اثر میں ہے عن الاسود قال قلت لعائشة يغسل رأس الميت بخطمى فقالت لا تعنتوا ميتكم (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شبیه ۱۴، فی لمیت اذالم يوجد له سدر يغسل بغیر علمی اداشنان، ج ثانی ص ۱۳۵، نمبر ۱۰۹۱۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ میت کے سر کو عظمی سے دھونا
حاشیہ : (الف) ام عطیہ فرماتی ہیں کہ جس وقت حضور کی بیٹی کا انتقال ہوا تو آپ نے فرمایا ان کو تین مرتبہ نسل دو یا پانچ مرتبه نسل دو یا اس سے زیادہ اگر تم مناسب سمجھو پانی سے اور بیری کے پتے سے۔ اور اخیر میں کافور ڈالویا کا فور میں سے کچھ ڈالو۔ دوسری حدیث میں ہے کہ میت کی دائیں جانب سے شروع کر دو اور اس کی وضو کی جگہ سے شروع کرو (ب) اسماء بنت ابی بکڑ نے اپنے گھر والوں سے کہا جب میں مرجاؤں تو میرے کپڑے کو دھونی دینا پھر مجھ کو کفن دینا پھر مجھ کو حنوط دینا اور میرے کفن پر حنوط نہ چھڑکنا (ج) میں نے عائشہ سے پوچھا کیا میت کا سرخطمی سے دھویا جائے؟ تو فرمایا می پرستی نہ کرنا ( جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ علمی اس پر عمل کر سکتے ہو )
The Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 1, page 269. Book of Prayer. [405 (4)] When they intend to wash him, they place him on a bed and put a cloth over his private parts and remove his clothes. [406] (5) They perform wudu for him but do not rinse his mouth or nose. [407] (2) Then they pour water over him... Salamah: His eyes were open, so he closed them and said: 'When the soul is taken, the sight follows it' (a) (Muslim, Chapter on Good Word at the Time of Distress, p. 300, Book of Funerals, no. 920). From this hadith it is understood that at the time of death, the deceased's eyes should be closed. 405 (4) When one intends to wash the deceased, he should place him on a bed, cover his private area with a small cloth, and remove his clothes. He places him on the bed so that water flows down and washing is easy. He covers his private area so that it is not visible. However, washing will be difficult and the cloth will get wet, so all other clothes are removed. (2) In this hadith: It is not permissible to look at the private parts of a man; the Prophet said: 'Do not uncover your thigh and do not look at the thigh of anyone, living or dead' (b) (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Covering the Deceased during Washing, vol. 2, p. 92, no. 3140). From this it is understood that one should not look at the deceased's private parts during washing. (3) In an athar: From Ayyub, he said: I saw him washing a deceased person; he placed a cloth over his private parts and another cloth over his face, performed wudu like that for prayer, then started with his right side (c) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on Washing the Deceased, vol. 3, p. 398, no. 608; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 2, p. 248, no. 10883). From this athar it is understood that a small cloth should be placed over the deceased's private parts so that they are not visible. [406] (5) And perform wudu for the deceased, but do not rinse his mouth and do not pour water into his nose. (1) Rinsing the mouth and putting water in the nose is sunnah, but it would be difficult to remove water from the deceased's mouth and nose. So a piece of bread is soaked in water and placed in the mouth and nose, so that a kind of rinsing and nasal cleansing occurs. Water is not poured in the regulated manner as in life. In life, rinsing the mouth and nose was sunnah; at the time of death, its method changes slightly. (2) In an athar: From Sa'id ibn Jubayr, he said: The deceased is given wudu like the wudu for prayer, except that he does not rinse his mouth or nose (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 2, p. 449, no. 10897). [407] (6) Then pour water over the deceased. For washing, water is poured an odd number of times so that every limb is washed. In a hadith: From Umm Atiyyah, she said: The Messenger of Allah entered upon us when his daughter died, and he said: 'Wash her three times, or five times, or more than that if you see fit, with water and lotus leaves, and put camphor in the last [wash]' (no. 1253). And in another hadith: 'Start with her right side and the places of wudu' (a) (Bukhari, Chapter on Washing the Deceased and Wudu with Water and Lotus, p. 67, no. 1254). From this hadith the following matters are understood: Wash an odd number of times; use lotus leaves in the wash; finally put camphor on the deceased so that fragrance remains and insects do not come quickly; start washing from the right side. From this hadith it is also understood that water should be poured completely over the deceased so that water reaches every part. [408] (7) Fumigate his bed with incense an odd number of times. Fumigating the bed gives it fragrance so that the deceased's odor is not felt. Similarly, fumigate the cloth an odd number of times so that fragrance remains. (2) In an athar: From Asma bint Abi Bakr, she said to her family: 'Fumigate my clothes when I die, then shroud me, then apply hanut to me, and do not sprinkle hanut on my shroud' (b) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, Chapter on Not Following the Deceased with Incense, vol. 3, p. 4217, no. 615; Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 11020). From this athar it is understood that the deceased's clothes should be fumigated with frankincense, and his bed should also be fumigated. However, one should not follow the deceased carrying incense, because that involves fire and people might associate it with idol worship. [409] (8) Boil water with lotus leaves or with ushnan (soapwort); if these are not available, then with pure water. Lotus leaves or ushnan grass provide better cleansing. So one of these is added and the water is boiled, then the deceased is washed with that water. If they are not available, then wash with pure water. (2) The hadith from Bukhari (no. 1253) and Muslim (Chapter on Washing the Deceased, p. 304, no. 939) mentioned in the issue with 'with water and lotus' has passed; its meaning was that lotus leaves are added and boiled. [410] (9) Wash the deceased's head and beard with khitmi (marshmallow). In an athar: From Aswad, he said: I asked A'ishah: 'Should the deceased's head be washed with khitmi?' She said: 'Do not cause hardship to your dead' (c) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol. 2, p. 135, no. 10917). From this athar it is understood that washing the deceased's head with khitmi is permissible. Footnotes: (a) Umm Atiyyah said: When the daughter of the Prophet died, he said: 'Wash her three times, or five times, or more if you think fit, with water and lotus leaves, and in the last put camphor or something of camphor. And start with her right side and the places of wudu.' (b) Asma bint Abi Bakr told her family: 'When I die, fumigate my clothes, then shroud me, then apply hanut, and do not sprinkle hanut on my shroud.' (c) I asked A'ishah: 'Should the deceased's head be washed with khitmi?' She said: 'Do not cause hardship to your dead.' (Meaning: you may act upon this knowledge.)
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage from Sharh al-Thamiri is a commentary on the matn of a Hanafi fiqh work, specifically on the rules for washing the deceased (ghusl al-mayyit). The commentator expands on each point of the matn, providing proof from the Quran, Sunnah, or athar (sayings of the Companions). The passage covers nine points: (4) placing the deceased on a bed and covering the private parts, (5) performing a reduced wudu without mouth rinsing or nose washing, (6) pouring water an odd number of times, (7) fumigating the bed with incense, (8) boiling water with lotus leaves or soapwort, and (9) washing the head and beard with marshmallow. For each point, the commentator explains the wisdom (hikmah) and cites relevant hadith. The overall tone is instructive, guiding the practitioner to follow the prophetic method with precision. The commentary emphasizes ease (taysir) while maintaining the sunnah.

Key Terms
ستر (satr): The private parts (awrah) of the deceased that must be covered during washing.
خرقة (khirqah): A piece of cloth used to cover the private parts of the deceased during washing.
وضوء (wudu): The ritual washing performed on the deceased, similar to wudu for prayer but without rinsing mouth/nose.
سدر (sidr): Lotus tree leaves used in washing the deceased for cleansing.
حرض (hurd/hurdu (ushnan)): Soapwort or a type of plant used as a cleansing agent in ghusl al-mayyit.
خطمي (khitmi): Marshmallow plant used for washing the head and beard of the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on covering the deceased's private parts during washing?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah Muakkadah
C) Mubah
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
Covering the deceased's private parts during ghusl is a stressed sunnah in the Hanafi school, supported by prophetic prohibition and companion practice.

Drying and Perfuming the Deceased After Washing
Ruling on drying and perfuming the deceased after washing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended actions after washing the deceased and identify the evidence for applying hanut and camphor according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Drying the deceased and applying perfume are recommended, not obligatory, based on prophetic practice.

After washing the deceased, the Hanafi school prescribes specific actions to prepare the body for burial. These actions are considered recommended (mustahabb/sunnah) rather than obligatory. The passage outlines the procedure of drying the body with a cloth to avoid wetting the shroud, followed by applying a perfume mixture (hanut) to the head and beard and camphor to the prostration spots. These practices are rooted in the hadith and reports from the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions and their legal status
Read the passage to list the three main actions: drying the body, applying hanut, and applying camphor. Note that each is described as recommended (mustahabb or sunnah) in the commentary.
The ruling level is based on the context of the hadith.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Find the hadith from Bukhari (1254) and the athar from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibrahim. Understand that the hadith 'And make the last of it camphor' is the main proof for applying camphor.
The imperative is interpreted as a recommendation due to other contextual factors.
3
Understand the application details
Note where hanut is applied (head and beard) and where camphor is applied (prostration spots: face, palms, knees, feet). The commentary explains the wisdom: to keep those areas smooth and fragrant.
This is a practical implementation of the sunnah.
4
Recognize the absence of obligation
The passage and evidence show these acts are not obligatory. If omitted, the burial is still valid. This distinguishes the Hanafi view from schools that may consider camphor obligatory.
The hukm level is mustahabb (recommended) for hanut and sunnah for camphor.

(۱۲) ثم ينشفه بثوب ويدرج في اکفانه ۴۱۴] (۱۳) ويجعل الحنوط على رأسه و لحيته والكافور على مساجده ۴۱۵ (۱۲) پھر کپڑے سے میت کا پانی خشک کیا جائے گا اور اس کو کفن میں لپیٹ دیا جائے گا۔
کپڑے سے غسل کا پانی اس لئے خشک کیا جائے تا کہ کفن گیلا نہ ہو جائے، اور کفن میں لپیٹنے کی تفصیل آگے آرہی ہے۔
(۱۳) حنوط لگایا جائے گا میت کے سر پر ، اور اس کی ڈاڑھی پر اور کافور لگایا جائے گا اس کے سجدے کی جگہ پر۔ کئی چیزوں کو ملا کر حنوط ایک قسم کی خوشبو بناتے ہیں۔ جس کو مردوں پر ملتے ہیں۔ غسل کے بعد اس کو ڈاڑھی اور سر پر ملنا مستحب ہے، اور سجدے کی جگہ مثلا چہرہ ، دونوں ہتھیلی ، دونوں گھٹنے اور دونوں پاؤں جو سجدے کے وقت زمین پر سکتے ہیں ان پر ملا جائے تا کہ یہ جگہیں چکنی رہیں اور خوشبودار بھی رہیں۔ اثر میں ہے عن ابن مسعود قال يوضع الكافور على موضع سجود الميت ، عن ابراهيم في حنوط الميت قال يبدأ بمساجده (الف) مصنف ابن ابي هيبة ۳۳ ، فی الحوط کیف يضع به و این مجعل ج ثانی ص ۴۶۰، نمبر ۱۱۰۲۷۱۱۰۲۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ کافور اور حنوط میت کے سجدے کی جگہ پر ملے جائیں گے (۲) حدیث میں گزر چکا ہے کہ واجعلن في الآخرة فورا (بخاری شریف نمبر ۱۲۵۴) کہ اخیر میں میت کو کافور لگاؤ۔
(12) Then he dries him with a cloth and wraps him in his shroud. (13) And he places hanut on his head and beard, and camphor on his places of prostration. (12) Then with a cloth the water of the deceased is dried and he is wrapped in the shroud. The water from the bath is dried with a cloth so that the shroud does not become wet. The details of wrapping come later. (13) Hanut is applied to the head of the deceased and his beard, and camphor is applied to his prostration spots. By mixing several things, hanut is a type of perfume that is applied to the deceased. After washing, it is mustahabb to apply it to the beard and head, and apply to the prostration spots like the face, both palms, both knees, and both feet that touch the ground during prostration, so that these spots remain smooth and fragrant. There is an athar from Ibn Mas'ud that camphor is placed on the prostration spots of the deceased. From Ibrahim regarding the hanut of the deceased: he said, 'Begin with his prostration spots.' (From Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah 33, Kitab al-Hanut, how to place it and where, vol. 2, p. 460, nos. 11027-11023). This athar indicates that camphor and hanut are applied to the prostration spots of the deceased. (2) In the hadith it has already passed: 'And make the last of it camphor' (Bukhari no. 1254) that at the end, apply camphor to the deceased.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage gives the rulings after washing the deceased. The first part states that after the bath, the body is dried with a cloth to prevent the shroud from getting wet, then wrapped in the shroud. The second part discusses applying hanut (a perfume mixture) to the head and beard, and camphor to the prostration spots (sajdah places: forehead, nose, hands, knees, feet). The Urdu commentary explains that applying hanut is mustahabb (recommended), and the prostration spots are anointed to keep them smooth and fragrant. The proof is from athar (reports of Ibn Mas'ud and Ibrahim) and a hadith from Bukhari (1254) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed to make camphor the last thing applied to the deceased. This establishes the sunnah practice.

Key Terms
حنوط (hanut): A compound perfume applied to the deceased, especially on the head and beard.
كافور (kafur): Camphor, a fragrant substance applied to the prostration spots of the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of drying the deceased after washing?
A) To prevent the shroud from becoming wet
B) To remove impurities for ritual purity
C) To prepare the body for burial in a timely manner
D) To allow the hanut to adhere better

Key Takeaway
After washing, the deceased is dried, perfumed with hanut on the head/beard and camphor on prostration spots—all recommended acts based on prophetic practice.

Sunnah Shroud for Men: Three Pieces
Ruling on the recommended shroud for men consisting of three pieces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah shroud for a man and identify the three pieces with their descriptions.

Core Idea
Sunnah shroud for a man is three pieces: izār, qamīṣ, lifāfa; two are permissible.

When preparing a deceased man for burial, the Hanafi school prescribes a specific number and type of garments as sunnah. This passage explains the recommended composition and the evidence from the Prophet's practice and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shrouding a deceased man. The ruling is that it is sunnah muakkadah to use three garments; two are permissible.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadiths: the shrouding of the Prophet in three white cotton cloths, and the Prophet giving his qamis to shroud Abdullah ibn Ubayy.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit action in the first hadith indicates sunnah; the request for the qamis shows its permissibility and inclusion in the shroud.
4
List the three pieces and their descriptions
1) Izār: lower wrap, head to foot. 2) Qamīṣ: upper wrap, sleeveless, no hem, no collar, split for head, not sewn. 3) Lifāfa: outer sheet wrapping all.
5
Note the exception
If only two garments are used, it is still permissible, though less preferred (makruh tanzih if without reason).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴) والسنة ان يكفن الرجل فى ثلثة اثواب ازار و قميص و لفافة فان اقتصروا على ثوبين جاز (۱۴) سنت یہ ہے کہ مرد کو تین کپڑوں میں کفن دیا جائے گا (۱) ازار (۲) قمیص (۳) اور چادر، پس اگر دو کپڑوں پر اکتفا کرے تب بھی جائز ہے۔ (۱) مرد عموما زندگی میں تین کپڑے پہنتا ہے اس لئے تین کپڑوں میں کفن دینا سنت ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة ان رسول الله كفن في ثلثة اثواب يمانية بيض سحولية من كرسف ليس فيهن قميص ولا عمامة (ب) (بخاری شریف، باب الثياب البيض للكفن ص ۱۶۹ نمبر ۱۲۶۴ و ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الکفن ج ثانی ص ۹۳ نمبر ۳۱۵۱ و مسلم شریف ، باب الجنائز ص ۳۰۵ نمبر ۹۴۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مرد کو تین کپڑوں میں کفن دینا سنت ہے۔ قمیص کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے ان عبد الله بن ابی لما توفی جاء ابنه الى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال اعطني قمیصک اکفنه فیه (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب الکفن في قميص الذي يكف ص ۱۶۹ نمبر (۱۲۶۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک ایسا کپڑا بھی کفن میں دیا جائے گا جس کو قمیص کہتے ہیں۔ لیکن اس میں آستین نہیں ہوگی اور نہ دامن اور کلی ہوگی۔ بلکہ درمیان میں پھاڑ کر سر گھسانے کا بنا دیا جائے گا۔ اور اس کو سیا بھی نہیں جائے گا۔ اس طرح تین کپڑے پورے کر دیئے گئے۔
(14) And the sunnah is that the man is shrouded in three garments: izār, qamīṣ, and lifāfa. If they content themselves with two garments, it is permissible. (14) The sunnah is that a man should be given a shroud of three cloths: (1) izār, (2) qamīṣ, (3) and a sheet. If they suffice with two cloths, it is also permissible. (1) Generally a man wears three clothes in life, so shrouding in three cloths is sunnah. (2) There is a hadith from Aisha that the Prophet was shrouded in three white Yemeni cloths of cotton, with no qamīṣ or turban. (Bukhari 1264, Abu Dawud 3151, Muslim 941) This hadith indicates that shrouding a man in three cloths is sunnah. For the qamīṣ, there is the hadith that when Abdullah ibn Ubayy died, his son came to the Prophet and said, 'Give me your qamīṣ so I may shroud him in it.' (Bukhari 1269) This hadith indicates that a cloth called qamīṣ is given in the shroud, but it has no sleeves, no hem, and no collar; rather, it is split in the middle for the head to be inserted, and it is not sewn. Thus three cloths are completed.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the shroud for men. The core ruling is that the sunnah is to use three pieces: izār (a lower garment), qamīṣ (a sleeveless shirt-like wrap), and lifāfa (a sheet that wraps all). However, it is permissible to use only two pieces if necessary. The commentary explains that three garments reflect what a man normally wears, and cites two key hadiths: the shrouding of the Prophet in three white cotton cloths without qamīṣ or turban, and the incident where the Prophet gave his own qamīṣ to shroud Abdullah ibn Ubayy. The qamīṣ is described as unsown, with an opening for the head, no sleeves, hem, or collar. This lesson establishes the Hanafi position that three pieces are sunnah, but two are sufficient.

Key Terms
ازار (izar): A lower wrap, from head to foot, for the shrouded male.
قمیص (qamis): A sleeveless, collarless upper garment with head opening, not sewn.
لفافة (lifafa): A sheet that wraps over the entire shroud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the text, what is the sunnah number of cloths for a man's shroud?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Five

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah for a man's shroud is three specific pieces: izār, qamīṣ (unsewn), and lifāfa; two are permissible but less preferred.

Wrapping the Shroud for Men: Left Side First
Method of wrapping the lifafa and tying it to prevent unwrapping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of wrapping the lifafa and identify when tying is permissible.

Core Idea
Begin with the left side of the lifafa so the right side overlaps — then tie only if needed.

The way we wrap the deceased is a sunnah transmitted from the Salaf. This lesson presents the precise sequence: starting from the left, then the right, and the condition that allows tying. Understanding this method ensures that we follow the prophetic practice in funeral preparations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
The act is wrapping the lifafa (outer sheet) over the deceased. According to the Hanafi school, the method described is sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
If the method is not followed, the shroud remains valid but the sunnah is missed.
2
Memorize the sequence of wrapping
The full sequence: spread lifafa on bier, then izar, then qamis; place deceased on qamis; insert head into slit; fold qamis over; fold izar; then wrap lifafa starting with left side, then right.
The order before wrapping (spreading) is also part of the sunnah.
3
Understand why the left side is wrapped first
Wrapping the left side first ensures that the right edge is on top, honouring the general Islamic preference for the right side.
This instruction reverses the usual 'right first' pattern for dressing the living.
4
Recognize the exception for tying
If there is fear that the shroud will come undone (e.g., during transport), it is permissible to tie a knot. This is a practical allowance.
Tying without need may be makruh; the knot should be temporary.
5
Note the authority of this practice
The method is based on transmitted practice (zahir al-riwayah) from the Companions and early scholars, not on a specific Quranic verse or hadith cited here.
Other schools may have different sequences, but the Hanafi position is left-first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۵) واذا ارادوا لف اللفافة عليه ابتدأوا بالجانب الايسر فالقوه عليه ثم بالايمن فان خافوا ان ينتشر الكفن عنه عقدوه (۱۵) جب میت پر لفافہ ڈالنے کا ارادہ کرے تو بائیں جانب سے شروع کرے تو لفافہ اس پر ڈال دے، پھر دائیں جانب سے ڈالے، پس اگر خوف ہو کہ کفن کھل جائے گا تو اس پر گرہ لگا دے۔ کفن دیتے وقت پہلے تخت پر چادر لفافہ پھیلائے گا۔ اس کے اوپر ازار، اور ازار کے اوپر قمیص پھیلائے گا۔ پھر میت کو قمیض پر رکھ کر سر کو قمیص کی چیر میں گھسا دے۔ اور قمیص کا اوپر کا حصہ میت پر ڈال دے، اور پھر قمیص پر ازار بپیے اور پھر لفافہ لیپٹے۔ پہلے بائیں طرف کو لپیٹے اور پھر دائیں طرف کو لپیٹے تا کہ دایاں کنارہ اوپر ہو جائے اور اخیر میں لپیٹا جائے۔ دائیں طرف سے کرنے کی اہمیت پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔
(15) And when they intend to wrap the lifafa on him, they begin with the left side, then place it on him, then the right side. If they fear the shroud will spread open, they tie it. (15) When intending to place the lifafa on the deceased, one should begin from the left side, place the lifafa on him, then from the right side. If there is fear that the shroud will open, then tie a knot. At the time of shrouding, first spread the lifafa sheet on the bier, over it spread the izar, and over that spread the qamis. Then place the deceased on the qamis, insert the head into the slit of the qamis, put the upper part of the qamis on the deceased, then fold the izar over the qamis, then wrap the lifafa. First wrap the left side, then the right side, so that the right edge is on top, and finally wrap. The importance of the right side has passed earlier.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage details the step-by-step method of wrapping the shroud for a man. The key instruction is to begin with the left side of the lifafa, then the right, so that the right edge overlaps the left. If there is concern the shroud may come undone, a knot may be tied. The Urdu commentary expands on the sequence: first spread the lifafa, then the izar, then the qamis; place the deceased; insert head into qamis; bring qamis over; fold izar; then wrap lifafa starting left then right. This ensures the right side is uppermost, following the general Islamic preference for the right side. No specific proof is cited here; it is a practical transmission.

Key Terms
لفافة (lifafa): The outer sheet used to wrap the entire shroud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Left side
B) Right side
C) Both sides simultaneously
D) It does not matter

Key Takeaway
When shrouding a man, the lifafa is wrapped left side first, then right; a knot is allowed if needed.
